The Ruling on Quran Recitation for a Menstruating Woman and Junub
Proving the prohibition of reciting even one verse of Quran for a menstruating woman and junub, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting the Quran during menstruation and janabah, identify the primary evidence, and apply the exception for partial verses and dhikr.

Core Idea
A full verse of the Quran is haram for a menstruating woman or junub, but tasbih, tahlil, and partial verses are permitted.

This lesson examines the evidence for the prohibition of Quran recitation during states of major impurity. Understanding the precise limit—what is prohibited and what is allowed—is essential for correct practice. We will analyze the hadith and the scholarly refinements that permit tasbih and partial verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting even one full verse of the Quran while in a state of menstruation or janabah. The Hanafi ruling is haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Ibn Umar narrated in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sunan Abi Dawud: 'لا تقرء الحائض ولا الجنب شيئا من القرآن'.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition (لا تقرء) indicates haram. The word 'شيئا' is general and includes any portion, but Hanafi scholars restrict it to a complete verse based on other evidence.
The exception for partial verses comes from athar and scholarly interpretation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Maliki school permits recitation without touching the mushaf; the Shafi'i school prohibits recitation only for the junub, not for the menstruating woman.
The Hanafi school treats both states equally.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts the view that full verses are prohibited, but partial verses (for teaching) and dhikr (tasbih, tahlil, du'a) are allowed, based on reports from the Salaf and the commentary in Tirmidhi.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۵۱) [۳] قرآن مجید کی ایک آیت پڑھنا۔ وجه (1) عن ابن عمر عن النبي الله قال لا تقرء الحائض ولا الجنب شيئا من القرآن. (ترندى شريف باب ماجاء فی الجنب والحائض لا يقرا القرآن، ص ۳۶ نمبر ۱۳۱ ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الجنب يقرا القرآن، ص۱۳۴ نمبر ۲۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حائضہ اور جنبی قرآن کریم کی آیت نہ پڑھے۔ (۲) علماء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عورت کو نیچے پڑھانا ہو تو آیت کو ٹکڑ انکڑا کر کے پڑھائے۔ البتہ تسبیح اور تہلیل پڑھ سکتی ہے، دعا پڑھ سکتی ہے، اثر میں ہے۔ عن هشام بن حسان قال: الجنب يسبح و يحمد الله ، و يدعو ، ولا يقرأ آية واحدة - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب صل تذکر اللہ الحائض والحب ، ج اول ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۱۳۱۱) (۳) اور ترمذی شریف میں اس طرح ہے۔ قالوا : لا تقرأ الحائض و لا الجنب من القرآن شيئا الا طرف الآية و الحرف و نحو ذالک ، و رخصو اللجنب و الحائض في التسبيح و التهليل ۔(ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في الحب والحائض أنهما لا يقرآن القرآن ص ۱۳۶ نمبر (۱۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ لوگ پوری آیت نہیں پڑھ سکتے البتہ آیت کو تو ڑتوڑ کر پڑھ سکتے ہیں اور نبیح او تحلیل وغیرہ پڑھ سکتے ہیں۔
Translation: (251) [3] Reciting one verse of the Quran. Evidence: (1) From Ibn Umar from the Prophet, he said: 'Neither the menstruating woman nor the junub should recite anything of the Quran.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) (2) Scholars say that if a woman needs to teach someone below, she may recite the verse in parts. However, she may recite tasbih and tahlil, and may make supplication. There is an athar from Hisham ibn Hassan: 'The junub may glorify Allah and praise Him, and supplicate, but not recite a single verse.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) (3) And in Tirmidhi it says: 'The menstruating woman and the junub may not recite anything of the Quran except the end of a verse or a letter and the like, and they permitted the junub and menstruating woman to recite tasbih and tahlil.'
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proof for the prohibition of Quran recitation during menstruation and janabah. The primary evidence is the hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet forbade such recitation. The Hanafi school permits reciting partial verses (less than one full verse) for teaching purposes, and allows tasbih, tahlil, and du'a. This is based on athar (reports from the Salaf) as narrated by Hisham ibn Hassan and the statement in Tirmidhi. The key point is that a full verse is prohibited, but parts of a verse are permissible.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, such as after sexual intercourse or seminal emission.
تسبيح (tasbih): Expression of glorification of Allah, e.g., saying 'SubhanAllah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what may a menstruating woman recite from the Quran?
A) Any verse she wishes.
B) Only full verses, but not chapters.
C) She may recite less than a full verse, e.g., part of a verse.
D) She may recite nothing at all, not even tasbih.

Key Takeaway
Reciting even one full verse of the Quran is haram for a menstruating woman or a person in janabah; however, tasbih, tahlil, and partial verses are permissible.

Prohibition of Touching the Quran Without Wudu
Proving the prohibition of touching the Quran without ritual purity using Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching the Quran without wudu, identify the Quranic and hadith evidence, and apply the ruling to cases involving objects with Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Only the ritually pure may touch the Quran—this prohibition is established by Quran, Sunnah, and the practice of the Salaf.

In this lesson, we examine the evidence for the prohibition of touching the Quran without wudu. The Hanafi school considers it haram based on the Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified' (al-Waqi'ah 56:79) and the Prophet's instruction to Amr ibn Hazm. We will also explore how this ruling applies to items containing Quranic verses, such as coins, and note a difference with the Maliki school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position on touching the Quran without wudu: it is haram for anyone in a state of hadath (minor or major).
The prohibition applies regardless of the type of impurity.
2
Examine the primary dalil
Analyze the Quranic verse 56:79. Note that its thubut is qat'i (certain) but dalala is zanni (speculative) because the referent of 'it' and the meaning of 'purified' can be interpreted. The Hanafi school interprets 'purified' as those free from hadath.
The verse is the strongest proof.
3
Examine the secondary dalil
Consider the hadith from the Prophet's letter to Amr ibn Hazm: 'Do not touch the Quran except in a state of purity.' This hadith is a clear command.
Multiple narrations support this.
4
Apply to extended cases
Understand that the prohibition extends to any part of the Mus'haf, including covers attached to it. For objects with Quranic verses (e.g., dirhams), the Salaf differed; the Hanafi school prohibits touching them without wudu unless wrapped in a separate cloth.
The athar from Ata and al-Qasim allow touching wrapped dirhams, but the Hanafi school distinguishes this from the Mus'haf.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Contrast the Hanafi position with the Maliki school, which permits touching the Quran with a barrier (e.g., gloves) without wudu. The Hanafi school relies on the general import of the Quranic verse and the hadith.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: under Hanafi, even with a barrier it is haram; under Maliki, it is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۵۲) (۴۳) قرآن مجید کا بلا غلاف چھونا۔
وجه: (ا)لا يمسه الا المطهرون ( آیت ۷۹ سورۃ الواقعۃ ۵۶) (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عبد الله بن ابی بكر عن ابيه قال : كان في كتاب النبي لعمرو بن حزم الا تمس القرآن الاعلى طهر - ( دار قطنی ، باب فی تھی المحدث عن مس القرآن، ج اول ص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۴۲۹ رسن للبيتي ، باب الحائض لا تمس المصحف ولا تقرا القرآن ج ۴۶۱، نمبر ۱۴۷۸) اس قسم کی بہت سی احادیث دار قطنی میں نقل کی ہیں جن سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قرآن کو بغیر وضو چھونا جائز نہیں ہے۔(۳) عن عامر و سالم قالا : لا يمس الرجل الدرهم فيها كتاب الله و هو جنب قال : وقال عطاء و القاسم : يمسها اذا كانت مصرورة في خرقة ، مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، باب ۱۳۸ الرجل يمس الدراهم وهو جنب ، ج اول ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۱۲۱۹ار مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب مس المصحف والدراهم التي فيها القرآن، ج اول ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۳۳۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ درھم کو رکھنے کی جوتھیلی ہوتی
Translation: (252) (43) Touching the Quran without a cover. Evidence: (1) 'None touch it except the purified' (Surah al-Waqi'ah 56:79) (2) Hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Bakr from his father: 'In the letter of the Prophet to Amr ibn Hazm: Do not touch the Quran except in a state of purity.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi) Many such hadiths are narrated in Darqutni showing that touching the Quran without wudu is not permissible. (3) From Amir and Salim: 'A man should not touch a dirham that has the name of Allah on it while he is junub.' They said: 'Ata and al-Qasim said: He may touch it if it is wrapped in a cloth.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) This athar indicates that a dirham kept in a pouch...
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proofs for the prohibition of touching the Quran without a cover for a menstruating woman or a junub. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified' (al-Waqi'ah 56:79), which indicates that only those in a state of ritual purity may touch the Mus'haf. Further evidence comes from the Prophet's letter to Amr ibn Hazm commanding not to touch the Quran except in a state of purity. The text also discusses objects containing Quranic verses, such as dirhams with the name of Allah, and notes a difference of opinion among the Salaf: some prohibited touching them while junub, others permitted it if wrapped. The Hanafi school follows the general prohibition of touching the Quran without wudu, including for the menstruating woman.

Key Terms
مس (mass): Touching or making contact with the Quran, including the pages or covers that are attached.
مطهرون (mutahharun): Those who are purified, i.e., in a state of wudu or ghusl, free from major and minor ritual impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi ruling that a menstruating woman cannot touch the Quran?
A) A hadith from the Prophet alone.
B) The Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified' and a hadith from the Prophet's letter.
C) Consensus of the Companions only.
D) Qiyas on the prohibition of prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits touching the Quran without ritual purity based on clear textual evidence; this prohibition extends to any part of the Mus'haf and is lifted only by performing wudu or ghusl.

Why Salah and Fasting Are Prohibited During Hayd
Ruling with proof for prohibition of salah and sawm during hayd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prayer and fasting are prohibited during hayd, explain the hadith proof, and distinguish the consequence (qada for fasting, none for salah).

Core Idea
A menstruating woman must not pray or fast; missed salah is not made up, but missed fasts are.

This passage addresses a fundamental ruling for women: the prohibition of performing salah and sawm during the state of hayd (menstruation). While the ruling is well-known, understanding its proof and the specific consequences (which acts require qada and which do not) is essential. Let's examine the text and its authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (salah and sawm during hayd) and what the hukm (legal ruling) is: haram.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish from Bukhari. Note its category (Sunnah ahad).
The hadith actually discusses istihadah, but the command to leave prayer during hayd is explicit.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Identify the operative phrase: 'fa idha aqbalat al-haydatu fataraki al-salah' – the imperative 'leave prayer' proves prohibition.
For fasting, the proof is qiyas (analogy) to salah, as both require purity.
4
Note the thamarah (consequence)
Determine the practical consequence: missed salah is not made up (qada), but missed fasts are. This is a key distinction in the Hanafi school.
The hadith only mentions leaving prayer; the ruling on fasting is derived by consensus and analogy.
5
Evaluate cross-madhhab agreement
Check that this ruling is agreed upon by all schools (muttafaq alayh), though the issue of qada for salah differs.
Shafi'is require qada for missed salah; Hanafis do not, due to hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يحرم بالحيض والنفاس (۲۵۱) والصوم وقراءة آية من القرآن (۲۵۲) ومشها الا بغلاف (۲۵۳) ودخول مسجد ہے کہ حائضہ عورت نہ نماز پڑھے اور نہ روزہ رکھے۔ (۲) عن عائشة انها قالت قالت فاطمة بنت ابي حبيش لرسول الله لا يا رسول الله اني لا اطهر افأدع الصلاة ؟ فقال رسول الله علم انما ذالک عرق و لیس بالحيضة ، فاذا اقبلت الحيضة فاتركى الصلاة فاذا ذهب قدرها فاغسلى عنك الدم و صلی ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب الاستحاضة ،ص ۵۳، نمبر ۳۰۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حیض کی حالت میں نماز نہ پڑھے۔
What is prohibited during menstruation and postpartum: (251) fasting and reciting an ayah of Quran, (252) touching it without a wrapper, (253) entering a mosque. That is, a menstruating woman should not pray nor fast. (2) From Aisha that Fatima bint Abi Hubaish said to the Messenger of Allah, 'O Messenger of Allah, I do not become pure, should I abandon prayer?' The Messenger of Allah said, 'That is a vein and not menstruation. So when menstruation comes, leave prayer; when it goes, wash the blood from yourself and pray.' (Bukhari, Book of Istihada, p.53, no.306) This hadith says that during menstruation, one should not pray.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof for the prohibition of performing salah and fasting during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The author first lists the prohibitions in summary, then explains that a woman in this state must not pray or fast. The proof is the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish, which is actually about istihadah, but the author uses it to show the general principle that during actual hayd, salah is abandoned. For fasting, the ruling is derived by qiyas: just as salah is left because purity is required and the woman cannot purify herself, so too fasting is not valid during hayd. The hadith explicitly commands leaving salah during hayd, and the ruling for fasting is agreed upon in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حیض (hayd): Menstrual blood that flows from a woman's womb after the age of nine, lasting a minimum of three days and maximum of ten days.
نفساء (nufasa'): Postpartum bleeding after childbirth, which has the same rulings as hayd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two acts are prohibited for a menstruating woman?
A) Prayer and fasting
B) Reciting Quran and touching it without a wrapper
C) Entering a mosque and tawaf
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Salah and sawm are prohibited during hayd; missed salah does not require qada, but missed fasts do.

Prohibition of Touching Quran Without Wrapper During Menstruation
Ruling with proof for prohibition of touching the Quran without a wrapper during hayd/nifas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for touching the Quran during hayd/nifas and identify the three proofs used by the Hanafi school to establish the prohibition.

Core Idea
Touching the Quran without ritual purity is haram; a wrapper makes it permissible.

This lesson examines the ruling on touching the Quran during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The Hanafi school holds that direct contact with the mushaf is prohibited for anyone not in a state of ritual purity, but indirect contact via a wrapper is allowed. The author provides three proofs: a Qur'anic verse, a Prophetic hadith, and an athar from the salaf. Understanding these proofs will help you apply the ruling correctly and appreciate the school's reliance on multiple sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is touching the physical mushaf (Quran). The ruling is haram when the person is in a state of impurity (hayd, nifas, janabah, or without wudu). Touching via a wrapper is permissible.
The prohibition is limited to the mushaf; reciting from memory is allowed during hayd.
2
Locate the first proof
The primary proof is the Qur'anic verse 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79). Identify the text and its transmission (qat'i thubut).
Hanafi usul classifies this verse as zanni al-dalala because the word 'mutahharun' is open to interpretation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah of the verse
The negative phrase 'la yamassuhu' indicates prohibition. The word 'al-mutahharun' is interpreted by the Hanafi school as those who are ritually pure (i.e., in wudu or ghusl), not as angels. Thus the verse prohibits touching the Quran without purity.
Shafi'is and others also agree on this interpretation; a minority (Zahiri) restrict it to angels.
4
Identify the second and third proofs
The hadith from the Prophet's letter to Amr bin Hazm states: 'Do not touch the Quran except while pure.' The athar from the salaf (Amir, Salim, Ata, Qasim) analogizes touching a dirham with Allah's name via a wrapper to touching the Quran via a wrapper.
These strengthen the ruling and show continuity from the Prophet's practice and the understanding of the Companions.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A menstruating woman may touch the Quran only with a wrapper (e.g., a cloth cover or a separate booklet). If no wrapper is available, she should not touch it directly. This differs from schools that allow her to touch it without wrapper if she has wudu (but hayd prevents wudu being effective).
The ruling applies equally to a person in janabah or without wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۵۲) (۴۳) قرآن مجید کا بلا غلاف چھونا۔ وجه: (ا)لا يمسه الا المطهرون ( آیت ۷۹ سورۃ الواقعۃ ۵۶) (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عبد الله بن ابی بکر عن ابيه قال : كان في كتاب النبي لعمرو بن حزم الا تمس القرآن الاعلى طهر - ( دار قطنی ، باب فی تھی المحدث عن مس القرآن، ج اول ص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۴۲۹ رسن للبيتي ، باب الحائض لا تمس المصحف ولا تقرا القرآن ج ۴۶۱، نمبر ۱۴۷۸) اس قسم کی بہت سی احادیث دار قطنی میں نقل کی ہیں جن سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قرآن کو بغیر وضو چھونا جائز نہیں ہے۔(۳) عن عامر و سالم قالا : لا يمس الرجل الدرهم فيها كتاب الله و هو جنب قال : وقال عطاء و القاسم : يمسها اذا كانت مصرورة في خرقة ، مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، باب ۱۳۸ الرجل يمس الدراهم وهو جنب ، ج اول ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۱۲۱۹ار مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب مس المصحف والدراهم التي فيها القرآن، ج اول ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۳۳۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ درھم کو رکھنے کی جوتھیلی ہوتی ہے اسکے ذریعہ درھم کو چھوئے ، اسی طرح قرآن کے رکھنے کا جو غلاف ہوتا ہے اسکے ذریعہ سے قرآن کو چھوئے۔
Translation: (252) (43) Touching the Noble Quran without a wrapper. Proof: (1) 'None touch it except the purified' (Surah Al-Waqi'ah 56:79) (2) A hadith: From Abdullah bin Abi Bakr from his father: 'In the letter of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Amr bin Hazm: Do not touch the Quran except while pure.' (Darqutni...) Many such hadiths are narrated in Darqutni which indicate that touching the Quran without wudu is not permissible. (3) From Amir and Salim: They said: 'A man in janabah should not touch a dirham that has Allah's name on it.' And Ata and Qasim said: 'He may touch it if it is wrapped in a cloth.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) This athar indicates that the pouch in which the dirham is kept should be used to touch it, and likewise the wrapper of the Quran should be used to touch the Quran.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the prohibition of touching the Qur'an during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas), as well as for anyone in a state of minor impurity (hadath) or major impurity (janabah). The author provides three proofs: First, the Qur'anic verse 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79) – the word 'mutahharun' implies those who are ritually pure (i.e., in wudu). Second, a hadith from the Prophet's letter to Amr bin Hazm: 'Do not touch the Quran except while pure.' Third, an athar from the salaf about touching dirhams with Allah's name; they allowed touching them via a wrapper. The same principle applies to the Qur'an: a menstruating woman (and others in impurity) may touch the mushaf only through a wrapper or cover. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
مطہرون (mutahharun): Those who are ritually pure, i.e., free from hadath (minor or major impurity) according to the Hanafi exegesis.
غلاف (ghilaf): A cover or wrapper that prevents direct touch of the mushaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the ayah 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79) prove according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only angels may touch the Quran
B) Only Muslims may touch the Quran
C) Only those in a state of ritual purity may touch the Quran
D) The Quran is untouchable

Key Takeaway
Directly touching the Quran without ritual purity is haram, but using a wrapper makes it permissible, based on Quran, hadith, and athar.

Prohibition of Entering Mosque and Tawaf During Menstruation
Ruling with proof for prohibition of entering mosque and tawaf during hayd/nifas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two prohibitions during menstruation and postpartum, identify the proofs, and apply the exception of passing through a mosque.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman must not enter a mosque (except passing through) nor perform tawaf until purification.

Menstruation and postpartum entail several prohibitions that affect worship. Among the most important are entering a mosque and performing tawaf. The Hanafi school, relying on Quranic text, prophetic hadith, and analogy, holds these acts to be absolutely prohibited. However, the prohibition on entering the mosque has a well-known exception: passing through without staying is permitted when necessary. This lesson unpacks the evidence and clarifies the ruling, including the unique Hanafi position on the Eidgah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited acts
The lesson explicitly states that entering the mosque and performing tawaf are prohibited for a menstruating (ha'idh), postpartum (nufasa'), and junub person. Recognize that the first prohibition is for entering to stay; the second is for the ritual circumambulation of the Kaaba.
2
Examine the first proof: Quranic verse
Read Surah An-Nisa 4:43: 'Do not approach the prayer while you are intoxicated ... nor while you are junub except passing through the way.' The Hanafi scholars interpret 'prayer' as the place of prayer (mosque). This verse directly prohibits junub from entering the mosque, except as a passer-by. By qiyas (analogy), the same ruling applies to menstruating women as they share the same state of ritual impurity.
The exception 'passing through' is crucial.
3
Examine the second proof: Hadith of Aisha
The hadith from Aisha (Abu Dawud) quotes the Prophet saying: 'Direct these huts away from the mosque, for I do not permit the mosque to a menstruating woman or a junub.' This is a clear textual prohibition. It also implies that tawaf, which takes place in the Sacred Mosque, is included.
4
Examine the proof for tawaf prohibition
The hadith from Aisha (Bukhari and Abu Dawud) reports that when she menstruated during Hajj, the Prophet told her to do all the Hajj rituals except tawaf until she becomes pure. This explicitly prohibits tawaf during menstruation, and by analogy, during postpartum.
Tawaf requires ritual purity (taharah).
5
Understand the Hanafi ruling on Eidgah
The hadith of Umm Atiyyah (Bukhari) shows that menstruating women are ordered to attend the Eid prayer but must stay away from the musalla (prayer area). The Hanafi school categorizes the Eidgah as a mosque, so the same prohibition applies: they must avoid the prayer area but may be present in the surrounding space.
This shows the comprehensive application of the mosque ruling.

ترجمه : (۲۵۳) [۵] مسجد میں داخل ہونا ۔ [4] اور طواف کرنا بھی ممنوع ہے۔ تشریح : حائضہ نفساء اور جنسی مسجد میں داخل نہ ہو، اور طواف کرنا مسجد حرام میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ طواف بھی نہ کرے۔ وجه : (۱) آیت میں ہے۔ یایھا الذین آمنوا لا تقربوا الصلوة و انتم سكرى حتى تعلموا ما تقولون و لا جنباً الا عابرى سبيل حتى تغتسلوا ( آیت ۴۳ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جنبی نماز یعنی مسجد کے قریب نہ جائے ، اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے حائضہ اور نفساء بھی مسجد میں داخل نہ ہوں ۔ (۲) سمعت عائشة ... فقال وجهوا هذه البيوت عن المسجد فانى لا احل المسجد لحائض ولا جنب ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی الجنب يدخل المسجد ، ص ۳۴، نمبر ۲۳۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حائضہ عورت مسجد میں داخل نہیں ہوسکتی۔ اور مسجد حرام میں طواف ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ طواف بھی نہیں کر سکتی۔ (۳) عورتوں کو عیدین میں شریک ہونے کی اجازت ہے لیکن حائضہ عورتیں عید گاہ سے الگ رہیں کیونکہ عید گاہ مسجد ہے اسلئے اس سے بھی حائضہ عورت کو الگ رہنے کا حکم دیا ، حدیث یہ ہے . عن ام عطية قالت : أمرنا أن نخرج الحيض يوم العيدين و ذوات الخدور فيشهدن جماعة المسلمين و دعوتهم ، ويعتزل الحيض عن مصلاهن ۔(بخاری شریف، باب وجو بالصلاة فی الثياب ،ص ۵۱، نمبر ( ۳۵ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حائضہ عورت عید گاہ سے الگ رہے کیونکہ وہ بھی مسجد ہے۔ (۴) اور طواف نہ کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة ..... قال لعلك نفست؟ قلت نعم قال فان ذالک شیء كتبه الـلـه على بنات آدم فافعل ما يفعل الحاج غير لا تطوفى بالبيت حتى تطهری ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب تقضی الحائض المناسک کلھا الا الطواف بالبيت، ص۱۵۳، نمبر ۳۰۵ را بوداود شریف، باب الحائض نقل بالحج ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۱۷۴۳) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حائضہ عورت طواف نہیں کرے گی۔
Translation: (253) [5] Entering the mosque. [4] And performing tawaf are also prohibited. Explanation: The menstruating woman, postpartum woman, and junub should not enter the mosque, and tawaf is performed in the Sacred Mosque, so she should not perform tawaf either. Proof: (1) In the ayah: 'O you who believe! Approach not the prayer while you are intoxicated until you know what you say, nor while you are junub except passing through the way until you bathe' (Surah An-Nisa 4:43). This ayah states that the junub should not go near the prayer (i.e., the mosque). By analogy (qiyas), the menstruating and postpartum women also should not enter the mosque. (2) I heard Aisha... she said: 'Direct these huts away from the mosque, for I do not permit the mosque to a menstruating woman or a junub.' (Abu Dawud no.232) This hadith shows that a menstruating woman cannot enter the mosque. And tawaf is performed in the Sacred Mosque, so she also cannot perform tawaf. (3) Women are allowed to attend the Eid prayers, but menstruating women should stay away from the Eidgah because the Eidgah is a mosque; therefore the menstruating woman is commanded to stay apart. The hadith: From Umm Atiyyah: 'We were ordered to bring out the menstruating women on the two Eids, and the women of seclusion, so that they witness the Muslims' gathering and their supplication, and the menstruating women should stay away from the place of prayer.' (Bukhari no.35) This hadith indicates that a menstruating woman should stay away from the Eidgah because it is also a mosque. (4) And as for not performing tawaf, there is this hadith: From Aisha... he (the Prophet) said: 'Perhaps you have begun your menses?' She said yes. He said: 'That is something Allah has written upon the daughters of Adam. So do what the pilgrim does except do not perform tawaf of the House until you become pure.' (Bukhari no.305, Abu Dawud no.1743) The hadith shows that a menstruating woman should not perform tawaf.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for two related prohibitions during menstruation and postpartum: entering a mosque and performing tawaf. The author explains that a menstruating woman (and junub) may not enter a mosque, except for passing through (e.g., as a traveller). The proofs include: (1) Quran 4:43, which prohibits junub from coming near the prayer (mosque) except as a passer-by; by analogy (qiyas), menstruating women have the same ruling. (2) A hadith from Aisha prohibiting the entry of a menstruating woman or junub into the mosque. (3) A hadith about Eid prayer: menstruating women attend but must stay away from the musalla (prayer area) because it is considered a mosque. (4) A hadith specifically prohibiting tawaf during menstruation until purity is regained. The Hanafi ruling is clear: entering the mosque and performing tawaf are both prohibited during hayd and nifas.

Key Terms
مسجد (masjid): A place established for the five daily prayers and congregational worship; includes the Sacred Mosque (Masjid al-Haram) and Eidgah (open prayer ground).
طواف (tawaf): The ritual circumambulation of the Kaaba, a pillar of Umrah and Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Fasting and praying
C) Reciting Quran and touching Quran
D) Sexual intercourse and intimacy

Key Takeaway
A menstruating or postpartum woman must avoid entering a mosque (except passing through) and must not perform tawaf until purified.

Prohibition of Sexual Intercourse and Intimacy During Menstruation
Ruling with proof for prohibition of intercourse and conditional intimacy during hayd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse and intimacy during menstruation, explain the proof from Quran 2:222, and apply the condition of the barrier (izar) to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
Intercourse during menstruation is absolutely haram; intimacy with a barrier is permissible, without it is prohibited due to risk.

This passage clarifies the rulings of intimacy during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. While intercourse is unequivocally forbidden, other intimacy between navel and knee requires a barrier to prevent potential transgression. Understanding the underpinning proof from the Quran and the effective cause ('illa) of harm allows a nuanced application of the law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, determine what act is being ruled upon: sexual intercourse (jima') and other intimacy between navel and knee. Then note the hukm: intercourse is haram; intimacy without barrier is prohibited, with barrier is permissible.
The text uses 'halal nahin hai' (not permissible) for intimacy without barrier.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites Quran 2:222 as the primary proof. Note the exact wording and its references to 'keeping away' and 'not approaching'.
The ayah is mutawatir in transmission (qat'i al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is open to interpretation (zanni).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the ayah proves the ruling: the command 'fa'tazilu' and 'la taqrabuhunna' imply prohibition of all proximity that may lead to intercourse, because the 'illa is 'adha (harm).
The Hanafi school extends this to intimacy between navel and knee due to the risk of arousal leading to intercourse.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Identify that there is disagreement: some Hanafis consider intimacy without barrier as makruh tanzih, but the mufta bihi view is prohibition (makruh tahrimi or haram). Also note cross-madhhab differences.
The Shafi'i school, for example, also prohibits intercourse but allows intimacy with a barrier, while Maliki and Hanbali are stricter.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Understand why the cautious view (prohibition without barrier) is relied upon: it is based on ihtiyat (precaution) to prevent falling into haram, supported by the general purport of the ayah.
The authority_weight is from later Hanafi fatawa (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۵۴) [۷] جماع - [۸] ناف کے نیچے سے لیکر زانو کے نیچے تک فائدہ اٹھانا بھی حلال نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : حائضہ اور نفساء عورت سے جماع کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور شرمگاہ میں وطی نہ کرے تو ناف کے نیچے سے زانو کے نیچے تک استعمال کرنا جائز ہے، لیکن خطرہ ہے کہ جماع کر بیٹھے اس لئے اس کو نا جائز قرار دیا ، البتہ اس پر ازار لپیٹ لے اور اس کے اوپر سے فائدہ اٹھائے تو جائز ہے، کیونکہ اب کوئی خطرہ نہیں ہے۔ وجه (1) آیت میں ہے۔ ویسئلونک عن المحيض قل هو اذى فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض ولاتقربوهن حتى يطهرن (آیت ۲۲۲ سورة البقرة (۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ حیض والی عورت کے قریب بھی مت جاؤ۔ (۲) ولی تو کرنا حرام
Translation: (254) [7] Sexual intercourse – [8] Benefiting from what is below the navel to below the knee is also not permissible. Explanation: Sexual intercourse with a menstruating or postpartum woman is haram. And if one does not engage in intercourse, then using the area from below the navel to below the knee is permissible, but due to the fear that one may engage in intercourse (in the heat of passion), it has been declared impermissible. However, if she wraps an izar (lower garment) around herself and then enjoys from above it, it is permissible because there is no fear. Proof: (1) In the ayah: 'And they ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they become pure' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:222). This ayah states not to go near the menstruating woman. (2) [The text ends abruptly but context is clear: intimacy beyond that is also prohibited.]
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the prohibition of sexual intercourse and certain types of intimacy during menstruation and postpartum. The author distinguishes between absolute prohibition of intercourse (haram) and the conditional prohibition of intimacy between the navel and knee. Direct intercourse is clearly haram based on Quran 2:222. For other intimate contact, the ruling is that the area between the navel and knee may be enjoyed if there is no fear of leading to intercourse; but because of that risk, the cautious ruling (ihtiyat) is to prohibit it unless a barrier (izar) is worn. This is a typical Hanafi position: the underlying 'illa (effective cause) is the risk of sinful intercourse, so if the risk is eliminated by a physical barrier, the intimacy becomes permissible. The proof is the general command to 'keep away' (fa'tazilu) which implies all proximity that may lead to intercourse.

Key Terms
جماع (jima'): Sexual intercourse; specifically insertion of the male genital into the female genital.
ازار (izar): A lower garment wrapped around the waist to cover the area between navel and knee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible if she is willing
B) Permissible after three days
C) Haram
D) Makruh tanzih

Key Takeaway
Intercourse during menstruation is absolutely haram; intimacy between navel and knee is prohibited without a barrier but permissible with one, based on Quranic command to avoid proximity during hayd.

Prohibitions during Menstruation and Postpartum Bleeding
Lists prohibitions and conditions for resuming intimacy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four prohibitions for a menstruating or postpartum woman and explain the Hanafi evidence for each prohibition.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman must not enter the mosque, perform tawaf, engage in intercourse, or enjoy intimacy between navel and knee without a barrier.

This lesson examines the specific acts prohibited during hayd (menstruation) and nifas (postpartum bleeding) according to the Hanafi school. The passage lists four prohibitions: entering the mosque, performing tawaf, sexual intercourse, and deriving pleasure between the navel and knee without a barrier. Each prohibition is supported by clear proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, and qiyas. Understanding these prohibitions is essential for a Muslim woman's observance of purity during these times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibitions
Read the matn and list the four prohibited acts: mosque entry, tawaf, intercourse, and intimacy below navel to knee without barrier.
The fourth prohibition has an exception when a barrier (izar) is used.
2
Analyze the proof for mosque entry
Examine the Quranic verse (4:43) from which the Hanafis derive the prohibition for the menstruating woman by qiyas on the junub, and the hadith from Aisha (ra) explicitly prohibiting it.
The hadith is used as direct evidence.
3
Understand the prohibition of tawaf
Note that tawaf is performed within the mosque, so the same prohibition applies; the hadith of Aisha (ra) during Hajj specifically forbids tawaf until purification.
Tawaf is a form of worship requiring purity.
4
Examine the evidence for intimacy restrictions
Study the Quranic verse (2:222) prohibiting approach during menstruation, and the hadiths showing that intimacy with a barrier (izar) is permitted while direct skin contact in the forbidden area is not.
The barrier eliminates the risk of intercourse.

ترجمه : (۲۵۴) [۷] جماع - [۸] ناف کے نیچے سے لیکر زانو کے نیچے تک فائدہ اٹھانا بھی حلال نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : حائضہ اور نفساء عورت سے جماع کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور شرمگاہ میں وطی نہ کرے تو ناف کے نیچے سے زانو کے نیچے تک استعمال کرنا جائز ہے، لیکن خطرہ ہے کہ جماع کر بیٹھے اس لئے اس کو نا جائز قرار دیا ، البتہ اس پر ازار لپیٹ لے اور اس کے اوپر سے فائدہ اٹھائے تو جائز ہے، کیونکہ اب کوئی خطرہ نہیں ہے۔
وجه (1) آیت میں ہے۔ ویسئلونک عن المحيض قل هو اذى فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض ولاتقربوهن حتى يطهرن (آیت ۲۲۲ سورة البقرة (۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ حیض والی عورت کے قریب بھی مت جاؤ۔ (۲) ولی تو کرنا حرام
صلى الله
ت۔ البتہ عورت کو ازار پہنا کر اسکے ساتھ لیٹ سکتا ہے۔ اسکے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ سمعت ميمونة تقول : كان رسول الله کوازار اذا اراد أن يباشر امرأة من نسائه أمر ها فاتزرت و هی حائض بخاری شریف، باب مباشرة الحائض ، ص۵۳ نمبر ۳۰۳)(۳) عن ميمونة قالت ان النبي لعل الله كان يباشر المرأة من نسائه و هي حائض اذا كان عليها ازار الى انصاف الفخذين او الركبتين تحتجز به ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الرجل یصیب منها ما دون الجماع ، ص ۴۸، نمبر ۲۶۷) ان احادیث میں ہے کہ حیض کی حالت میں ازار کے اوپر سے فائدہ اٹھا سکتا ہے۔(۴) صرف جماع حرام ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے. عـن بـعض ازواج النبي قالت ان النبي كان اذا اراد من الحائض شيئا القى على فرجها ثوبا ۔ ( ابودا وشریف، باب فی الرجل یصیب منها ما دون الجماع، ص ۴۹، نمبر۲۷۲)
صلى الله
ترجمه : (۲۵۵) اور جب حیض و نفاس کا خون اکثر مدت میں منقطع ہو تو بلا انسل وچلی جائز ہے۔ تشریح : مثلا حیض کی اکثر مدت دس دن ہے، اور دس دن پر خون آنا بند ہوا تو اب بغیر عورت کے نہائے ہوئے بھی وطی کرسکتا ہے، کیونکہ اب تو حیض آئے گا ہی نہیں ، اور اگر آئے گا تو وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہو گا ، اس لئے عورت یقینی طور پر پاک ہوگئی ۔ اسی طرح نفاس کی اکثر مدت چالیس روز ہے، اور چالیس روز پر خون بند ہوا تو بغیر نہائے ہوئے بھی وطی کر سکتا ہے ، کیونکہ عورت یقینی طور پر
پاک ہو گئی۔
وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے کہ عورت پاک ہو جائے تو اس سے وطی کرو، اور یہ عورت یقینی طور پر پاک ہوگئی ہے اس لئے اس سے وطی کرنا جائز ہے ۔ویسئلونک عن المحيض قل هو اذى فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض و لا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن فاذا تطهرن فأتوهن من حيث أمر كم الله ان الله يحب التوابين و يحب المتطهرين (آیت ۲۲۲،سورة البقرة ٢) (۲)۔ عن مجاهد في قوله عزوجل ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن حتى ينقطع الدم فاذا تطهرن قال
يقول اذا اغتسلن (سن للبیہقی ، باب الحائض لا توحاً حتى تظهر وتغتسل ، ج اول ص ۴۶۲ نمبر ۱۴۸۲) اس اثر میں خون منقطع ہو نے کو نسل کرنا قراردیا گیا ہے اسلئے غسل نہ بھی کرے تو صحبت جائز ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۵۶) اور جب اپنی عادت کے موافق کم مدت میں خون منقطع ہو تو ولی جائز نہیں مگر یہ کہ غسل کرلے یا (غسل پر قادر نہ ہو تو ) تیم کرلے اور نماز پڑھ لے۔ تشریح : مثلا عورت کی پرانی عادت پانچ دن خون آنے کی تھی اب چار دن میں خون آنا بند ہو گیا تو ابھی یہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ ایک روز اور خون آجائے کیونکہ اس کی عادت پانچ روز کی ہے اس لئے یہ کمل پاک نہیں ہوئی اس لئے اس سے ولی کرنا جائز نہیں جب تک
Fruit of Success Volume 1. What is prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. And tawaf (254) and intercourse and enjoyment from below the navel to below the knee. Through it [the wrapper] touch the dirham, similarly through the wrapper of the Quran touch it. Translation: (253) [5] Entering the mosque. [4] And tawaf is also prohibited. Explanation: The menstruating woman, woman in postpartum bleeding, and the sexually impure should not enter the mosque, and tawaf occurs in the Sacred Mosque, so she should also not perform tawaf. Evidence: (1) The verse: 'O you who have believed, do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated until you know what you are saying, nor while you are in a state of janabah, except those passing through, until you have washed.' (Surah al-Nisa 4:43) This verse states that the junub should not approach prayer, i.e., the mosque, and by analogy, the menstruating woman and woman in postpartum bleeding should also not enter the mosque. (2) I heard Aisha... she said: 'Direct these houses away from the mosque, for I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman or a junub.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-junub yadkhul al-masjid, p.34, no.232) This hadith indicates that a menstruating woman cannot enter the mosque. And tawaf occurs in the Sacred Mosque, so she cannot perform tawaf. (3) Women are allowed to attend the two Eid prayers, but menstruating women should stay away from the prayer ground because it is like a mosque; thus the menstruating woman is commanded to stay away. The hadith: From Umm Atiyyah, she said: 'We were commanded to bring out the menstruating women on the two Eids and the secluded women, so they witness the congregation of Muslims and their supplication, and the menstruating women should keep away from their prayer place.' (Bukhari, Bab wujub al-salat fi al-thiyab, p.51, no. 305) This hadith states that the menstruating woman should stay away from the Eid prayer ground because it is also a mosque. (4) And for not performing tawaf, there is this hadith: From Aisha... he said: 'Perhaps you are menstruating?' I said: 'Yes.' He said: 'That is something Allah has decreed upon the daughters of Adam, so do what the pilgrim does, but do not circumambulate the House until you become pure.' (Bukhari, Bab taqdi al-ha'id al-manasik kullaha illa al-tawaf bi al-bayt, p.153, no.305; Abu Dawud, Bab al-ha'id tuqall bi al-hajj, p.257, no.1743) The hadith indicates that a menstruating woman should not perform tawaf. Translation: (254) [7] Intercourse - [8] Deriving enjoyment from below the navel to below the knee is also not permissible. Explanation: Sexual intercourse with a menstruating or postpartum woman is forbidden. And if one does not penetrate the private part, then using the area from below the navel to below the knee is permissible, but there is the risk of engaging in intercourse, so it has been declared impermissible. However, if she wraps a waist-wrapper (izar) over herself and he derives enjoyment from above it, it is permissible because there is no longer any risk. Evidence: (1) The verse: 'And they ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they become pure.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:222) This verse says: Do not even go near the menstruating woman. (2) But intercourse is forbidden. However, he can lie with her after she wears a waist-wrapper. For this, the hadith: I heard Maymunah say: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) wanted to be intimate with one of his wives while she was menstruating, he would command her to wear a waist-wrapper, and she would wear it.' (Bukhari, Bab mubasharat al-ha'id, p.53, no.303) (3) From Maymunah: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) would be intimate with his wives while they were menstruating if they wore a waist-wrapper reaching to the middle of the thighs or knees, tying it tightly.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-rajul yusib minha ma dun al-jima', p.48, no.267) These hadiths indicate that during menstruation, enjoyment can be had from above the waist-wrapper. (4) Only intercourse is forbidden, as evidence of this hadith: From some of the wives of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) wanted something from a menstruating woman, he would place a cloth over her private part.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-rajul yusib minha ma dun al-jima', p.49, no.272) Translation: (255) And when the blood stops after the maximum duration of menses and postpartum bleeding, intercourse is permissible without ghusl. Explanation: For example, the maximum duration of menses is ten days, and if the blood stops on the tenth day, then he can have intercourse with her even if she has not bathed, because now no menses will come; if it does come, it is the blood of istihadah, so the woman is definitely pure. Similarly, the maximum duration of postpartum bleeding is forty days; if the blood stops on the fortieth day, he can have intercourse without her bathing, because the woman is definitely pure. Evidence: (1) The verse states: 'So when they have purified themselves, go to them from where Allah has commanded you.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:222) And this woman has definitely become pure, so intercourse with her is permissible. (2) From Mujahid regarding the statement of Allah 'until they become pure': he said: until the blood stops; 'so when they have purified themselves': he said: when they have bathed. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-ha'id la tuha' hatta tathur wa taghtasil, vol.1, p.462, no.1482) This effect considers the stopping of blood as purification, so even if she does not bathe, intercourse is permissible. Translation: (256) And when the blood stops according to her habitual duration [but less than maximum], intercourse is not permissible unless she performs ghusl or (if unable to perform ghusl) tayammum and prays. Explanation: For example, a woman's habit was five days of blood, and now the blood stopped after four days. It is very possible that another day of blood will come because her habit is five days, so she has not become completely pure; therefore, intercourse with her is not permissible until she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof commentary from Thamaratun Najah, explaining the prohibitions during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas) in the Hanafi school. It opens with a concise matn listing what is prohibited: entering the mosque, performing tawaf, engaging in intercourse, and deriving pleasure from the area between the navel and knee. The commentary then expands on each prohibition with detailed evidence from the Quran, Hadith, and qiyas (analogy). The first prohibition is entering the mosque. The author cites Quran 4:43, which prohibits the junub from approaching the mosque, and extends this ruling to the menstruating woman by analogy (qiyas). A hadith from Aisha (ra) explicitly states that a menstruating woman should not enter the mosque. Similarly, tawaf is prohibited because it is performed within the Sacred Mosque, which is a mosque. Evidence is also provided from the hadith of Umm Atiyyah about menstruating women staying away from the Eid prayer ground, which is considered a mosque in status. For tawaf, the hadith of Aisha (ra) during Hajj explicitly forbids the menstruating woman from circumambulating the Kaaba until she becomes pure. The second prohibition covers sexual intercourse and intimacy. Intercourse is absolutely forbidden, based on Quran 2:222. Intimacy below the navel and above the knee is generally impermissible due to the risk of leading to intercourse. However, the Hanafi school permits intimacy if the woman wears a waist-wrapper (izar) as a barrier, citing multiple hadiths from Maymunah (ra) and the practice of the Prophet (saw). The passage then transitions to the conditions under which intercourse becomes permissible after the bleeding stops. The general principle is that purity must be certain. The author distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the blood stops after reaching the maximum duration (10 days for hayd, 40 days for nifas), the woman is deemed pure with certainty, and intercourse is allowed even without ghusl, because any subsequent bleeding would be istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding). This is supported by the literal interpretation of Quran 2:222—'purified themselves' can mean the cessation of blood, not necessarily a ritual bath. An athar from Mujahid confirms this. (2) If the blood stops before the maximum but within her usual habit, she is not considered purified until she performs ghusl (or tayammum and prays if unable to perform ghusl). The reasoning is that her habit indicates the possibility of further bleeding, so certainty of purity is lacking. The commentary uses an example: a woman whose habit is five days, but blood stops on the fourth day—intercourse is not permissible until she bathes. The passage consistently uses Hanafi methodology: primary reliance on Quran and authentic hadith, analogical reasoning, and consideration of istihsan (juristic preference) in the permissibility of intimacy with a barrier. The source authority weight is that of a later sharh (commentary) on a matn, but the rulings align with the Hanafi mu'tamad (relied-upon position) found in the Zahir al-Riwayah. The commentary does not mention any intra-madhhab disagreement, indicating these are settled rulings.

Key Terms
حائض (ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding (hayd)
نفساء (nafsa'): A woman experiencing postpartum bleeding (nifas)
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah, a pillar of Hajj and Umrah
جماع (jima'): Sexual intercourse, specifically penetration
استمتاع (istimta'): Physical enjoyment or intimacy short of intercourse
ازار (izar): A waist-wrapper or lower garment used as a barrier during intimacy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT prohibited for a menstruating woman according to this passage?
A) Entering the mosque
B) Performing tawaf
C) Reciting Quran from memory
D) Intimacy without a barrier between navel and knee

Key Takeaway
A menstruating or postpartum woman must refrain from entering mosques, performing tawaf, sexual intercourse, and direct intimacy between navel and knee unless a barrier (izar) is used.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Resuming Intercourse After Bleeding Stops
Explains the two scenarios for permissibility after bleeding stops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two scenarios (maximum duration vs habitual duration) and apply the Hanafi ruling on when intercourse becomes permissible after menstrual or postpartum bleeding stops.

Core Idea
After maximum duration, purity is certain; within habitual duration, ghusl is needed for certainty.

Once the bleeding of hayd or nifas ceases, when is it permissible to resume sexual intercourse? The Hanafi school answers with a nuanced ruling that depends on the duration of bleeding. If the blood stops after reaching the maximum limit (10 days for hayd, 40 days for nifas), intercourse is allowed immediately without ghusl. But if it stops before the maximum and within the woman's habitual duration, intercourse is not allowed until she performs ghusl (or tayammum and prays if unable). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and evidence behind this important differentiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note two distinct cases: (1) blood stops after maximum duration (10 days hayd, 40 days nifas) and (2) blood stops within the habitual duration but before the maximum (e.g., habit of 5 days, stops on day 4).
The ruling differs based on certainty of purity.
2
Understand the ruling for maximum duration
When bleeding stops after the maximum, the woman is definitively pure. Any further bleeding would be istihadah (non-menstrual). Intercourse is allowed without ghusl because purity is certain.
The evidence includes the verse 'until they become pure' interpreted as cessation of blood.
3
Analyze the ruling for habitual duration
When bleeding stops before the maximum but within her habit, there is a possibility of further bleeding. Therefore, purity is not certain. Intercourse is not allowed until she performs ghusl (or tayammum if unable) and prays, which acts as a verification of purity.
This is stricter to avoid transgression.
4
Examine the evidence
The author cites Quran 2:222 and the athar from Mujahid explaining that 'purification' in the verse means cessation of blood for the first scenario, but requires ghusl for the second scenario.
The Hanafi interpretation combines both literal and contextual meanings.

صلى الله
ت۔ البتہ عورت کو ازار پہنا کر اسکے ساتھ لیٹ سکتا ہے۔ اسکے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ سمعت ميمونة تقول : كان رسول الله کوازار اذا اراد أن يباشر امرأة من نسائه أمر ها فاتزرت و هی حائض بخاری شریف، باب مباشرة الحائض ، ص۵۳ نمبر ۳۰۳)(۳) عن ميمونة قالت ان النبي لعل الله كان يباشر المرأة من نسائه و هي حائض اذا كان عليها ازار الى انصاف الفخذين او الركبتين تحتجز به ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الرجل یصیب منها ما دون الجماع ، ص ۴۸، نمبر ۲۶۷) ان احادیث میں ہے کہ حیض کی حالت میں ازار کے اوپر سے فائدہ اٹھا سکتا ہے۔(۴) صرف جماع حرام ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے. عـن بـعض ازواج النبي قالت ان النبي كان اذا اراد من الحائض شيئا القى على فرجها ثوبا ۔ ( ابودا وشریف، باب فی الرجل یصیب منها ما دون الجماع، ص ۴۹، نمبر۲۷۲)
صلى الله
ترجمه : (۲۵۵) اور جب حیض و نفاس کا خون اکثر مدت میں منقطع ہو تو بلا انسل وچلی جائز ہے۔ تشریح : مثلا حیض کی اکثر مدت دس دن ہے، اور دس دن پر خون آنا بند ہوا تو اب بغیر عورت کے نہائے ہوئے بھی وطی کرسکتا ہے، کیونکہ اب تو حیض آئے گا ہی نہیں ، اور اگر آئے گا تو وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہو گا ، اس لئے عورت یقینی طور پر پاک ہوگئی ۔ اسی طرح نفاس کی اکثر مدت چالیس روز ہے، اور چالیس روز پر خون بند ہوا تو بغیر نہائے ہوئے بھی وطی کر سکتا ہے ، کیونکہ عورت یقینی طور پر
پاک ہو گئی۔
وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے کہ عورت پاک ہو جائے تو اس سے وطی کرو، اور یہ عورت یقینی طور پر پاک ہوگئی ہے اس لئے اس سے وطی کرنا جائز ہے ۔ویسئلونک عن المحيض قل هو اذى فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض و لا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن فاذا تطهرن فأتوهن من حيث أمر كم الله ان الله يحب التوابين و يحب المتطهرين (آیت ۲۲۲،سورة البقرة ٢) (۲)۔ عن مجاهد في قوله عزوجل ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن حتى ينقطع الدم فاذا تطهرن قال
يقول اذا اغتسلن (سن للبیہقی ، باب الحائض لا توحاً حتى تظهر وتغتسل ، ج اول ص ۴۶۲ نمبر ۱۴۸۲) اس اثر میں خون منقطع ہو نے کو نسل کرنا قراردیا گیا ہے اسلئے غسل نہ بھی کرے تو صحبت جائز ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۵۶) اور جب اپنی عادت کے موافق کم مدت میں خون منقطع ہو تو ولی جائز نہیں مگر یہ کہ غسل کرلے یا (غسل پر قادر نہ ہو تو ) تیم کرلے اور نماز پڑھ لے۔ تشریح : مثلا عورت کی پرانی عادت پانچ دن خون آنے کی تھی اب چار دن میں خون آنا بند ہو گیا تو ابھی یہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ ایک روز اور خون آجائے کیونکہ اس کی عادت پانچ روز کی ہے اس لئے یہ کمل پاک نہیں ہوئی اس لئے اس سے ولی کرنا جائز نہیں جب تک
Fruit of Success Volume 1. What is prohibited during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. And tawaf (254) and intercourse and enjoyment from below the navel to below the knee. Through it [the wrapper] touch the dirham, similarly through the wrapper of the Quran touch it. Translation: (253) [5] Entering the mosque. [4] And tawaf is also prohibited. Explanation: The menstruating woman, woman in postpartum bleeding, and the sexually impure should not enter the mosque, and tawaf occurs in the Sacred Mosque, so she should also not perform tawaf. Evidence: (1) The verse: 'O you who have believed, do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated until you know what you are saying, nor while you are in a state of janabah, except those passing through, until you have washed.' (Surah al-Nisa 4:43) This verse states that the junub should not approach prayer, i.e., the mosque, and by analogy, the menstruating woman and woman in postpartum bleeding should also not enter the mosque. (2) I heard Aisha... she said: 'Direct these houses away from the mosque, for I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman or a junub.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-junub yadkhul al-masjid, p.34, no.232) This hadith indicates that a menstruating woman cannot enter the mosque. And tawaf occurs in the Sacred Mosque, so she cannot perform tawaf. (3) Women are allowed to attend the two Eid prayers, but menstruating women should stay away from the prayer ground because it is like a mosque; thus the menstruating woman is commanded to stay away. The hadith: From Umm Atiyyah, she said: 'We were commanded to bring out the menstruating women on the two Eids and the secluded women, so they witness the congregation of Muslims and their supplication, and the menstruating women should keep away from their prayer place.' (Bukhari, Bab wujub al-salat fi al-thiyab, p.51, no. 305) This hadith states that the menstruating woman should stay away from the Eid prayer ground because it is also a mosque. (4) And for not performing tawaf, there is this hadith: From Aisha... he said: 'Perhaps you are menstruating?' I said: 'Yes.' He said: 'That is something Allah has decreed upon the daughters of Adam, so do what the pilgrim does, but do not circumambulate the House until you become pure.' (Bukhari, Bab taqdi al-ha'id al-manasik kullaha illa al-tawaf bi al-bayt, p.153, no.305; Abu Dawud, Bab al-ha'id tuqall bi al-hajj, p.257, no.1743) The hadith indicates that a menstruating woman should not perform tawaf. Translation: (254) [7] Intercourse - [8] Deriving enjoyment from below the navel to below the knee is also not permissible. Explanation: Sexual intercourse with a menstruating or postpartum woman is forbidden. And if one does not penetrate the private part, then using the area from below the navel to below the knee is permissible, but there is the risk of engaging in intercourse, so it has been declared impermissible. However, if she wraps a waist-wrapper (izar) over herself and he derives enjoyment from above it, it is permissible because there is no longer any risk. Evidence: (1) The verse: 'And they ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation and do not approach them until they become pure.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:222) This verse says: Do not even go near the menstruating woman. (2) But intercourse is forbidden. However, he can lie with her after she wears a waist-wrapper. For this, the hadith: I heard Maymunah say: 'When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) wanted to be intimate with one of his wives while she was menstruating, he would command her to wear a waist-wrapper, and she would wear it.' (Bukhari, Bab mubasharat al-ha'id, p.53, no.303) (3) From Maymunah: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) would be intimate with his wives while they were menstruating if they wore a waist-wrapper reaching to the middle of the thighs or knees, tying it tightly.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-rajul yusib minha ma dun al-jima', p.48, no.267) These hadiths indicate that during menstruation, enjoyment can be had from above the waist-wrapper. (4) Only intercourse is forbidden, as evidence of this hadith: From some of the wives of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) wanted something from a menstruating woman, he would place a cloth over her private part.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-rajul yusib minha ma dun al-jima', p.49, no.272) Translation: (255) And when the blood stops after the maximum duration of menses and postpartum bleeding, intercourse is permissible without ghusl. Explanation: For example, the maximum duration of menses is ten days, and if the blood stops on the tenth day, then he can have intercourse with her even if she has not bathed, because now no menses will come; if it does come, it is the blood of istihadah, so the woman is definitely pure. Similarly, the maximum duration of postpartum bleeding is forty days; if the blood stops on the fortieth day, he can have intercourse without her bathing, because the woman is definitely pure. Evidence: (1) The verse states: 'So when they have purified themselves, go to them from where Allah has commanded you.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:222) And this woman has definitely become pure, so intercourse with her is permissible. (2) From Mujahid regarding the statement of Allah 'until they become pure': he said: until the blood stops; 'so when they have purified themselves': he said: when they have bathed. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-ha'id la tuha' hatta tathur wa taghtasil, vol.1, p.462, no.1482) This effect considers the stopping of blood as purification, so even if she does not bathe, intercourse is permissible. Translation: (256) And when the blood stops according to her habitual duration [but less than maximum], intercourse is not permissible unless she performs ghusl or (if unable to perform ghusl) tayammum and prays. Explanation: For example, a woman's habit was five days of blood, and now the blood stopped after four days. It is very possible that another day of blood will come because her habit is five days, so she has not become completely pure; therefore, intercourse with her is not permissible until she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof commentary from Thamaratun Najah, explaining the prohibitions during menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas) in the Hanafi school. It opens with a concise matn listing what is prohibited: entering the mosque, performing tawaf, engaging in intercourse, and deriving pleasure from the area between the navel and knee. The commentary then expands on each prohibition with detailed evidence from the Quran, Hadith, and qiyas (analogy). The first prohibition is entering the mosque. The author cites Quran 4:43, which prohibits the junub from approaching the mosque, and extends this ruling to the menstruating woman by analogy (qiyas). A hadith from Aisha (ra) explicitly states that a menstruating woman should not enter the mosque. Similarly, tawaf is prohibited because it is performed within the Sacred Mosque, which is a mosque. Evidence is also provided from the hadith of Umm Atiyyah about menstruating women staying away from the Eid prayer ground, which is considered a mosque in status. For tawaf, the hadith of Aisha (ra) during Hajj explicitly forbids the menstruating woman from circumambulating the Kaaba until she becomes pure. The second prohibition covers sexual intercourse and intimacy. Intercourse is absolutely forbidden, based on Quran 2:222. Intimacy below the navel and above the knee is generally impermissible due to the risk of leading to intercourse. However, the Hanafi school permits intimacy if the woman wears a waist-wrapper (izar) as a barrier, citing multiple hadiths from Maymunah (ra) and the practice of the Prophet (saw). The passage then transitions to the conditions under which intercourse becomes permissible after the bleeding stops. The general principle is that purity must be certain. The author distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the blood stops after reaching the maximum duration (10 days for hayd, 40 days for nifas), the woman is deemed pure with certainty, and intercourse is allowed even without ghusl, because any subsequent bleeding would be istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding). This is supported by the literal interpretation of Quran 2:222—'purified themselves' can mean the cessation of blood, not necessarily a ritual bath. An athar from Mujahid confirms this. (2) If the blood stops before the maximum but within her usual habit, she is not considered purified until she performs ghusl (or tayammum and prays if unable to perform ghusl). The reasoning is that her habit indicates the possibility of further bleeding, so certainty of purity is lacking. The commentary uses an example: a woman whose habit is five days, but blood stops on the fourth day—intercourse is not permissible until she bathes. The passage consistently uses Hanafi methodology: primary reliance on Quran and authentic hadith, analogical reasoning, and consideration of istihsan (juristic preference) in the permissibility of intimacy with a barrier. The source authority weight is that of a later sharh (commentary) on a matn, but the rulings align with the Hanafi mu'tamad (relied-upon position) found in the Zahir al-Riwayah. The commentary does not mention any intra-madhhab disagreement, indicating these are settled rulings.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadah): Chronic non-menstrual bleeding that does not prevent prayers, fasting, or intercourse
عادة (adah/habit): A woman's typical number of days for menstrual bleeding
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath required to become pure after menstrual bleeding
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with pure earth when water is unavailable or harmful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman's menstrual habit is 6 days. On day 7 her bleeding stops. According to the Hanafi school, what must she do before intercourse?
A) Nothing, because the blood stopped
B) Perform ghusl (or tayammum and pray) before intercourse
C) Wait until day 10
D) Perform wudu only

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after bleeding stops is permissible either immediately if the maximum duration is reached (certainty of purity) or after ghusl/tayammum if the bleeding stopped within her habitual duration (to resolve uncertainty).

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Permissibility of Intercourse After Hayd and Nifas
Explaining when intercourse becomes permissible after menstrual or postpartum bleeding ceases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi scenarios when intercourse becomes permissible after hayd/nifas and identify the condition(s) required for each.

Core Idea
Intercourse after hayd/nifas is permissible only when purity is certain: after maximum duration, or after ghusl/prayer following early cessation.

This lesson clarifies the precise conditions under which intercourse becomes permissible after menstrual or postpartum bleeding stops. The Hanafi school distinguishes between three scenarios based on when the bleeding ceases relative to the maximum duration and the woman's habit. The proofs are drawn from the Quran, hadith, and statements of early authorities (tābi‘ūn).

Guided Path
1
Understand the general prohibition during hayd
Recognize that intercourse is haram during active bleeding (hayd/nifas); only intimacy above the izār is allowed based on hadith.
The prohibition is based on Quran 2:222.
2
Identify Scenario 1: Blood stops at maximum duration
If blood ceases at the maximum of hayd (10 days) or nifas (40 days), the woman is definitively pure and intercourse is permissible even without ghusl.
Certainty of purity removes the need for ghusl.
3
Identify Scenario 2: Blood stops before completing habit or before maximum
If cessation occurs before her usual habit or after habit but before maximum, purity is not certain; she must perform ghusl (or tayammum if unable) and pray one prayer before intercourse.
Ghusl and prayer are required to establish purity.
4
Identify Scenario 3: A prayer becomes qada on the woman
If after cessation, she has enough time for ghusl and takbīr tahrimah but neglects to do so, and the prayer time passes, the prayer becomes a debt (qada) on her, which indicates purity and makes intercourse permissible.
The obligation of prayer evidences her purity.
