ما يحرم بالحيض والنفاس
ثمرة النجاح جلد ا (۲۵۵) واذا انقطع الدم لاكثر الحيض والنفاس حل الوطئ بلا غسل . ۲۵۶ ) ولا يحل ان انقطع ہے۔ البتہ عورت کو ازار پہنا کر اسکے ساتھ لیٹ سکتا ہے۔ اسکے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ سمعت ميمونة تقول : كان رسول الله کوازار اذا اراد أن يباشر امرأة من نسائه أمر ها فاتزرت و هی حائض بخاری شریف، باب مباشرة الحائض ، ص۵۳ نمبر ۳۰۳)(۳) عن ميمونة قالت ان النبي لعل الله كان يباشر المرأة من نسائه و هي حائض اذا كان عليها ازار الى انصاف الفخذين او الركبتين تحتجز به ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الرجل یصیب منها ما دون الجماع ، ص ۴۸، نمبر ۲۶۷) ان احادیث میں ہے کہ حیض کی حالت میں ازار کے اوپر سے فائدہ اٹھا سکتا ہے۔(۴) صرف جماع حرام ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے. عـن بـعض ازواج النبي قالت ان النبي كان اذا اراد من الحائض شيئا القى على فرجها ثوبا ۔ ( ابودا وشریف، باب فی الرجل یصیب منها ما دون الجماع، ص ۴۹، نمبر۲۷۲)
ترجمه : (۲۵۵) اور جب حیض و نفاس کا خون اکثر مدت میں منقطع ہو تو بلا انسل وچلی جائز ہے۔ تشریح : مثلا حیض کی اکثر مدت دس دن ہے، اور دس دن پر خون آنا بند ہوا تو اب بغیر عورت کے نہائے ہوئے بھی وطی کرسکتا ہے، کیونکہ اب تو حیض آئے گا ہی نہیں ، اور اگر آئے گا تو وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہو گا ، اس لئے عورت یقینی طور پر پاک ہوگئی ۔ اسی طرح نفاس کی اکثر مدت چالیس روز ہے، اور چالیس روز پر خون بند ہوا تو بغیر نہائے ہوئے بھی وطی کر سکتا ہے ، کیونکہ عورت یقینی طور پر پاک ہو گئی۔ وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے کہ عورت پاک ہو جائے تو اس سے وطی کرو، اور یہ عورت یقینی طور پر پاک ہوگئی ہے اس لئے اس سے وطی کرنا جائز ہے ۔ویسئلونك عن المحيض قل هو اذى فاعتزلوا النساء في المحيض و لا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن فاذا تطهرن فأتوهن من حيث أمر كم الله ان الله يحب التوابين و يحب المتطهرين (آیت ۲۲۲،سورة البقرة ٢) (۲)۔ عن مجاهد في قوله عزوجل ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن حتى ينقطع الدم فاذا تطهرن قال يقول اذا اغتسلن (سن للبیهقی ، باب الحائض لا توحاً حتى تظهر وتغتسل ، ج اول ص ۴۶۲ نمبر ۱۴۸۲) اس اثر میں خون منقطع ہو نے کو نسل کرنا قراردیا گیا ہے اسلئے غسل نہ بھی کرے تو صحبت جائز ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۵۶) اور جب اپنی عادت کے موافق کم مدت میں خون منقطع ہو تو ولی جائز نہیں مگر یہ کہ غسل کرلے یا (غسل پر قادر نہ ہو تو ) تیم کرلے اور نماز پڑھ لے۔ تشریح : مثلا عورت کی پرانی عادت پانچ دن خون آنے کی تھی اب چار دن میں خون آنا بند ہو گیا تو ابھی یہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ ایک روز اور خون آجائے کیونکہ اس کی عادت پانچ روز کی ہے اس لئے یہ کمل پاک نہیں ہوئی اس لئے اس سے ولی کرنا جائز نہیں جب تک
لونه لتمام عادتها الا ان تغتسل او تتيمم وتصلى (۲۵۷) او تصير الصلوة دينا في ذمتها وذلك بان تجد بعد الانقطاع من الوقت الذى انقطع الدم فيه زمنا يسع الغسل والتحريمة فما فوقها ولم تغتسل کہ غسل نہ کر لے۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اپنی عادت کے مطابق پانچ روز کے بعد خون بند ہوا، لیکن دس روز سے پہلے بند ہوا تب بھی جب تک غسل نہ کرے وطی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ اس کی عادت بدل گئی ہوا اور دس دن تک خون آسکتا ہے۔۔ اب غسل کی تین صورتیں بیان کر رہے ہیں [1] غسل کر لے [۲] غنسل پر قادر نہ ہو تو غسل کا تیم کرلے اور نماز پڑھ لے تو عورت پاک سمجھی جائے گی اور اب وطی کرنا جائز ہو گا[۳] تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک نماز کی قضا ذمہ میں لازم ہو جائے تو یہ عورت پاک سمجھی جائے گی اور اس سے اب وطی کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ وجه : (ا) عن مجاهد في قوله عز وجل ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن حتى ينقطع الدم فاذا تطهرن قال يقول اذا اغتسلن (سن للمتقی ، باب الحائض لا قوطا حتى تظهر وتغتسل ، ج اول ص ۲۶۲، نمبر ۱۴۸۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ غسل کرے تب ولی جائز ہے۔ (۲) سأل انسان عطاء قال الحائض ترى الطهر ولا تغتسل اتحل لزوجها؟قال لا حتى تغتسل. (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يصيب امرأته وقد رأت العبر ولم تغتسل ج اول ص ۲۵۶، نمبر ۱۲۷۵ ر السفن للبیھقی ، باب الحائض لا توطاً حتى تظهر وتغتسل ، ج اول ص ۴۶۲، نمبر ۱۳۸۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ جب تک کہ غسل نہ کر لے ولی جائز نہیں ہے۔ (۳) اور غسل پر قادر نہ ہو تو تمیم کرے، اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے . عن عطاء قال اذا طهرت الحائض فلم تجد ماء تتيمم و يأتيها زوجها - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من قال اذا ظهرت وھی فی سفر تیم دیا تھا ، ج اول ص ۹۳ نمبر ۱۰۳۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تیم کرے۔ ترجمه : (۲۵۷) یا ایک نماز کی قضا عورت کے ذمہ لازم ہو جائے اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ خون منقطع ہونے کے بعد مثلا اتنا وقت باقی رہے کہ جس میں صرف غسل اور تحریمہ یا اس سے زیادہ ادا کر سکتی ہے اور اس نے غسل یا تیم نہیں کیا اور وقت نکل گیا تو اب اس سے ولی جائز ہے۔ تشریح : ولی حلال ہونے کی تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت کے ذمے ایک نماز قضا ہو جائے تو اس سے وطی حلال ہو جائے گی - [1] قضا کی ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ خون بند ہونے کے بعد نماز کا مکمل وقت گزر گیا اور عورت نے نماز نہیں پڑھی اور وہ نماز اس کے ذمے قضا ہوگئی ۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ نماز کا وقت چل رہا تھا کہ اس کے آخیر وقت میں خون بند ہوا، لیکن اتنا وقت باقی تھا کہ منسل کر کے نماز کا تحریمہ باندھ لیتی ، اور غسل پر قادر نہیں تو غسل کا تیم کر کے نماز کا تحریمہ باندھ سکتی تھی، لیکن اس نے نہ غسل کیا، نہ تیتم کیا اور نہ تحریمہ باندھا جسکی وجہ سے یہ نمازعورت پر قضارہ گئی تو اس سے وطی کرنا حلال ہو گیا۔
What is prohibited due to hayd and nifas. Thamaratun Najah vol. 1 (255) And when the blood ceases for the maximum of hayd and nifas, intercourse is permissible without ghusl. (256) And it is not permissible if it ceases... but the woman can lie with him by wearing an izār. For this there is a hadith: I heard Maymūnah say: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ, when he wanted to be intimate with one of his wives, he would tell her to put on an izār and she would, while she was menstruating. (Bukhari, chapter on direct contact with menstruating woman, p.53 no.303) (3) From Maymūnah that the Prophet ﷺ would be intimate with a woman from his wives while she was menstruating if she had an izār up to the middle of the thighs or knees covering herself. (Abu Dawud, chapter on a man having contact with her less than intercourse, p.48 no.267) In these hadiths, benefit from above the izār is permissible during menstruation. (4) Only intercourse is forbidden; its proof is this hadith: From some wives of the Prophet that when he wanted something from a menstruating woman, he would throw a cloth over her private part. (Abu Dawud, chapter on a man having contact with her less than intercourse, p.49 no.272). Translation: (255) And when the blood of hayd and nifas stops at the maximum duration, intercourse is permissible without ghusl. Explanation: For example, the maximum duration of hayd is ten days, and if the blood stops at ten days, then he can have intercourse even if the woman has not bathed, because now there will be no more hayd, and if blood comes it will be istihādah, so the woman is definitely pure. Similarly, the maximum duration of nifas is forty days, and if blood stops at forty days, he can have intercourse without bathing, because the woman is definitely pure. Wajh (proof): (1) In this verse: 'They ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation, and do not approach them until they become pure. Then when they have purified themselves, come to them from where Allah has commanded you. Indeed, Allah loves those who repent and loves those who purify themselves.' (Quran 2:222). And the woman is definitely pure, so intercourse with her is permissible. (2) From Mujāhid regarding His saying 'until they become pure': until the blood ceases; 'then when they have purified themselves' he said: 'when they have bathed.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on a menstruating woman not being approached until she becomes pure and bathes, vol.1 p.462 no.1482) In this effect, cessation of blood is considered purification, so even if she has not bathed, intercourse is permissible. Translation: (256) And when the blood stops at a duration less than her habit, intercourse is not permissible unless she performs ghusl or (if unable to use water) performs tayammum and prays. Explanation: For example, a woman's usual habit was five days of blood, now blood stops at four days. It is very possible that blood may come for another day because her habit is five days, so she is not completely pure, therefore intercourse with her is not permissible until she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays. (257) Or the prayer becomes a debt in her liability, that is, after the cessation, she finds sufficient time for ghusl and takbīr tahrimah and more, and she does not perform ghusl. The second scenario is that blood stopped after five days according to her habit, but before ten days, then also intercourse is not permissible until she performs ghusl, because it is possible that her habit changed and blood may come up to ten days. Now three scenarios of ghusl are being explained: [1] She performs ghusl, [2] if unable to perform ghusl, she performs tayammum and prays, then the woman is considered pure and intercourse becomes permissible, [3] the third scenario is that the qadā of one prayer becomes obligatory on her, then the woman is considered pure and intercourse with her becomes permissible. Wajh: (a) From Mujāhid regarding His saying 'nor approach them until they become pure' until the blood ceases, 'then when they have purified themselves' he said: 'when they have bathed.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on a menstruating woman not being approached until she becomes pure and bathes, vol.1 p.462 no.1482) In this saying of a tābi‘ī, when she bathes then intercourse is permissible. (2) A person asked ‘Atā: A menstruating woman sees purity but does not bathe: is she permissible for her husband? He said: No, until she bathes. (Musannaf ‘Abd al-Razzāq, chapter on a man having intercourse with his wife after she has seen purity and not bathed, vol.1 p.256 no.1275; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on a menstruating woman not being approached until she becomes pure and bathes, vol.1 p.462 no.1383) In this saying of a tābi‘ī, as long as she does not bathe, intercourse is not permissible. (3) And if she is unable to use water, she performs tayammum; for this there is this effect: From ‘Atā: When a menstruating woman becomes pure and does not find water, she performs tayammum and her husband may come to her. (Musannaf Ibn Abī Shaybah, chapter on those who say when she becomes pure while traveling she performs tayammum, vol.1 p.93 no.1033) In this effect, she performs tayammum. Translation: (257) Or the qadā of one prayer becomes obligatory on the woman. Its scenario: after cessation of blood, there remains enough time for ghusl and takbīr tahrimah or more, and she did not perform ghusl or tayammum, and the time passed, then intercourse with her is permissible. Explanation: The third scenario for halāl intercourse is that the woman has a qadā prayer on her, then intercourse becomes halāl. [1] One scenario of qadā: the complete time for prayer passed after blood stopped, and she did not pray, that prayer becomes qadā on her. Second scenario: the time of prayer was ongoing, and at its end blood stopped, but there was enough time that if she bathed she could make takbīr tahrimah, and if unable to bathe, she could perform tayammum and make takbīr tahrimah, but she neither bathed, nor performed tayammum, nor said takbīr, so that prayer becomes qadā on her, then intercourse with her becomes halāl.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when intercourse becomes permissible after menstruation (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas) stops, following the Hanafi school. The author presents three main scenarios. First (255): If blood stops at the maximum duration of hayd (10 days) or nifas (40 days), the woman is considered definitively pure (ṭāhir) even without ghusl, so intercourse is permissible immediately. The proof is that Allah's command to 'approach them when they have purified themselves' applies, and Mujāhid interprets 'purification' as cessation of blood. Second (256): If blood stops before completing her usual habit (e.g., habit is 5 days but stops at 4), or if it stops after the habit but before the maximum, she is not yet pure, so intercourse is forbidden until she performs ghusl (or tayammum if water unavailable) and prays one prayer. The proof from Mujāhid and ‘Atā emphasizes that ghusl is required. Third (257): If after cessation, the woman has enough time for ghusl and takbīr tahrimah but neglects to perform them, and the prayer time passes, then the prayer becomes a debt (qadā) on her, and intercourse becomes permissible. This is because the obligation of prayer indicates her purity. The text also includes hadiths allowing intimacy above the izār during hayd, and a hadith forbidding intercourse by placing a cloth over the private part. All rulings are based on Quran and Sunnah proofs, with explanations in Urdu.

Key Terms
حیض (hayḍ): Menstrual blood that occurs naturally and prevents valid prayer, fasting, and intercourse during its flow.
نفاس (nifās): Postpartum bleeding after childbirth; maximum 40 days in the Hanafi school.
استحاضة (istiḥāḍah): Irregular bleeding not counted as hayḍ or nifās; treated as chronic excuse (udhr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman has a menstrual habit of 6 days. She sees blood stop on the 4th day. According to the Hanafi ruling, when is intercourse permissible?
A) Immediately, because the blood has stopped.
B) Only after she performs ghusl or tayammum and prays one prayer.
C) Only after waiting until the maximum of 10 days.
D) After 6 days, regardless of ghusl.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse after hayd/nifas is permissible only when purity is established either by maximum duration or by ghusl/prayer (or qada).

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
When Intercourse Becomes Permissible After Menstruation
Explains three conditions for permissibility of intercourse after hayd/nifas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that make intercourse halal after hayd/nifas in the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for each condition.

Core Idea
Permissibility requires purification: ghusl, tayammum+salat, or a missed prayer becoming due.

Many assume that mere cessation of blood allows marital relations, but the Hanafi school stipulates an additional act of purification. This passage details the three conditions that transform a woman from prohibited to permissible for her husband, supported by traditions from the Successors and rational analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is marital intercourse (wat’) after the end of menstruation (hayd) or postnatal bleeding (nifas). The default ruling is prohibition (haram) until one of the stated conditions is met. The passage clarifies that merely seeing no blood is insufficient.
The ruling for intercourse during hayd is haram; after cessation, it becomes mubah (permissible) upon purification.
2
List the three conditions
The passage enumerates three conditions: (1) performing ghusl, (2) performing tayammum and then offering a prayer (if water unavailable), (3) a prayer becoming a debt (qada) on the woman because she had sufficient time to purify but did not, and the prayer time passed.
These are mutually exclusive alternatives; any one of them suffices.
3
Examine the evidence for each condition
For ghusl: the verse 'Do not approach them until they become pure' interpreted by Mujahid as 'when they perform ghusl'. For tayammum: a tradition from ‘Ata allowing tayammum for the menstruating woman who cannot find water. For the third condition: a tradition from Mujahid: 'Do not approach her until prayer becomes permissible for her', and rational analogy: when Allah’s obligation (prayer) is due, the husband’s right also becomes due.
The proofs are from the Successors (mawquf and mursal narrations), considered valid in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi‘i) require ghusl only after complete cessation; they do not accept the third condition of a prayer becoming due. The difference stems from interpreting the verse and the weight given to the actions of the Salaf.
The Hanafi school considers the third condition a valid sign of purity because the prayer obligation confirms that the woman was able to purify herself.
5
Understand the rationale for the third condition
The third condition uses the legal principle that once a divine obligation (prayer) becomes binding on her as a debt, it indicates that she was mandated to purify herself; by neglecting it, she has effectively delayed purification, but the marital right nevertheless becomes due.
This is unique to the Hanafi school and relies on rational analogy (qiyas).

(مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يصيب امرأته وقد رأت العبر ولم تغتسل ج اول ص ۲۵۶، نمبر ۱۲۷۵ ر السفن للبیھقی ، باب الحائض لا توطاً حتى تظهر وتغتسل ، ج اول ص ۴۶۲، نمبر ۱۳۸۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ جب تک کہ غسل نہ کر لے ولی جائز نہیں ہے۔ (۳) اور غسل پر قادر نہ ہو تو تیم کرے، اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے . عن عطاء قال اذا طهرت الحائض فلم تجد ماء تتيمم و يأتيها زوجها - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من قال اذا ظهرت وھی فی سفر تیم دیا تھا ، ج اول ص ۹۳ نمبر ۱۰۳۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تیم کرے۔ ترجمه : (۲۵۷) یا ایک نماز کی قضا عورت کے ذمہ لازم ہو جائے اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ خون منقطع ہونے کے بعد مثلا اتنا وقت باقی رہے کہ جس میں صرف غسل اور تحریمہ یا اس سے زیادہ ادا کر سکتی ہے اور اس نے غسل یا تیم نہیں کیا اور وقت نکل گیا تو اب اس سے ولی جائز ہے۔ تشریح : ولی حلال ہونے کی تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت کے ذمے ایک نماز قضا ہو جائے تو اس سے وطی حلال ہو جائے گی - [1] قضا کی ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ خون بند ہونے کے بعد نماز کا مکمل وقت گزر گیا اور عورت نے نماز نہیں پڑھی اور وہ نماز اس کے ذمے قضا ہوگئی ۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ نماز کا وقت چل رہا تھا کہ اس کے آخیر وقت میں خون بند ہوا، لیکن اتنا وقت باقی تھا کہ غسل کر کے نماز کا تحریمہ باندھ لیتی ، اور غسل پر قادر نہیں تو غسل کا تیم کر کے نماز کا تحریمہ باندھ سکتی تھی، لیکن اس نے نہ غسل کیا، نہ تیم کیا اور نہ تحریمہ باندھا جسکی وجہ سے یہ نماز عورت پر قضا رہ گئی تو اس سے وطی کرنا حلال ہو گیا۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن مجاهد في الحائض ينقطع عنها الدم قال لا يأتيها حتى تحل لها الصلوۃ ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب في المرأة منقطع عنها الدم فيا تيها قبل ان تغتسل ، ج اول ص ۹۲ نمبر ۱۰۲۷) اس اثر میں ہے که نماز ذمے میں آئے تب وطی حلال ہوگی ۔ (۲) اس کی دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ جب اللہ کا فرض اس کے ذمے ہو گیا تو انسان کا فرض [ وطی ] بھی اس کے ذمے آجائے گا۔۔ اس کے لئے کوئی اثر نہیں ملا۔
What becomes prohibited by menstruation and postnatal bleeding... except that she performs ghusl, or performs tayammum and prays, or the prayer becomes a debt in her responsibility. That is by finding after the cessation, from the time in which the blood stopped, a period that accommodates ghusl and takbirat al-ihram and more, and she did not perform ghusl. Second scenario: Blood stopped after five days according to her habit but before ten days; even then, until she performs ghusl, intercourse is not permissible. Three forms of ghusl: (1) performs ghusl; (2) if unable to perform ghusl, performs tayammum and prays; then the woman is considered pure; (3) one prayer becomes obligatory in her responsibility. Proof: (1) From Mujahid regarding the verse 'Do not approach them until they become pure'... he said 'when they perform ghusl'. (2) A person asked 'Ata': 'The menstruating woman sees purity but does not perform ghusl, is she permissible for her husband?' He said 'No, until she performs ghusl.' (3) For tayammum: From 'Ata' who said: 'When the menstruating woman becomes pure and cannot find water, she performs tayammum and her husband comes to her.' Translation of (257): Or one prayer becomes due in her responsibility; the scenario is that after cessation, enough time remains for ghusl and takbirat al-ihram, but she neither performed ghusl nor tayammum, and the time passed, then intercourse becomes permissible. Explanation: Third scenario: one prayer becomes qada' on the woman. Two forms: (a) the entire prayer time passed after cessation without prayer; (b) at the end of the time, blood stopped and there was enough time for ghusl and takbir, but she did not do so, causing the prayer to become qada'. Proof for third scenario: (1) From Mujahid: 'The menstruating woman whose blood stops – he said: Do not approach her until prayer becomes permissible for her.' (2) Rational proof: When Allah's obligation becomes due, the human obligation [intercourse] also becomes due. No tradition was found for this.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on when intercourse becomes permissible for a woman after her menstrual or postnatal bleeding has ceased. It emphasizes that mere cessation of blood is not sufficient; one of three conditions must be met. The first condition is performing ghusl (ritual bath). The second condition applies if water is unavailable or harmful: performing tayammum (dry ablution) and then offering a prayer, which establishes her purity. The third condition, unique to the Hanafi school, arises if she neglects to perform ghusl or tayammum despite having enough time, causing a prayer to become a debt (qada') on her; at that point, intercourse becomes permissible even without purification. The author supports these rulings with athar (traditions) from the tabi‘een (Successors), such as Mujahid and 'Ata, and also employs rational reasoning for the third condition: once a divine obligation (the missed prayer) becomes due, the marital right (intercourse) also becomes due. This episode clarifies that the ruling is not based on mere physical purity but on the completion of ritual obligations.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual full-body washing required after menstruation or postnatal bleeding to become pure.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth when water is unavailable or harmful, substituting for ghusl.
قضا (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its time has expired; here, it becomes a debt (dayn) on the woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for intercourse to become permissible after menstruation in the Hanafi school?
A) She performs ghusl
B) She performs tayammum and prays
C) She has a missed prayer become due on her
D) She waits one complete day after blood stops

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, marital intercourse after menstruation is not permissible until one of three conditions is fulfilled: ghusl, tayammum+salat, or a prayer becoming qada.

Menstruating Woman: Make Up Fasts, Not Prayers
States ruling with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a woman who misses fasts and prayers due to menstruation or postpartum bleeding, and explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha (RA).

Core Idea
A menstruating woman must make up missed fasts but not prayers – the command is limited.

This lesson addresses a common question: what acts of worship must a woman make up after her period? The answer is clear: fasts are made up, prayers are not. The proof is a direct statement from Aisha (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) commanded only the make-up of fasts. This ruling is based on ease and is unanimously accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the exact ruling: a woman who misses fasts due to hayd/nifas must perform qada' for those fasts, but she does not need to make up missed prayers.
The ruling applies to both menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Mu‘adhah who asked Aisha (RA). Aisha replied that women were commanded to make up fasts but not prayers.
Hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'we were commanded... and not commanded' indicates that the command (amr) for fasting is explicit, while the absence of a command for prayers implies it is not required.
In usul, lack of command indicates non-obligation.
4
Note the reason (hikmah)
The commentary mentions hardship: ten days of missed prayers (approx 50 prayers) would be burdensome, whereas fasts are only a few days.
This is not the primary cause but a wisdom underlying the ruling.
5
Confirm consensus
All major schools (Hanafi, Shafi‘i, Maliki, Hanbali) agree on this ruling. It is muttafaq alayh.
No valid ikhtilaf exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقضى الحائض والنفساء الصوم دون الصلوة. تشریح : دس روز میں نماز پچاس ہو جائے گی اس لئے نماز کی قضا نہ کرے، اور روزہ صرف دس ہی ہونگے اس لئے روزے کی قضا کرے۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بعد میں نماز کی قضا نہ کرے صرف روزے کی قضا کرے ۔عن معاذة قالت سألت عائشة فقلت ما بال الحائض تقضى الصوم ولا تقضى الصلوة؟ فقالت احرورية انت؟ قلت لست بحرورية ولكنى اسأل قـالـت كـان يصيبنا ذلك فنؤمر بقضاء الصوم ولا نؤمر بقضاء الصلوۃ۔ (مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب قضاء الصوم على الحائض دون الصلوۃ ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۳۳۵ /۷۶۳ بخاری شریف، باب لا تقضى الحائض الصلوۃ ص ۵۶ نمبر ۳۲۱)
And the menstruating and postpartum woman makes up the fast and not the prayer. Explanation: In ten days, prayer becomes fifty, so she does not make up prayer; fasting is only ten, so she makes up fasting. Proof: In this hadith: from Mu‘adhah that she asked ‘A'ishah, 'Why does the menstruating woman make up the fast and not the prayer?' She said, 'Are you a Haruriyyah? I am not a Haruriyyah, but I ask.' She said, 'That used to happen to us, and we were commanded to make up the fast and not commanded to make up the prayer.'
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This short lesson provides the ruling that a woman who misses fasts due to menstruation (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas) must make them up later (qada'), but she does not have to make up missed prayers. The reason given in the commentary is that the number of prayers missed (e.g., five daily prayers over ten days = fifty) is large and would cause hardship, whereas fasts are only a few (ten days). The proof is the well-known hadith of ‘A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) reported by Mu‘adhah, which states that during the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) women were commanded to make up fasts but not prayers. This ruling is unanimous among the schools, based on this hadith.

Key Terms
قضاء الصوم (qada' al-sawm): Making up missed fasts after Ramadan due to menstruation or postpartum bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Aisha (RA), what were menstruating women commanded to do?
A) Make up both fasts and prayers.
B) Make up fasts only.
C) Make up prayers only.
D) Make up neither.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating or postpartum woman must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers, based on the explicit command of the Prophet (SAW).

Five Prohibitions for a Junub
Lists the five actions prohibited in a state of janabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five actions prohibited for a junub and explain the rationale based on the state of major impurity.

Core Idea
A junub cannot pray, recite the Qur'an, touch it directly, enter a mosque, or perform tawaf.

This lesson presents the five actions that become forbidden (haram) when a person is in a state of janabah (major ritual impurity). These prohibitions apply equally to a menstruating woman (ha'id) and a postpartum woman (nufasa'). Memorizing these helps maintain the sanctity of worship and the Qur'an. The Hanafi school holds these prohibitions strictly; other schools may allow recitation or touching with a barrier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the state of janabah
Understand what causes janabah (sexual intercourse or ejaculation) and that it requires ghusl. The junub is in a state of major impurity.
This ruling also applies to ha'id and nufasa' as the source commentary notes.
2
Enumerate the five prohibitions
Memorize the list: (1) performing any salah, (2) reciting any verse of the Qur'an, (3) touching the mushaf without a cover, (4) entering a mosque, (5) performing tawaf.
The order in the matn is standard in Hanafi texts.
3
Recognize the underlying principle
These acts require ritual purity (taharah). Janabah removes that purity, so they become invalid and sinful if performed.
The junub is in the same rank as the menstruating woman.
4
Apply the exception for touching
The text says 'except with a cover' (illa bi-ghilaf). Touching the mushaf through a barrier (cloth, box) is permitted. Direct touch is prohibited.
Some later Hanafis allow recitation of short verses for blessing if not intended as tilawah, but the relied-upon view is complete prohibition.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
The Shafi'i school permits the junub to recite Qur'an (without touching the mushaf). The Hanafi school strictly prohibits it. Compare the evidence.
This ikhtilaf is mentioned in the analytical toolbox.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحرم بالجنابة خمسة اشياء .) (۲۵۹) الصلوة وقراءة آية من القرآن ومسها الا بغلاف ودخول مسجد والطواف . ترجمه : (۲۵۹) جنبی کے لئے یہ پانچ چیزیں حرام ہیں [1] نماز پڑھنا، [۲] قرآن کی ایک آیت کی بھی تلاوت کرنا، [۳] قرآن کو بغیر غلاف کے چھونا، [۴] مسجد میں داخل ہونا [۵] بیت اللہ کا طواف کرنا۔ تشریح : جنبی ناپاک ہے، اور حائضہ اور نفساء کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے جو باتیں انکے لئے ممنوع ہیں اس کے لئے بھی
And five things are prohibited by major impurity (janabah): (259) prayer, reciting a verse of the Qur'an, touching it except with a cover, entering a mosque, and tawaf. Translation: For a junub, these five things are forbidden: [1] praying, [2] reciting even one verse of the Qur'an, [3] touching the Qur'an without a cover, [4] entering a mosque, [5] performing tawaf of the House of Allah. Explanation: A junub is impure and is in the same rank as the menstruating and postpartum woman, so what is prohibited for them is also prohibited for him/her.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage enumerates five actions that are prohibited (haram) for a person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah), which includes a junub (one who has had sexual intercourse or ejaculation without bathing), as well as a menstruating or postpartum woman. The five are: (1) performing any prayer (salah), (2) reciting any verse of the Qur'an (even a single ayah), (3) touching the Qur'an without a wrapper or covering (the Arabic mushaf itself is sacred and must be touched with purity), (4) entering a mosque (masjid), and (5) performing tawaf around the Ka'bah. The explanation notes that the junub shares the same prohibitions as a menstruating woman (ha'id) and postpartum woman (nufasa') because all are in a state of major impurity requiring ghusl for purification.

Key Terms
جنابة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, caused by sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
مسها الا بغلاف (massuha illa bighilaf): Touching the physical mushaf (Qur'an) except via a covering (like a cloth or box).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which act is permitted for a junub?
A) Reciting the Fatihah during prayer.
B) Touching the Qur'an through a covering.
C) Entering a mosque to attend a lesson.
D) Performing tawaf for 'umrah.

Key Takeaway
The five prohibitions for a junub are derived from the requirement of ritual purity and apply equally to menstruating and postpartum women.

Ruling on Qada for Menstruating Woman
Ruling with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a menstruating woman must make up missed fasts but not prayers, and cite the hadith evidence from Aisha.

Core Idea
Menstruating women make up fasts, not prayers—a mercy from explicit command.

This lesson addresses a common question: what acts of worship must a menstruating woman compensate? The Hanafi school, supported by a clear hadith, distinguishes between prayer and fasting. Understanding this ruling clarifies the role of textual evidence in determining legal obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the ruling: a menstruating woman (haa'id) and postpartum woman (nafsaa') must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers. Note that this applies to both conditions.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the hadith quoted in the passage: Mu'adhah's narration from Aisha (RA). Aisha explicitly states that they were commanded to make up fasts and not prayers.
The hadith is authentic, reported in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the reasoning behind the distinction
The passage also mentions a rational explanation: the number of missed prayers is large (e.g., 50 in 10 days) while fasts are few (10), making prayer qada burdensome. However, the primary basis is the textual command.
The ruling is ta'abbudi (based on divine command), not merely rational.
4
Note the madhhab status
This is the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi). Some earlier scholars held that she must make up prayers, but the Hanafi school follows the authentic hadith.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih, but the Hanafi view is strongly supported.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقضى الحائض والنفساء الصوم دون الصلوة.

ترجمه: (۲۵۸) اور حائض اور نفسا صرف روزے کی قضا کرے نماز کی نہیں۔
تشریح: دس روز میں نماز پچاس ہو جائے گی اس لئے نماز کی قضا نہ کرے، اور روزہ صرف دس ہی ہونگے اس لئے روزے کی قضا کرے۔

وجه: اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بعد میں نماز کی قضا نہ کرے صرف روزے کی قضا کرے۔ عن معاذة قالت سألت عائشة فقلت ما بال الحائض تقضى الصوم ولا تقضى الصلوة؟ فقالت احرورية انت؟ قلت لست بحرورية ولكنى اسأل قالت كان يصيبنا ذلك فنؤمر بقضاء الصوم ولا نؤمر بقضاء الصلوة۔ (مسلم شریف، باب وجوب قضاء الصوم على الحائض دون الصلوة ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۳۳۵ /۷۶۳ بخاری شریف، باب لا تقضى الحائض الصلوة ص ۵۶ نمبر ۳۲۱)
And the menstruating woman and the woman with postpartum bleeding must make up the fast but not the prayer.

Translation (258): And the menstruating and postpartum woman shall only make up the fast, not the prayer.
Explanation: In ten days, prayers become fifty, so she does not make up the prayer, and fasts are only ten, so she makes up the fast.

Evidence: In this hadith, that later she does not make up the prayer, only the fast. From Mu'adhah: She said, I asked Aisha, 'Why does the menstruating woman make up the fast and not the prayer?' She said, 'Are you a Haruriyyah?' I said, 'I am not a Haruriyyah, but I am asking.' She said, 'That used to happen to us, and we were commanded to make up the fast and not commanded to make up the prayer.' (Muslim, chapter on obligation of qada of fast for menstruating woman not prayer, p. 149 no. 335/763; Bukhari, chapter on menstruating woman does not make up prayer, p. 56 no. 321)
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage states a ruling for menstruating and postpartum women: they must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers. The explanation clarifies that in a typical ten-day period, the number of prayers missed (fifty) would be excessive to make up, while fasts are only ten. The evidence is a hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) affirming this practice. This is a standard Hanafi position based on the Sunnah and ease.

Key Terms
حائض (haa'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding within the menstrual period.
نفساء (nafsaa'): A woman experiencing postpartum bleeding after childbirth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling that a menstruating woman does not make up missed prayers?
A) Quran verse 2:184
B) Hadith of Aisha (RA)
C) Qiyas on fasting
D) Ijma of the companions

Key Takeaway
The menstruating woman's exemption from making up missed prayers is based on an explicit hadith, not merely on hardship.

Five Prohibitions for the Junub
Enumerating five acts prohibited for one in major ritual impurity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five acts prohibited for a person in a state of janabah and cite the primary evidence for each prohibition.

Core Idea
A junub must avoid prayer, Quran recitation, touching the Quran, entering mosque, and tawaf until ghusl.

This lesson presents five clear prohibitions for the state of major ritual impurity (janabah) as taught in the Hanafi school. Understanding these prohibitions is essential for every Muslim to maintain proper ritual purity and avoid sin. The rulings are derived from the Quran, Sunnah, and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Define the state of janabah
Identify who is considered junub (a person in major ritual impurity requiring ghusl). This state applies to both men and women after sexual intercourse, ejaculation, or menstruation/postpartum bleeding.
The junub is impure until ghusl is performed.
2
List the five prohibited acts
Memorize the five specific actions that become haram for the junub: (1) offering salah, (2) reciting any verse of the Quran, (3) touching the Quran without a cover, (4) entering a mosque, (5) performing tawaf.
These are all prohibited regardless of intention.
3
Understand the rationale
The junub is equated with the menstruating woman in terms of impurity; thus the same prohibitions apply. The evidence is based on Quran (4:43) and ahadith.
The prohibition is due to the state of impurity, not the act itself.
4
Note the exception for touching Quran
Touching the Quran is only prohibited when there is no covering (ghilaf). If the Quran is held with a cover, it is permitted.
The cover can be a cloth, box, or any barrier.
5
Connect to evidence
The Quranic verse (4:43) forbids approaching prayer while junub, interpreted as entering the mosque. The hadith from Ibn Umar explicitly prohibits recitation for the junub and menstruating woman. The hadith from Aisha prohibits entering the mosque.
These proofs establish the rulings definitively.

ويحرم بالجنابة خمسة اشياء .

(۲۵۹) الصلوة وقراءة آية من القرآن ومسها الا بغلاف ودخول مسجد والطواف .

ترجمه: (۲۵۹) جنبی کے لئے یہ پانچ چیزیں حرام ہیں [1] نماز پڑھنا، [۲] قرآن کی ایک آیت کی بھی تلاوت کرنا، [۳] قرآن کو بغیر غلاف کے چھونا، [۴] مسجد میں داخل ہونا [۵] بیت اللہ کا طواف کرنا۔

تشریح: جنبی ناپاک ہے، اور حائضہ اور نفساء کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے جو باتیں انکے لئے ممنوع ہیں اس کے لئے بھی ممنوع ہوں گیں۔ دلائل حیض کی بحث میں گزر چکی۔

وجه: (ا) عن ابن عمر عن النبي عله قال لا تقرء الحائض ولا الجنب شيئا من القرآن . (ترمذى شريف، باب ما جاء فی الجنب والحائض لا يقرا القرآن ، ص ۳۶ نمبر ۱۳۱ رابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الجنب يقرا القرآن ،ص۳۴، نمبر ۲۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنبی کچھ بھی قرآن نہ پڑھے۔ (۲) آیت میں ہے۔ یایھا الذین آمنوا لا تـقـربـوا الصلوة و انتم سكرى حتى تعلموا ما تقولون ولا جنباً الا عابرى سبیل حتی تغتسلوا ( آیت ۴۳ ،سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جنبی نماز یعنی مسجد کے قریب نہ جائے ۔ (۳) سمعت عائشة ... فقال وجهوا هذه البيوت عن المسجد فاني لا احل المسجد لحائض ولا جنب - ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الحب يدخل المسجد، ص ۱۳۴، نمبر ۲۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنبی مسجد میں داخل نہ ہو۔
And five things are prohibited due to janabah.

(259) Prayer, reciting a verse of the Quran, touching it except with a covering, entering a mosque, and tawaf.

Translation (259): For the junub, these five things are haram: [1] offering prayer, [2] reciting even one verse of the Quran, [3] touching the Quran without a covering, [4] entering a mosque, [5] performing tawaf of the Kaaba.

Explanation: The junub is impure and is in the same grade as the menstruating and postpartum woman, so whatever is prohibited for them is also prohibited for him. The proofs have passed in the discussion of menstruation.

Evidence: (1) From Ibn Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Neither the menstruating woman nor the junub should recite anything of the Quran.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on junub and menstruating woman not reciting Quran, p. 36 no. 131; Abu Dawud, chapter on junub reciting Quran, p. 34 no. 229) This hadith states that the junub should not recite any Quran. (2) In the verse: 'O you who believe, do not approach prayer while you are drunk until you know what you are saying, nor while you are junub except as travelers until you have washed [ghusl].' (4:43) This verse says that the junub should not approach prayer i.e. the mosque. (3) I heard Aisha... she said: 'Direct these houses away from the mosque, for I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman or a junub.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the junub entering the mosque, p. 134 no. 232) This hadith says that the junub should not enter the mosque.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage lists five prohibitions for a person in a state of janabah (major ritual impurity). The rulings are: (1) performing salah, (2) reciting any verse of the Quran, (3) touching the Quran without a cover, (4) entering a mosque, (5) performing tawaf. The explanation links the junub's status to that of a menstruating woman. The provided proofs include: a hadith prohibiting recitation, a Quranic verse prohibiting approaching the mosque while junub, and a hadith prohibiting entry into the mosque. These are established prohibitions in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
مس المصحف (mass al-mushaf): Touching the physical copy of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT prohibited for a junub according to this passage?
A) Reciting a verse of the Quran
B) Touching the Quran with a cover
C) Entering a mosque
D) Performing tawaf

Key Takeaway
A junub must abstain from prayer, Quran recitation, touching the Quran, entering mosques, and tawaf until ghusl is performed.

Prohibitions for a Person in Hadath
Prohibitions for one in minor impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three acts prohibited for a person in hadath and identify which acts remain permissible.

Core Idea
A person without wudu cannot pray, perform tawaf, or touch the Quran without a cover.

This lesson focuses on the first ruling in our passage: the restrictions for someone in a state of minor impurity (hadath). Understanding what becomes forbidden and what remains allowed is essential for daily worship practices like prayer, tawaf, and handling the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the state of hadath
Recognize that 'hadath' here refers to the state of having no wudu (minor ritual impurity). A person in this state is called a muhdith.
2
List the three prohibitions
State the three acts that become haram: salah (prayer), tawaf (circumambulation of the Kaaba), and touching the Quran without a covering (ghilaf).
The prohibition for touching the Quran includes any physical contact with the text itself, even with the hand.
3
Note the exception for touching the Quran
Touching the Quran with a covering (e.g., a cloth or bag) is permissible. The prohibition is on direct contact.
4
Recognize what remains permissible
Reciting the Quran from memory and entering the mosque are allowed for a muhdith. The passage explicitly mentions these as exceptions.
Performing wudu removes the prohibition, so these acts become valid again.

ويحرم على المحدث ثلاثة اشياء . الصلوة، والطواف، ومسُ المصحف الا بغلاف

(۲۶۱) ودم الاستحاضه كرعاف دائم لا يمنع صلوة ولا صوما ولا وطئا.

ترجمه: (۲۶۰) اور بلا وضو والے پر تین چیزیں حرام ہیں [۱] نماز ، [۲] طواف ، [۳] قرآن مجید کا بغیر غلاف کے چھونا۔
تشریح: جو آدمی بغیر وضو کے ہو اس کے لئے نماز پڑھنا جائز نہیں بیت اللہ کا طواف کرنا جائز نہیں اور بغیر غلاف کے قرآن چھونا جائز نہیں ہے۔ البتہ قرآن کا پڑھنا جائز ہے، اور مسجد میں داخل ہونا جائز ہے۔ دلائل باب الوضو میں گزر چکے ہیں۔

ترجمه: (۲۶۱) اور استحاضہ کا خون نکسیر دائم کی طرح ہے نماز و روزہ و وطی کو منع نہیں کرتا۔
تشریح: شرمگاہ کے اندر خاص قسم کی جھلی ہوتی ہے جس سے ہر ماہ میں خون آتا ہے وہ خون حیض کا خون ہے، اور اس جھلی کے علاوہ جوخون آتا ہے وہ استحاضہ کا خون ہے، اس کا حکم نکسیر پھوٹنے کی طرح ہے، اس وقت نماز پڑھے، روزہ رکھے، اور وطی بھی کرے

وجه: (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة انها قالت قالت فاطمة بنت ابى حبيش لرسول الله عله يا رسول الله اني لا اطهر؟ افادع الصلوة فقال رسول الله الله انما ذلك عرق وليس بالحيضة فاذا اقبلت الحيضة
And three things are prohibited for the one in hadath: prayer, tawaf, and touching the Quran except with a covering.

(261) And the blood of istihadah is like a continuous nosebleed; it does not prevent prayer, nor fasting, nor intercourse.

Translation (260): And for the one without wudu, three things are haram: [1] prayer, [2] tawaf, [3] touching the Quran without a cover.
Explanation: A person who is without wudu may not pray, may not perform tawaf, and may not touch the Quran without a cover. However, reciting the Quran is permissible, and entering the mosque is permissible. The proofs have passed in the chapter of wudu.

Translation (261): And the blood of istihadah is like a persistent nosebleed; it does not prevent prayer, nor fasting, nor intercourse.
Explanation: Inside the private part there is a specific membrane from which blood comes every month—that is menstrual blood. And blood that comes from elsewhere is istihadah blood. Its ruling is like a nosebleed. At that time, she may pray, keep fast, and have intercourse.

Evidence: (1) In the hadith: From Aisha that Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh said to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), 'O Messenger of Allah, I do not become pure; should I abandon prayer?' He said, 'That is only a vein, not menstruation. When the menstruation comes...'
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First, for a person in a state of minor impurity (hadath, i.e., without wudu), three acts are prohibited: performing salah, performing tawaf, and touching the Quran without a covering. However, reciting the Quran and entering the mosque are allowed. The evidence is from the wudu section. Second, it discusses istihadah (non-menstrual vaginal bleeding). This blood is likened to a continuous nosebleed; it does not affect the validity of prayer, fasting, or marital relations. The woman should continue her worship and intercourse as normal. The proof is the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh where the Prophet explained it is from a vein, not menstruation.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdith): A person without wudu (minor ritual impurity).
حدث (hadath): Minor ritual impurity that requires wudu to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is permissible for a person in hadath (without wudu)?
A) Performing salah
B) Performing tawaf
C) Touching the Quran without a cover
D) Reciting the Quran from memory

Key Takeaway
A person in hadath is prohibited from prayer, tawaf, and touching the Quran without a cover; recitation and mosque entry are allowed.

Ruling on Istihadah (Non-Menstrual Bleeding)
Ruling on istihadah blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on istihadah blood and explain why it does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse.

Core Idea
Istihadah blood is like a continuous nosebleed; it does not affect any worship or marital relations.

This lesson covers the second ruling in our passage: the legal status of istihadah (bleeding from a vein, not menstruation). The text compares it to a persistent nosebleed, emphasizing that it does not prevent any acts of worship or intimacy. This distinction is crucial for women who experience prolonged bleeding.

Guided Path
1
Understand what istihadah is
Istihadah is vaginal bleeding that comes from a vein, not from the menstrual uterus. It is not considered hayd (menstruation).
The passage mentions a specific membrane; the point is istihadah has a different source.
2
Identify the analogy used
The text likens istihadah to a continuous nosebleed (ru'af da'im). Just as a nosebleed does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse, neither does istihadah.
This analogy helps to convey that istihadah is not a purity-impairing condition.
3
State the three acts not prevented
The passage explicitly says it does not prevent salah, sawm (fasting), or wat' (intercourse). These remain permissible during istihadah.
Some scholars include tawaf and Quran handling; the passage focuses on these three.
4
Recognize the prophetic evidence
The passage quotes the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'It is only a vein, not menstruation'.
This hadith is the primary evidence for the ruling.

Three Prohibitions for One in Impurity
States three prohibitions and provides three proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibitions for a person in minor or major impurity according to the Hanafi school and identify the dalil for each prohibition.

Core Idea
Prayer, tawaf, and touching the Quran without a wrapper are prohibited for one in impurity.

This lesson examines three key prohibitions that apply when a person lacks ritual purity. The text presents a concise ruling listing prayer, circumambulation of the Kaaba, and handling the Quran without a cover as forbidden. The author then provides scriptural evidence from the Quran and Sunnah to support these rulings, demonstrating how the Hanafi school derives these obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the three items: salah (prayer), tawaf (circumambulation), and mass al-mushaf (touching the physical Quran). Note that the ruling is haram/invalid.
The heading says 'janabah' but the matn uses 'al-muhdith' which includes minor impurity.
2
Locate the dalil for each prohibition
Find the three proofs cited: hadith from Ibn Umar (recitation forbidden for junub), Quran 4:43 (do not approach salah in janabah), and hadith from Aisha (mosque forbidden for junub).
Touching the Quran is derived via qiyas from the first hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof establishes the prohibition. For example, the Ibn Umar hadith explicitly prohibits recitation; by analogy, touching is also prohibited as a means to prevent recitation and out of respect.
4
Note the scope: minor vs major impurity
The text uses 'al-muhdith' but proofs address janabah. For minor impurity, the same three prohibitions apply except recitation is allowed.
This is a key Hanafi distinction.
5
Identify the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Contrast with Shafi'i: they permit touching the Quran for one without wudu (only janabah prohibits touching).
The Hanafi position includes minor impurity, based on a hadith that 'None touches the Quran but the purified.'

What is forbidden due to major impurity: (260) And it is forbidden for the one in a state of impurity three things: prayer, tawaf, and touching the mus-haf except with a cover. (261) And the blood of istihadah is like a continuous nosebleed; it does not prevent prayer, fasting, nor intercourse. They are prohibited. The proofs have passed in the discussion of hayd. May Allah bless him and grant him peace. Evidence: (1) From Ibn Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite anything from the Quran. (Tirmidhi, chapter on junub and menstruating woman not reciting Quran, p.36, no.131; Abu Dawood, chapter on junub reciting Quran, p.34, no.229) This hadith states that the junub should not recite any Quran. (2) In the verse: O you who believe! Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated until you know what you say, nor in a state of janabah except passing through until you have bathed (Surah an-Nisa 4:43). This verse states that the junub should not approach the mosque. (3) I heard Aisha... she said: Direct these houses away from the mosque, for I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman nor a junub. (Abu Dawood, chapter on the junub entering the mosque, p.134, no.232) This hadith states that the junub should not enter the mosque. And for the one without wudu, three things are forbidden: one look [into] prayer, ... tawaf, touching the Quran without a cover.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author begins by stating the heading 'What is forbidden due to janabah' and then gives a numbered ruling: (260) Three things are prohibited for a person in a state of hadath (impurity): prayer (salah), circumambulation (tawaf) of the Kaaba, and touching the mus-haf (Quran) unless it is in a cover (ghilaf). Although the heading mentions janabah (major impurity), the text says 'al-muhdith' which generally means one in minor impurity (without wudu). The commentary clarifies that for one without wudu, the same three things are forbidden. This is because the prohibition of touching the Quran is for both major and minor impurity, but recitation is only prohibited for janabah, not for minor impurity—a point not elaborated here but established elsewhere. The author then provides proofs: (a) a hadith from Ibn Umar prohibiting junub and menstruating woman from reciting Quran; (b) the verse from Surah an-Nisa 4:43 prohibiting junub from approaching the mosque for prayer; (c) a hadith from Aisha prohibiting junub and menstruating woman from entering the mosque. These proofs specifically address janabah, establishing the prohibition of recitation, entering mosque, and by extension tawaf. The commentary then reiterates in Urdu: for one without wudu, three things are haram: salah, tawaf, and touching the Quran without a cover. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
المحدث (al-muhdith): The person who is in a state of minor impurity (without wudu) or major impurity (janabah), as the commentary clarifies.
الصلوة (al-salah): The ritual prayer, which is invalid without purity.
مس المصحف (mass al-mushaf): Touching the physical copy of the Quran with bare skin.
الغلاف (al-ghilaf): A cover or wrapper that prevents direct contact with the Quran pages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT prohibited for a person in minor impurity (without wudu)?
A) Prayer (salah)
B) Tawaf of the Kaaba
C) Touching the Quran without a cover
D) Reciting the Quran from memory

Key Takeaway
The three prohibited acts for one in impurity are prayer, tawaf, and touching the Quran without a cover; recitation is prohibited only for major impurity.

Ruling on Istihadah: Like a Nosebleed, No Obstruction to Worship and Marital Relations
States the similarity of istihadah to epistaxis and its legal consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istihadah blood and explain why it does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse.

Core Idea
Istihadah blood is like a continuous nosebleed — it does not break purity or forbid worship.

This passage draws a clear analogy: just as a persistent nosebleed does not prevent a person from praying, so too does istihadah blood not prevent a woman from her religious duties or marital life. This ruling is foundational for understanding the Hanafi approach to chronic bleeding conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The passage addresses the blood of istihadah, i.e., chronic vaginal bleeding outside of menses.
Distinguish from hayd (menstrual blood) and nifas (postnatal bleeding).
2
Understand the analogy
The blood of istihadah is compared to a continuous nosebleed (ru'af da'im); both are excused conditions that do not create ritual impurity.
The analogy emphasizes that istihadah is not a hadath (ritual impurity) like menses.
3
List the three acts not prevented
The text mentions prayer, fasting, and sexual intercourse; none are prohibited due to istihadah.
This is the core takeaway for memorization.
4
Note the implication
Since istihadah does not prevent these acts, it does not require ghusl or invalidate wudu (per other Hanafi texts, wudu is recommended for each fard prayer but not obligatory).
The passage itself does not detail wudu; that comes from other sources.
5
Recall the evidence location
The text states that the proofs have passed in the discussion of hayd, so the student should know the hadith evidence was given earlier.
For this lesson, we accept the ruling as established.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. The author presents the second ruling of this section: istihadah (chronic vaginal bleeding outside the normal menstrual period) is legally analogous to a continuous nosebleed (ru'af da'im). This means it is not considered a ritual impurity that breaks purity for prayer or requires ghusl. Consequently, it does not prevent a woman from performing prayer (salah), fasting (sawm), or engaging in sexual intercourse (wati') with her husband. The author then notes that the proofs for this ruling have already been given in the earlier discussion of hayd (menstruation), meaning the hadith evidence was provided in a previous section of the book. In the Hanafi madhhab, this is a well-established ruling: istihadah does not affect the validity of worship or marital relations, as the blood is from a vein (irq) and not menstrual blood.

Key Terms
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Chronic vaginal bleeding that is not menstrual or postnatal, often due to a vein or illness.
كرعاف دائم (ka-ru'af da'im): Like a continuous nosebleed; meaning it is excused and does not invalidate acts of worship.

Key Takeaway
Istihadah blood, like a continuous nosebleed, does not obstruct prayer, fasting, or marital relations in the Hanafi school.

Ruling for Mustahadah and Those with Chronic Excuses: Wudu for Each Fard Time
States the ruling and provides hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a mustahadah and others with chronic excuses must perform wudu at each fard prayer time and explain the proof from the hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh.

Core Idea
A mustahadah's wudu is tied to the prayer time, not the individual prayer.

This passage addresses a critical mercy in Islamic law: what happens when a Muslim cannot maintain purity due to a chronic condition. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that allows such individuals to pray without undue hardship. In this lesson, you will learn the specific obligation of wudu tied to each fard prayer time and the proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing wudu for a mustahadah or anyone with a chronic excuse (e.g., urinary incontinence). The ruling: it is wajib to perform wudu for the time of each fard prayer.
This is a mercy (rukhsah) from Allah to allow continuous prayer despite impurity.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Avoid prayer during the days of your menses, then perform ghusl and perform wudu for every prayer, even if blood drips on the mat.'
Other hadith confirm fasting and marital relations are also permitted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'perform wudu for every prayer' indicates that the wudu is linked to the prayer itself, but the Hanafi understanding is that 'every prayer' means every prayer time, because the blood is continuous.
This is supported by the principle that the time itself breaks the wudu, not the impurity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that the mustahadah must perform a separate wudu for each individual prayer, not for the entire time.
This difference leads to practical consequences in daily worship.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it is based on the ease (taysir) granted by the Sunnah and the need to avoid hardship.
The relied-upon view is that the wudu is valid until the prayer time ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(٢٦٢) وتتوضأ المستحاضة . ومن به عذر كسلس بول واستطلاق بطن لوقت كل فرض ويصلون
فاتركي الصلوة فاذا ذهب قدرها فاغسلى عنك الدم وصلی ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب الاستحاضہ ،ص۵۳، نمبر ۱۳۰۶ مسلم شریف، باب المستحاضة وغسلها وصلوا تھا ص ۱۴۷، نمبر۷۵۳/۳۳۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مستحاضہ نماز پڑھے گی ۔ (۲)

روزے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن النبی الله قال في المستحاضة يدع الصلوة ايام اقرائها التي كانت تحيض فيها ثم تغتسل وتتوضأ عند كل صلوة وتصوم وتصلى. ترندى شريف، باب ما جاء ان المستحاضة تعوضاً لكل صلوة بس ۱۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مستحاضہ نماز پڑھے اور روزہ بھی رکھے۔ (۳) شوہر وطی کرے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عكرمة قال كانت ام حبيبة تستحاض فكان زوجها يغشاها. حيض واستحاضة كى تحقيق رحم کے اندر چاروں طرف حیض کی جھلیاں ہوتی ہیں وہ بڑھتی رہتی ہیں۔ جب حیض کا زمانہ آتا ہے تو وہ کٹ کٹ کر خون کے ساتھ گرتی ہیں۔ اس لئے حیض کا خون گاڑھا اور کالا ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن رحم کی رگوں میں کوئی بیماری ہو تو حیض کے بعد بھی اس سے خون گرتا ہے۔ جس میں وہ جھلیاں نہیں ہوتی یا سرخ رنگ کا خون ہوتا ہے یا مٹیالا یا زرد رنگ کا خون ہوتا ہے، استحاضہ کا خون رحم میں خراش یا بیماری کی وجہ سے آتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۶۲) مستحاضہ اور جس کو عذر ہو مثلا سلسل بول اور دست آنے کی بیماری، وہ ہر فرض نماز کے وقت پر وضو کر کے اس سے جو چاہے فرائض و نوافل نماز پڑھے۔
تشریح : مستحاضہ عورت اور جسکو عذر ہے، جیسے مسلسل پیشاب آتا رہتا ہے، یا ہر وقت ہوا چھوٹتی رہتی ہے، یا ہر وقت پیخا نہ نکلتا رہتا ہے، اتنا وقفہ نہیں ملتا کہ وضو کر کے نماز پوری کر سکے تو وہ معذور ہے، وہ ہر نماز کے وقت وضو کرے اور اس وضو سے جتنے فرائض اور نوافل پڑھ سکے پڑھ لے، چاہے خون نکلتا رہتا ہو، اور جب نماز کا وقت ختم ہوگا تو اس عذر کی بنا پر وضوٹوٹ جائے گا ، اب دوسرے وقت کے لئے نیا وضو کرے۔

Investigation of menstruation and istihadah. (262) And the mustahadah (woman with istihadah) performs wudu, and whoever has an excuse like urinary incontinence or loose bowels, for the time of every fard (prayer) and they pray. 'Leave the prayer; then when its duration passes, wash the blood from yourself and pray.' (Bukhari, chapter on istihadah, p.53, no.1306; Muslim, chapter on mustahadah, p.147, no.753/333) From this hadith it is understood that the mustahadah will pray. (2) May Allah bless him and grant him peace. For fasting, this hadith: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding the mustahadah: 'She leaves prayer during the days of her menses that she used to menstruate, then she performs ghusl and performs wudu for every prayer, and she fasts and prays.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on mustahadah performing wudu for each prayer, p.133, no.126) This hadith states that the mustahadah prays and fasts. (3) The husband may have intercourse; the proof for this is the hadith: From `Ikrimah: Umm Habibah had istihadah and her husband had intercourse with her. (Abu Dawood, chapter on a man having intercourse with a mustahadah, p.49, no.309) This hadith states that he has intercourse with the mustahadah. Investigation of hayd and istihadah: Inside the womb, there are membranes of hayd on all sides; they keep expanding. When the time of hayd comes, they are cut and fall with the blood. Thus the blood of hayd is thick and black. But if there is an illness in the veins of the womb, blood flows even after hayd, which does not contain those membranes, or it is red, earthy, or yellow. The blood of istihadah comes due to a scratch or illness in the womb. Translation of (262): The mustahadah and whoever has an excuse, e.g., urinary incontinence or chronic diarrhea, performs wudu at the time of every fard prayer and with it prays whatever fard and nafl prayers she wishes. Explanation: The mustahadah woman and one with an excuse, like continuous urine, constant passing of wind, or continuous stool, such that she does not find enough time to perform wudu and complete the prayer - she is a ma'dhur (excused). She performs wudu for each prayer time and with that wudu she may pray as many fard and nafl as possible, even if blood continues to flow. When the prayer time ends, her wudu breaks due to the excuse, and for the next time she performs a new wudu. May Allah bless him and grant him peace. Evidence: (1) A hadith from Aisha: Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who has istihadah, so I do not become pure. Should I leave prayer? He said: No, that is (from) a vein and not menstrual blood. Avoid prayer during the days of your menses, then perform ghusl and perform wudu for every prayer, even if blood drips on the mat. (Ibn Majah, chapter on mustahadah who has counted the days of her menses, p.87, no.624; Nasa'i, chapter on istihadah, p.47, no.350; al-Daraqutni, Book of Hayd, vol.1, p.219, no.1808) (3) From these hadith it is understood that she performs wudu for every time.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins with a heading 'Investigation of hayd and istihadah', then presents the ruling (262): a woman with istihadah (mustahadah) and anyone with a chronic excuse (like urinary incontinence or constant diarrhea) should perform wudu for the time of each fard prayer and then pray any prayers they wish (both fard and nafl). The author then provides three hadith proofs: first, the hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh where the Prophet tells her to leave prayer during menstruation but to perform ghusl and wudu for each prayer during istihadah; second, a hadith confirming she can fast; third, a hadith from `Ikrimah that Umm Habibah's husband had intercourse with her while she had istihadah, proving marital relations are permissible. After the hadith, there is an Urdu explanation of the physiological difference between hayd (menstruation, thick dark blood from membranes) and istihadah (thin, yellow or red blood from a vein or illness). Then the author provides a translation and commentary in Urdu summarizing the ruling: the excused person (ma'dhur) performs wudu at each fard time, and that wudu remains valid until the time ends, even if the impurity continues. This ruling is based on the principle of 'dhururah' (necessity) and is a mercy from Allah. The authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman who experiences istihadah, i.e., chronic vaginal bleeding outside the normal menstrual period.
عذر ('udhr): An excuse; a chronic condition that prevents maintaining purity, such as urinary incontinence or constant flatulence.
لوقت كل فرض (li-waqti kulli fard): For the time of every fard prayer; meaning the wudu is tied to the prayer time, not to the individual prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mustahadah performs wudu for each fard prayer time, not for each individual prayer, and that wudu remains valid for all prayers within that time.

Rulings on the Wudu of Those with Chronic Excuses (Ma'dhur)
Explains the conditions for becoming ma'dhur, duration, and cessation of the excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a ma'dhur's wudu becomes invalid and apply the conditions for establishing, continuing, and ending the ma'dhur status.

Core Idea
The wudu of a ma'dhur breaks only when the prayer time exits — not from the chronic excuse itself.

Many assume that any occurrence of a chronic condition like continuous urine or istihadah immediately nullifies wudu. However, the Hanafi school provides a nuanced rule: the excuse itself does not break wudu during the prayer time; only the exit of that time does. This lesson unpacks the conditions for becoming a ma'dhur, the duration of the excuse, and how the status ends. We will also examine the prophetic evidence that supports this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
Extract the key statement: the wudu of a ma'dhur becomes invalid only with the exit of the prayer time (bikhuruj al-waqt). Note the exception: other unrelated hadath (e.g., passing wind) breaks wudu immediately.
The ruling is found in para (263) of the source.
2
Analyze the evidence
Examine the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish. Focus on the phrase 'توضئي لكل صلاة' (make wudu for every prayer). Explain how this indicates that the wudu remains valid for the entire prayer period and only needs renewal for the next time.
The proof relies on the implication that the chronic excuse does not break wudu within the same time.
3
Apply the conditions for ma'dhur status
List the three conditions: (1) Becoming ma'dhur – the excuse must encompass a full prayer time without a break sufficient for wudu and prayer. (2) Continuation – the excuse must appear at least once in each subsequent prayer time. (3) Cessation – a full prayer time completely free from the excuse ends the status.
These conditions are from paras (264)-(266).
4
Distinguish from other schools
Contrast with the Shafi'i position that wudu breaks with each occurrence of the excuse. Note the practical consequence (thamarah): in Hanafi, one can perform multiple prayers with one wudu; in Shafi'i, a new wudu is needed for each prayer.
This difference arises from how each school interprets the hadith.
5
Practice with a scenario
Apply the rulings: A person with continuous urine performs wudu for Dhuhr, prays, and the urine flows. Before Asr, he also passes wind. Determine when his wudu breaks and when he must renew it.
Answer: The wudu breaks immediately upon passing wind (different hadath), not from the urine; he must renew wudu for Asr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يحرم بالجنابة به ما شاء وا من الفرائض والنوافل . (۲۶۳) ويبطل وضوء المعذورين بخروج الوقت فقط . (۲۶۴) ولا يصير معذورا حتى يستوعبه العذر وقتا كاملا ليس فيه انقطاع بقدر الوضوء والصلوة . وهذا الله اس سے فرائض اور نوافل پڑھتی رہے چاہے خون چٹائی پر گرتار ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال فی المستحاضة يدع الصلوة ايام اقرائها التي كانت تحيض فيها ثم تغتسل وتتوضأ عند كل صلوة وتصوم و تصلی. ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء ان المستحاضة تخوضاً لكل صلوۃ ص۳۳ نمبر ۱۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مستحاضہ ہر نماز کے لئے وضو کرے۔ لغت : مسلسل البول : ہر وقت پیشاب نکلتا ہو۔ استطلاق بطن طلق کا معنی ہے چلنا ، اور استطلاق بطن: کا ترجمہ ہے ہر وقت پیخانہ نکلتے رہنا۔ ترجمه : (۲۶۳) اور معذوروں کا وضو باطل ہو گا صرف وقت نکلنے سے۔ تشریح : عذر کے علاوہ کوئی اور حدث پیش آئے تو اس سے وضو ٹوٹے گا، مثلا سلسل البول والے کو حدث ہو جائے تو اس حدث سے وضو ٹوٹے گا لیکن پیشاب نکلنے سے وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا، جب نماز کا وقت ختم ہو جائے گا تب پیشاب نکلنے سے وضوٹوٹے گا۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت جاءت فاطمة بنت أبي حبيش الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت يا رسول الله اني امرأة أسـتـحـاض فلا اطهر أفادع الصلاة ؟ قال : لا انما ذالك عرق و ليس بالحيضة اجتنبى الصلاة أيام محیضک ثم اغتسلی و توضئی لكل صلاة و ان قطر الدم على الحصير ( ابن ماجۃ شریف، باب ما جاء في المستحاضة التي قد عدت أيام اقرائها، ص ۸۸ نمبر۶۲۴ رنسائی شریف ، باب ذکر الاستحاضہ واقبال الدم واد بارہ ،ص ۴۷ ،نمبر ۳۵۰ / دار قطنی ، کتاب الحیض ، ج اول ص ۲۱۹ نمبر (۸۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ چٹائی پر خون گرے تب بھی وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا، اور توضئي لكل صلاة ، سے اشارہ ہے کہ نماز کا پورا وقت نکلے گا تب اس عذر سے وضو ٹوٹے گا۔ ترجمه : (۲۶۴) معذور نہیں ہو گا یہاں تک کہ عذر پورے وقت کو گھیر لے جس میں وضو کرنے اور نماز پڑھنے کی مقدار انقطاع نہ ہو، یہ عذر کے ثابت ہونے کی شرط ہے۔ تشریح : نماز کا جتنا وقت ہے پورے وقت میں اتنا موقع نہیں ملتا کہ وضو کر سکے اور نماز پڑھ سکے کہ خون آجاتا ہے ، یہ صورت حال پانچوں نمازوں میں رہتا ہے۔ ایک دن تک یہ صورت حال رہے تو یہ آدمی معذور قرار دیا جائے گا۔ وجه : عن عائشة انها قالت قالت فاطمة بنت ابى حبيش لرسول الله لا يا رسول الله اني لا اطهر؟ الفادع الصلوة - ( بخاری شریف، باب الاستحاضۃ ، ص ۵۳ نمبر ۱۳۰۰۶ مسلم شریف ، باب المستخاصتہ وغسلها وصلوا تھا ص ۱۴۷، نمبر) اس حدیث میں ہے لا اطھر، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ میں پورے دن میں پاک نہیں ہوتی ۔ (۲۶۵) وشرط دوامه وجوده فى كل وقت بعد ذلك ولو مرة. (۲۶۶) وشرط انقطاعه و خروج صاحبه عن كونه معذورا خلو وقت كامل عنه. ترجمه : (۲۶۵) عذر کے برقرار رہنے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ اس کے بعد ہر وقت میں پایا جائے ، چاہے ایک ہی مرتبہ کیوں نہ ہو۔ تشریح : معذور قرار دینے کے بعد پورے نماز کے وقت میں ایک مرتبہ بھی خون آجائے تو وہ معذور برقرار رہے گا۔ ترجمه : (۲۶۶) اور عذر کے ختم ہونے کی شرط، اور عذر والے کا عذر سے نکلنے کی شرط یہ ہے کہ پورا وقت اس عذر سے خالی رہے تشريح : معذور قرار دینے کے بعد اس وقت اس کو صحتمند قرار دیا جائے گا کہ پورا وقت اس عذر سے خالی رہے اور پورے وقت میں ایک مرتبہ بھی خون نہ آئے تو اس کو معذور سے نکال دیا جائے گا اور صحت کا حکم لگا دیا جائے گا۔
What is forbidden due to janabah? He (the author) said whatever he wished of obligatory and supererogatory (prayers). (263) The wudu of those with chronic excuses becomes invalid only with the exit of the time. (264) And a person does not become a ma'dhur (chronic excuse holder) until the excuse encompasses the entire prayer time without a break sufficient to perform wudu and prayer. And this Allah... From this hadith it is also that she should continue performing obligatory and supererogatory prayers even if blood drips onto the mat. (2) In this hadith there is also: From the Prophet (peace be upon him) concerning the mustahadah: 'She leaves prayer during the days of her menses, then she performs ghusl and makes wudu for every prayer, and fasts and prays.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a an al-mustahadah tatawadda' li kulli salat, p.33, no.126) This hadith indicates that the mustahadah should make wudu for every prayer. Lexicon: Continuous urine: urine flows all the time. Istitlaq al-batan: talaq means to go, and istitlaq al-batan means stool coming out all the time. Translation: (263) The wudu of ma'dhur becomes invalid only when the time exits. Explanation: If any other event besides the excuse occurs, then the wudu breaks from that event. For example, if a person with continuous urine experiences a hadath, the wudu breaks from that hadath, but from the urine exiting it does not break. When the prayer time ends, then from the urine exiting the wudu breaks. Evidence: In this hadith: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that Fatima bint Abi Hubaish came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who experiences istihadah and I do not become pure; should I abandon prayer?' He said: 'No, that is a vein and not menstruation. Avoid prayer during the days of your menses, then perform ghusl and make wudu for every prayer, even if blood drips onto the mat.' (Ibn Majah, Bab ma ja'a fi al-mustahadah allati qad 'addat ayyam aqra'iha, p.88, no.624; Nasa'i, Bab dhikr al-istihadah wa iqbal al-dam wa idbarah, p.47, no.350; Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Hayd, vol.1, p.219, no.808) This hadith indicates that even if blood falls on the mat, the wudu does not break, and the phrase 'make wudu for every prayer' points to the fact that when the entire prayer time exits, then from this excuse the wudu breaks. Translation: (264) A person does not become ma'dhur until the excuse encompasses the entire prayer time with no break of the duration sufficient for wudu and prayer; this is the condition for the establishment of the excuse. Explanation: In the entire prayer time, there is no opportunity such that he can perform wudu and pray because blood comes. This state continues for all five prayers. If this state continues for one full day, then this person will be declared ma'dhur. Evidence: From Aisha that Fatima bint Abi Hubaish said to the Messenger of Allah, 'O Messenger of Allah, I do not become pure; should I abandon prayer?' (Bukhari, Bab al-istihadah, p.53, no.13006; Muslim, Bab al-mustahadah wa ghusliha wa salatiha, p.147, no.?) This hadith includes 'I do not become pure,' from which we understand that she is not pure throughout the entire day. (265) The condition for its continuation is that it is found in every subsequent time, even if once. (266) And the condition for its cessation and for the person to exit from being ma'dhur is that a full time is devoid of it. Translation: (265) The condition for the continuation of the excuse is that it is found in every prayer time after that, even if only once. Explanation: After being declared ma'dhur, if blood comes once in the entire prayer time, he remains ma'dhur. Translation: (266) The condition for the excuse to end, and for the person to exit from being ma'dhur, is that a full time is free from it. Explanation: After being declared ma'dhur, he will be declared healthy when a full time is free from the excuse, and if blood does not come even once in the full time, he will be removed from the ma'dhur category and given the ruling of health.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the wudu of individuals with chronic excuses (ma'dhur), such as continuous urine or istihadah (non-menstrual uterine bleeding). The passage begins by stating the central ruling (263): the wudu of a ma'dhur becomes invalid only with the exit of the entire prayer time. This means that the chronic excuse itself does not break wudu during the prayer time; only the end of the time does. However, if another unrelated hadath (like normal urine or wind) occurs, that breaks wudu immediately. This is based on the hadith of the mustahadah woman, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded her to make wudu for every prayer, indicating that her wudu remains valid for the entire time period, even if blood flows continuously. The next ruling (264) establishes the condition for becoming ma'dhur: the excuse must be so persistent that during a full prayer time, there is no break long enough to perform wudu and pray. This is derived from the woman's statement 'I do not become pure' meaning the impurity (blood) lasts the whole day. Rulings (265) and (266) then set the conditions for the continuation and cessation of the ma'dhur status: once a person is ma'dhur, if the excuse occurs even once in each subsequent prayer time, the status continues; if a full prayer time passes completely without the excuse, the status ends. All rulings are supported by the authentic hadith literature on istihadah.

Key Terms
معذور (ma'dhur): A person with a chronic, continuous excuse (like continuous urine, istihadah, or a constant wound) that prevents performing wudu and prayer normally.
عذر ('udhr): A persistent, ongoing condition that is outside of one's control and excuses the normal requirements of wudu and purification.
حدث (hadath): A ritual impurity that breaks wudu, such as passing urine, stool, wind, or blood from other than wounds.
وقت (waqt): The designated time for a specific prayer, e.g., from sunrise to noon for Dhuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the wudu of a ma'dhur become invalid due to their chronic excuse according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately when the chronic excuse occurs.
B) Only at the exit of the entire prayer time.
C) When any hadath occurs, including the chronic excuse.
D) It never becomes invalid as long as the person is ma'dhur.

Key Takeaway
The wudu of a ma'dhur is invalidated only by the exit of the prayer time (or by an unrelated hadath), not by the chronic excuse itself; the conditions for becoming and remaining ma'dhur are defined by the persistence of the excuse over full prayer times.
