Definitions and Types of Impurities (Najasah) and Their Evidence
Defines najasah categories with textual evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the two main types of najasah (hukmi and haqiqi) and state the excusable amounts for each subcategory according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Impurities are two kinds: invisible (hukmi) requiring wudu/ghusl, and visible (haqiqi) with specific excusable amounts.

This lesson introduces the foundational classification of impurities in the Hanafi school. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for correctly applying the rules of purification before prayer. We will explore both non-physical impurities (hukmi) that break wudu or require ghusl, and physical impurities (haqiqi) that must be removed from the body, clothing, or place of prayer, along with the amounts that are excused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of najasah
The passage divides najasah into hukmi (ruled impurity, not visible) and haqiqi (physical, visible). Note the legal basis for each.
Hukmi includes minor and major hadath; haqiqi includes heavy and light.
2
Distinguish between minor and major hadath
Minor hadath (e.g., passing wind) requires wudu; major hadath (e.g., janabah, menstruation) requires ghusl.
These are not visible but affect the state of purity.
3
Subdivide haqiqi impurity into heavy and light
Heavy impurity (najasah ghalizah) includes blood and urine; light impurity (najasah khafifah) includes urine of halal animals.
The distinction affects the excusable amount.
4
Memorize the excusable amounts
For heavy impurity: less than a dirham (≈3g) is excused; a dirham or more requires washing. For light impurity: less than one-fourth of the garment is excused; one-fourth or more requires washing.
The dirham is a Hanafi measure; other schools may differ.
5
Connect the evidence to the ruling
The verse 'And purify your garments' (74:4) commands purification, indicating obligation (wajib). The hadith of Asma gives the method for removing menstrual blood.
The command is addressed to the Prophet but applies to the ummah.

(بخاری شریف، باب غسل دم الحيض، ص ۵۴، نمبر ۳۰۷رتر ندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی غسل دم ثوب ،ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۱۳۸ (۳) اور مکان پاک ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمران النبي نهي ان يصلي في سبعة مواطن في المزبلة والمجزرة والمقبرة وقارعة الطريق و فى الحمام و في معاطن الابل و
Chapter on Impurities and Purification from Them. Necessary Note: 'Anjas' is the plural of najis. Najis (impurity) is of two types: [1] Hukmi impurity: which is not a visible, physical impurity, but the Shariah has ruled it as impure. Then hukmi impurity is divided into two: [1] Minor hadath (small impurity), which necessitates wudu. [2] Major hadath (large impurity), which necessitates ghusl, such as the emission of semen, menstruation, or postpartum bleeding. [2] The second is Haqiqi impurity: which is physically visible. Then it has two types: [1] Heavy impurity (najasah ghalizah): less than a dirham is excused, and if a dirham or more sticks to a person, washing it becomes obligatory, like blood and urine. [2] The second is Light impurity (najasah khafifah): less than one-fourth of the garment is excused, and if one-fourth or more sticks, then it must be washed, then prayer becomes permissible. For example, the urine of animals whose meat is eaten. Here, the discussion is only about the rulings of haqiqi impurity. Its proof is this verse: 'And purify your garments' (Surah Al-Muddaththir, 74:4). (2) And this hadith: From Asma bint Abi Bakr (may Allah be pleased with them) that she said: A woman asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying, 'O Messenger of Allah, what is your opinion if menstrual blood gets on the garment of one of us; how should she act?' The Messenger of Allah said: 'If menstrual blood gets on the garment of one of you, she should rub it, then sprinkle it with water, and then pray in it.' (Bukhari, Bab ghusl dam al-hayd, p.54, no.307; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi ghusl dam al-thawb, p.138, no.138) (3) And for the place to be pure, there is this hadith: From Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade praying in seven places: in the garbage dump, slaughterhouse, graveyard, middle of the road, in the bathroom, in the camel resting places, and...
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling concerning impurities (najasah) and their purification. The author begins a new chapter and provides a necessary note categorizing najasah. First, najasah is divided into two main types: hukmi (ruled impurity) and haqiqi (physical impurity). Hukmi impurity consists of minor hadath (which breaks wudu) and major hadath (which requires ghusl) — these are not visible but have legal consequences. Haqiqi impurity is physically present and further divided into heavy (ghalizah) and light (khafifah). Heavy impurities, like blood and urine, are excused if less than a dirham (approximately 3 grams) in amount; if they equal or exceed a dirham, they must be washed off. Light impurities, such as the urine of halal animals, are excused if less than one-fourth of the garment; if one-fourth or more, they must be washed. The evidence for the obligation of purification from physical impurities is the Quranic verse 'And purify your garments' (74:4), which is a command (amr) indicating obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi principles. The hadith of Asma provides a practical method for removing menstrual blood. The hadith of Ibn Umar listing seven places where prayer is prohibited also relates to the purity of the place of prayer. These rulings are foundational for understanding the requirements of purity (taharah) before prayer in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
نجاست حکمیہ (najasah hukmiyah): Non-physical impurity established by Shar'iah, such as the state of hadath (minor or major) that requires wudu or ghusl.
نجاست حقیقیہ (najasah haqiqiyyah): Physical impurity that can be seen, such as blood, urine, feces, etc., which must be removed from the body, garment, or place of prayer.
نجاست غلیظہ (najasah ghalizah): Heavy impurity, such as blood and urine; less than a dirham is excused; if a dirham or more, washing is wajib.
نجاست خفیفہ (najasah khafifah): Light impurity, such as the urine of halal animals; less than one-fourth of the garment is excused; one-fourth or more requires washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what amount of heavy impurity (najasah ghalizah) is excused on the garment or body?
A) Any amount is excused as long as it is dry.
B) Less than a dirham (approximately 3 grams).
C) Less than one-fourth of the garment.
D) None; all impurity must be washed.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, physical impurities (haqiqi) are excused in small amounts: less than a dirham for heavy and less than one-fourth of the garment for light impurities, based on the Quranic command to purify garments.

Establishing, Maintaining, and Ceasing the Excuse of Continuous Impurity
Setting conditions for establishing and ending the excuse of continuous impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the 'udhr of continuous impurity and apply them to determine when a person is ma'dhur and when the excuse ends.

Core Idea
For continuous impurity, the excuse is established by one occurrence, maintained by at least one occurrence per prayer time, and ends only after a full prayer time without impurity.

In the Hanafi school, chronic conditions like istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) create a legal excuse ('udhr) that allows leniencies in purification. The classical text Thamaratun Najah precisely defines when this excuse begins, how it persists, and when it ceases. Understanding these three conditions is essential for correctly applying the rulings of wudu and prayer for persons who are ma'dhur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of establishment (thubut)
The excuse is established when the impurity occurs at least once within a complete prayer time. This is the threshold to become ma'dhur.
The prayer time is measured as the entire period from entry to exit.
2
Identify the condition of continuity (dawam)
To remain excused, the impurity must appear at least once in every subsequent prayer time. If it does not appear in a particular prayer time, the excuse lapses.
Continuity is tied to each prayer time individually.
3
Identify the condition of cessation (inqita')
The excuse ends only when a complete prayer time passes entirely without any impurity. Mere cessation for a part of the time does not end the excuse.
The person must be completely free of impurity for the entire duration of one prayer time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الانجاس و الطهارة عنها شرط ثبوته . (٢٦٥) وشرط دوامه وجوده فى كل وقت بعد ذلك ولو مرة. (٢٦٦) وشرط انقطاعه و خروج صاحبه عن كونه معذورا خلو وقت كامل عنه.
Chapter on Impurities and Purification from Them. The condition of its establishment: (265) And the condition of its continuity: its existence in every time after that, even once. (266) And the condition of its cessation, and the person's exit from being excused: a complete time being free of it.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah sets out the three conditions concerning the 'udhr (legal excuse) for a person suffering from continuous impurity, such as istihadah (non-menstrual uterine bleeding). The first condition (thubut) is that the impurity occurs once within a complete prayer time. The second (dawam) is that to remain excused, the impurity must continue to appear at least once in each subsequent prayer time. The third (inqita') is that the excuse ends only if a complete prayer time passes entirely without any impurity; only then is the person considered to be healthy and no longer excused. The Urdu commentary cites the hadith of Umm Habibah (رضی الله عنها) who said 'la at-har' (I do not become pure), indicating her constant state of impurity, which is the basis for these rulings. This is a key ruling in the Hanafi school regarding the treatment of chronic impurities.

Key Terms
عُذْر (‘udhr): A legal excuse that permits leniency, here continuous impurity
مَعْذُور (ma‘dhūr): A person legally excused due to continuous impurity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when does a person cease to be ma‘dhūr (excused) due to continuous impurity?
A) When the impurity stops even for a moment
B) When a complete prayer time passes without any impurity
C) When they perform ghusl
D) When they consult a scholar

Key Takeaway
The 'udhr of continuous impurity is governed by three precise conditions tied to prayer times: one occurrence establishes it, persistence keeps it, and a full time free ends it.

Division of Impurities into Ghaliẓah and Khafīfah
Categorizing physical impurities into major (ghaliẓah) and minor (khafīfah) with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two categories of physical impurity (ghaliẓah and khafīfah) and list the examples of ghaliẓah impurity as given by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school divides physical impurities into heavy (ghaliẓah) and light (khafīfah) with distinct rulings.

Physical impurity (najāsah ḥaqīqiyyah) is not uniform in severity. The Hanafi school classifies it into ghaliẓah (heavy) and khafīfah (light), each with its own rulings on how much can be excused in prayer. This lesson presents the list of ghaliẓah impurities as taught in the classical text Thamaratun Najah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage states impurity is divided into two: ghaliẓah (heavy) and khafīfah (light). Understanding this classification is the first step.
This is a foundational taxonomy in Hanafi fiqh.
2
List the heavy impurities
The passage enumerates specific items: wine, flowing blood, carrion meat and skin, urine of animals not eaten, dog feces, predator excrement and saliva, and droppings of chickens and ducks. Commit these to memory.
The list may include additional items in other texts; this is a standard list from Thamaratun Najah.
3
Connect to proof
The hadith reference (Tirmidhi) provides evidence for the excusable quantity of blood (dirham size). This proof supports the distinction between ghaliẓah and khafīfah.
The hadith is a dalil for the ruling on blood.
4
Understand the legal effect
Ghaliẓah impurities require washing if present in quantity of a dirham or more (for liquids) or if they are solid impurities. Khafīfah impurities are generally excused in small amounts.
Details of quantities are covered in advanced lessons.

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah defines the two categories of physical (ḥaqīqī) impurity: ghaliẓah (heavy) and khafīfah (light). The author then lists twelve items of ghaliẓah impurity: wine, flowing blood, carrion meat and skin, urine of non-edible animals, dog feces, predator excrement and saliva, and poultry droppings. The proof for the leniency in istinja' with stones indicates that trace amounts of impurity are excused. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad).

Definition and Examples of Light Impurity
Defining light impurity and listing its examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define light impurity (najasah khafifah) and list its three examples according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Light impurity arises from conflicting evidence: not strong enough for heavy impurity, excused until a quarter of the body or garment.

In Hanafi fiqh, impurities are classified into heavy (ghalizah) and light (khafifah). This lesson covers the definition of light impurity, its examples, and the reasoning behind its classification. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining the validity of acts of worship, especially prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
The passage directly defines light impurity (الخفيفة) with three examples: horse urine, urine of halal animals, and droppings of non-halal birds. Identify each example from the Arabic text.
The term 'الخفيفة' refers to the lighter category of najasah.
2
Understand the legal basis for halal animal urine
The commentary explains that halal animal urine is considered light because there is conflicting evidence about its purity. The people of 'Uraynah were ordered to drink camel urine (suggesting purity), but other hadith indicate impurity. This conflict places it in the light category.
The conflict (تعارض) is key: if evidence were clear for purity, it would be pure; if clear for impurity, it would be heavy.
3
Recognize the reasoning for non-halal bird droppings
Droppings of birds whose meat is not eaten are considered light impurity because these birds fly high and defecate from above, making it difficult to avoid contracting their droppings. The principle of relief (تخفيف) applies.
The hardship (مشقة) in avoidance justifies the lighter ruling.
4
Distinguish from heavy impurity
Note that not all substances from these animals are light. For example, the dung (پیخانہ) of halal animals remains heavy impurity. Only the urine is light in the case of halal animals.
Heavy impurities include blood, wine, dog saliva, and dung of halal animals.

(269) As for light impurity, it is the urine of a horse, similarly the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten, and the droppings of a bird whose meat is not eaten. Translation: (269) And light impurities: like the urine of a horse and lawful animals, and the droppings of unlawful birds. Explanation: Horse urine, lawful animal urine, and unlawful bird droppings are light impurities. Reason: (1) The meat of a horse is originally halal; it was only prohibited due to jihad. So it is a lawful animal, and the urine of a lawful animal is light impurity because the people of 'Uraynah were ordered to drink camel urine, meaning that the urine of a lawful animal is pure, but another narration showed that urine is impure, so due to this conflict, the urine of a lawful animal is light impurity, while its dung remains heavy impurity. Both types of hadith have passed in issue number 267. (2) The meat of a horse is originally halal; for this there is the hadith of Jabir bin Abdullah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the meat of donkeys on the day of Khaybar and permitted the meat of horses. (3) In this saying of a Tabi'i: 'Ata said: Whatever meat you eat, there is no harm in its urine. In this athar, there is that there is no harm in the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten. And such birds whose meat is not halal, they fly above and defecate from above, so it is difficult to avoid their droppings, therefore they are considered light impurity. (3) In this saying of a Tabi'i is its evidence: Al-Hasan said: A bird dropped on al-Hasan, and some people said: Shall we bring water to wash it? He said: No, and he wiped it off. In this athar, the droppings of a bird are pure, or light impurity.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines light impurity (najasah khafifah) and lists its examples. The author states that light impurities include the urine of a horse, the urine of any animal whose meat is eaten, and the droppings of a bird whose meat is not eaten. The commentary explains the reasoning: horse meat is originally halal but prohibited due to jihad, so its urine is treated as that of a lawful animal. Lawful animal urine is considered light impurity because there is conflicting evidence about its purity. The hadith of the people of 'Uraynah, where they were ordered to drink camel urine, suggests purity, while other hadith indicate impurity. Due to this conflict, it is classified as light. The droppings of birds whose meat is not eaten are also light impurity because it is difficult to avoid them. The passage also quotes supporting hadith and athar.

Key Terms
نجاست خفیفہ (najasah khafifah): Impurity about which there is conflicting evidence regarding its purity or impurity, such as the urine of halal animals and droppings of forbidden birds.
بول ما يؤكل لحمه (baul ma 'akul lahmuh): Urine of an animal whose meat is permitted to eat; considered light impurity in Hanafi fiqh.
خرء طير لا يؤكل (khur' tayr la yu'kal): Droppings of a bird whose meat is not eaten; considered light impurity due to difficulty in avoidance.

Pardonable Amount of Heavy Impurity in Prayer
Stating that heavy impurity up to the size of a dirham is excused in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on heavy impurity in prayer and apply the dirham measure (area vs weight) to determine whether a given amount is excused.

Core Idea
Heavy impurity less than a dirham is excused; dirham measured by area (thin) or weight (thick).

This passage addresses a common practical concern: how much impurity on clothing or body is acceptable during prayer. The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith, sets a clear threshold—the dirham. Understanding this ruling helps you avoid unnecessary repetitions of prayer while maintaining ritual purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the presence of heavy impurity (najasah ghalizah) during prayer. The ruling is that up to a dirham is excused; the prayer is valid. If equal to or more than a dirham, the prayer is invalid unless removed.
Heavy impurities include blood, urine (human, dog), and other clearly impure substances.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'The prayer is repeated due to a dirham's amount of blood.' This hadith is recorded by Daraqutni and Bayhaqi.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted as evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'min qadr al-dirham' ('from the amount of a dirham') sets the threshold. The command 'tu'ada al-salah' ('the prayer is repeated') implies that if impurity reaches or exceeds that amount, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
The hadith does not specify area vs weight; later scholars deduced the two measures.
4
Apply the measure based on impurity consistency
If the impurity is thin (liquid), the dirham is measured by area: a circle of diameter 2.75 cm (approx 5.94 cm² area). If the impurity is thick (solid or viscous), the dirham is measured by weight: 4.374 grams.
This reconciliation ensures the rule applies appropriately to different types of impurities.
5
Note cross-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school holds that any amount of heavy impurity invalidates prayer. The Hanafi school is more lenient, allowing up to a dirham. This difference stems from differing interpretations of general purity commands.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that a Hanafi may pray with a small unavoidable stain, while a Shafi'i must remove it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۷۰)وعفى قدر الدرهم من المغلظة. ترجمه : (۲۷۰) اور نجاست غلیظہ درہم کی مقدار معاف ہے۔ وجه : عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : تعاد الصلوة من قدر الدرهم من الدم (دار قطنی ، باب قدر النجاسة التي متبطل الصلوۃ ص ۳۸۵ نمبر ۴۷۹ ارسنن سبیھقی ، باب ما يجب غسله من الدم ، ج اول ص ۵۶۶، نمبر ۴۰۹۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خون یا اس جیسی نجاست غلیظہ درہم سے کم ہو تو معاف ہے۔ ور ہم کا حساب کی درھم کے بارے میں دو قسم کی باتیں ہیں ، ایک یہ کہ اسکے وزن کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور دوسری یہ کہ اسکی مساحت یعنی رقبے کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو دونوں قولوں میں ترتیب یہ ہے ہیں کہ جس قول میں مساحت کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے وہ پہلی نجاست کے بارے میں ہے۔ کہ پتلی نجاست ہو تو درھم کے رقبے کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور 2.75 سینٹی میٹر نجاست ہو تو جگہ نا پاک ہوگی ، اور جس قول میں وزن کا اعتبار ہے اسکا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نجاست گاڑھی ہو تو درھم کے وزن کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور 4.374 گرام وزن نجاست ہو تو جگہ ناپاک قرار دیا جائے چاہے رقبے کے اعتبار سے 2.75 سینٹی میٹر سے کم رقبے پر ہی نجاست لگی ہو۔ یہ انگلینڈ میں پچاس پینس کی مقدار ہے۔
(270) And the amount of a dirham from heavy impurity is excused. Translation: (270) And heavy impurity of the quantity of a dirham is excused. Evidence: From Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: The prayer is repeated due to the amount of a dirham of blood. (Daraqutni, Bayhaqi) From this hadith, it is understood that blood or similar heavy impurity less than a dirham is excused. Regarding the dirham, there are two types of statements: one is that its weight is considered, and the other is that its area (surface) is considered. The order among the two sayings is that the saying that considers area is concerning the first impurity: if the impurity is thin, then the area of a dirham is considered, and if impurity is 2.75 cm then the place becomes impure; and the saying that considers weight means that if the impurity is thick, then the weight of a dirham is considered, and if the impurity weighs 4.374 grams, then the place is deemed impure even if the area is less than 2.75 cm. This is the size of fifty pence in England.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that heavy impurity (najasah ghalizah) is excused if it is less than the size of a dirham. The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'The prayer is repeated due to a dirham's amount of blood.' The commentary then explains that there are two interpretations of the dirham: by area (2.75 cm) for thin impurities, and by weight (4.374 grams) for thick impurities. This distinction ensures that the pardonable amount is determined appropriately. The Hanafi school relies on this hadith and the corresponding fiqh rules.

Key Terms
الدرهم (al-dirham): A standard coin used as a measure; here interpreted as either area (2.75 cm) or weight (4.374 g) depending on impurity consistency.
نجاسة غليظة (najasah ghalizah): Impurity that is clearly impure, such as blood, urine of humans, dogs, etc.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school pardons heavy impurity less than a dirham in prayer, with the dirham measured by area for thin impurities and weight for thick ones.

Threshold for Light Impurity on Garment or Body
Stating the measure of light impurity that is excused

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi threshold for light impurity to be considered excessive and apply the qiyas analogy from satr and ihram.

Core Idea
Light impurity excused up to a quarter; beyond that, the garment becomes impure and prayer invalid.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on light impurity (najasah khafifah) on a garment or body. The school sets a clear threshold: less than a quarter is excused; a quarter or more renders the garment impure, requiring purification. This ruling is derived through qiyas (analogy) from rulings on uncovering the ‘awrah and shaving the head in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the presence of light impurity on a garment or body. The ruling is that it is excused (ma‘fu) if it is less than one quarter of the garment or body. If it reaches a quarter or more, the garment becomes impure (najis) and prayer in it is invalid.
Light impurity is defined as one with conflicting evidence (e.g., urine of halal animals).
2
Understand the qiyas analogy
The quarter measure is derived by analogy (qiyas) from two cases: (1) Uncovering the ‘awrah: if a quarter of the private parts is uncovered, it is considered equivalent to full exposure. (2) Shaving the head in ihram: shaving a quarter is equivalent to a complete shave. Similarly, if a quarter of the garment is affected by light impurity, it is equivalent to the whole garment being impure.
This is an example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because the connection is not explicit in the primary texts.
3
Note the distinction from heavy impurity
Heavy impurity (najasah ghalizah) has a different threshold – a dirham's area. Light impurity is more lenient because of the conflicting evidence, a quarter of the garment is the limit.
The dua‘s mentioned in the passage (e.g., urine of halal animals) illustrate why the ruling is lenient.
4
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
If you spill a small amount of camel urine (less than quarter of your garment), your prayer is valid. If the affected area reaches a quarter or more, you must wash it before praying. If you pray without washing, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This ruling applies to light impurity only; for heavy impurity, even a small amount requires purification.

(۲۷۱) وما دون ربع الثوب او البدن من الخفيفة (۲۲) وعفى رشاش بول كرؤوس الابر جائے. ترجمه : (۲۷۱) اور نجاست خفیفہ میں چوتھائی کپڑے اور چوتھائی بدن معاف ہے۔ تشریح : نجاست خفیفہ کے بارے میں اصل روایت یہ ہے کہ اتنا لگ جائے کہ لوگ اس کو کثیر اور زیادہ سمجھیں تو کپڑا نا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ اس عبارت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ و كان ابو حنيـفـه يـكـرهـه ، و كان يقول اذا وقع في وضوء افسد الوضوء، و ان اصاب الثوب منه شيء كثير ثم صلى فيه اعاد الصلوة كتاب الاثار ، باب ابوال البهائم وغیر تھا،ص نمبر (۳۴) اس عبارت میں ہے کہ پیشاب بہت لگے تو نماز لوٹائی جائے۔ لیکن کپڑے کی چوتھائی ہو تو وہ گویا کہ کثیر ہو گیا اور کپڑا ناپاک ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ستر کھلنے میں چوتھائی ستر کھل جائے تو وہ کل ستر کھلنے کے قائم مقام ہے ۔ احرام کی حالت میں سرمنڈوانے میں چوتھائی سرمنڈوائے تو کل سرمنڈوانے کے قائم مقام ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی چوتھائی کپڑے پر لگ جائے تو پورے کپڑے میں لگنے کے قائم مقام ہوگا اور کپڑا نا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ نجاست خفیفہ : اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کے پاک ہونے اور ناپاک ہونے میں دونوں قسم کے دلائل ہوں ، یا علماء میں اختلاف ہو۔ جیسے ان جانوروں کا پیشاب جن کا گوشت کھایا جاتا ہے کہ ان کے پاک اور ناپاک ہونے میں دونوں قسم کی احادیث ہیں۔ پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے حدیث میں ہے (۱) عن انس ان ناسا من عرينة قدموا المدينة فاجتووها فبعثهم رسول الله في ابل الصدقة وقال اشربوا من البانها و ابوالها - ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی بول ما یؤكل لحمه ص ۲۱ نمبر ۷۲ ) آپ نے اہل عرینہ کو اونٹ کا پیشاب پینے کا حکم دیا۔ وہ پاک ہو گا تب ہی تو پیشاب پینے کا حکم دیا ہو گا؟ (۲) عن البراء قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا بأس ببول ما اكل لحمه (دار قطنی ، باب نجاسة البول والامر بالتنزه منه والحكم في بول ما يؤكل لحمه بص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۴ ۴۵ ) اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماکول اللحم کا پیشاب پاک ہے۔ پیشاب کے ناپاک ہونے کی دلیل (۱) عن ابن صلى الله عباس... فقال النبي علة يعذبان وما يعذبان في كبير ثم قال بلى كان احدهما لا يستتر من بوله وكان الآخر يمشى بالنميمة - ( بخاری شریف، باب من الكبائران لایستر من بوله ، ص ۳۵ نمبر ۲۲۶ / ترمذی شریف، باب التنشد يدفی البول، ص ۳۱ نمبر ۷۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی بھی پیشاب لگنا گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ اس لئے وہ ناپاک ہے (۲) عن انس
(271) And less than a quarter of the garment or body from light impurity, and the spray of urine like the heads of needles is excused. Translation: (271) And in light impurity, a quarter of the garment and a quarter of the body is excused. Explanation: Regarding light impurity, the original narration is that if it clings to such an extent that people consider it abundant and excessive, then the garment becomes impure. This statement proves it: And Abu Hanifa disliked it, and he used to say: If it falls into ablution, it spoils the ablution, and if a large amount of it touches the garment and he prays in it, he repeats the prayer. (Kitab al-Athar, chapter on urines of animals) This statement says that if urine clings a lot, the prayer is repeated. But if it is a quarter of the garment, then it is as if it has become abundant and the garment becomes impure. Because in the uncovering of the satr (private parts), if a quarter of the satr is uncovered, it is equivalent to uncovering all of it. Similarly, in ihram, shaving a quarter of the head is equivalent to shaving the whole head. Likewise here, if a quarter of the garment is affected, it is equivalent to the entire garment being affected, and the garment becomes impure. Light impurity: It is that regarding which there is both evidence for purity and impurity, or there is disagreement among scholars. Like the urine of animals whose meat is eaten: there are both types of hadith regarding their purity and impurity. Proof of purity: (1) From Anas that some people from 'Uraynah came to Medina and fell ill, so the Messenger of Allah sent them to the camels of sadaqah and said: Drink from their milk and urine. (Tirmidhi) He ordered them to drink camel urine; it must be pure for him to order drinking it. (2) From al-Bara' that the Prophet said: By Allah, there is no harm in the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten. (Daraqutni) This indicates that the urine of halal meat is pure. Proof of impurity: (1) From Ibn Abbas... the Prophet said: They are punished and not for a great matter. Then he said: Yes, one of them did not protect himself from urine, and the other used to go about with slander. (Bukhari, Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates that any contact with urine is a major sin, so it is impure. (2) From Anas...
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on light impurity: it is excused if it is less than a quarter of the garment or the body. The commentary provides the original ruling from Abu Hanifa that if light impurity is considered abundant, it spoils ablution and requires prayer repetition. The quarter measure is derived by qiyas (analogy): in matters of covering the awrah, uncovering a quarter is equivalent to uncovering all; similarly, in ihram, shaving a quarter of the head stands for full shaving. Thus, light impurity affecting a quarter of the garment renders the whole garment impure. The passage then defines light impurity as something with conflicting evidence, and it includes a lengthy discussion on the hadith regarding urine of halal animals.

Key Terms
ربع الثوب (rub' al-thawb): One quarter of the garment; used as the threshold for light impurity being considered excessive.
نجاست خفیفہ (najasah khafifah): Impurity with conflicting evidence; excused up to quarter of garment.
نجاست غلیظہ (najasah ghalizah): Heavy impurity with clear evidence; excused only if less than a dirham's area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the threshold for light impurity on a garment to be considered excessive in the Hanafi school?
A) Any amount
B) Up to a dirham
C) A quarter of the garment
D) Half of the garment

Key Takeaway
Light impurity is excused on a garment or body if it covers less than one quarter; a quarter or more renders the garment impure, requiring purification before prayer.

Ruling on Light Impurity: Excusable Amount and Definition
Ruling on excusable amount of light impurity and its definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the excusable amount of light impurity in Hanafi fiqh, define light impurity, and identify the proof behind its classification.

Core Idea
Light impurity is excused if less than a quarter of the garment; if a quarter or more, prayer is invalid.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on light impurity (najasa khafifa), particularly the amount that is excused during prayer. The passage defines light impurity as that which has conflicting evidence regarding its purity, and sets the benchmark of one quarter of the garment or body as the threshold. We will also explore the proof from hadith and the intra-madhhab differences in measurement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage to find the specific ruling: less than a quarter of garment or body of light impurity is excused. Note that a quarter or more is considered significant and invalidates prayer unless washed.
This is the central rule of the lesson.
2
Understand the definition of light impurity
Light impurity is defined as that concerning which there is conflicting evidence (purity vs impurity) from primary texts or scholarly disagreement. The classic example is urine of animals whose meat is eaten.
Contrast with heavy impurity (najasa ghaliza) where evidence is unanimous.
3
Examine the proof for purity of edible animal urine
The passage cites two hadith: the Prophet commanding the people of Uraynah to drink camel urine, and the hadith 'no harm in urine of edible animals.' The command indicates permissibility and thus purity.
These hadith are considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Examine the proof for impurity of urine in general
The passage also cites hadith about punishment in the grave for not avoiding urine, implying that urine is impure. These apply to all urine generally.
The conflict is resolved by categorizing edible animal urine as light impurity.
5
See how the Hanafi school resolves the conflict
Because of conflicting evidence, Abu Hanifa classifies edible animal urine as light impurity. The excusable amount is less than a quarter, measured by area for liquid and weight for thick impurity.
This shows the application of istihsan and accommodation of both sets of evidence.

باب الانجاس و الطهارة عنها
(۲۷۱) وما دون ربع الثوب او البدن من الخفيفة (۲۲) وعفى رشاش بول كرؤوس الابر جائے تو دونوں قولوں میں ترتیب یہ ہے ہیں کہ جس قول میں مساحت کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے وہ پہلی نجاست کے بارے میں ہے۔ کہ پتلی نجاست ہو تو درھم کے رقبے کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور 2.75 سینٹی میٹر نجاست ہو تو جگہ نا پاک ہوگی ، اور جس قول میں وزن کا اعتبار ہے اسکا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نجاست گاڑھی ہو تو درھم کے وزن کا اعتبار کیا جائے اور 4.374 گرام وزن نجاست ہو تو جگہ ناپاک قرار دیا جائے چاہے رقبے کے اعتبار سے 2.75 سینٹی میٹر سے کم رقبے پر ہی نجاست لگی ہو۔ یہ انگلینڈ میں پچاس پینس کی مقدار ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۷۱) اور نجاست خفیفہ میں چوتھائی کپڑے اور چوتھائی بدن معاف ہے۔ تشریح : نجاست خفیفہ کے بارے میں اصل روایت یہ ہے کہ اتنا لگ جائے کہ لوگ اس کو کثیر اور زیادہ سمجھیں تو کپڑا نا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ اس عبارت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ و كان ابو حنيـفـه يـكـرهـه ، و كان يقول اذا وقع في وضوء افسد الوضوء، و ان اصاب الثوب منه شيء كثير ثم صلى فيه اعاد الصلوة كتاب الاثار ، باب ابوال البهائم وغیر تھا،ص نمبر (۳۴) اس عبارت میں ہے کہ پیشاب بہت لگے تو نماز لوٹائی جائے۔ لیکن کپڑے کی چوتھائی ہو تو وہ گویا کہ کثیر ہو گیا اور کپڑا ناپاک ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ستر کھلنے میں چوتھائی ستر کھل جائے تو وہ کل ستر کھلنے کے قائم مقام ہے ۔ احرام کی حالت میں سرمنڈوانے میں چوتھائی سرمنڈوائے تو کل سرمنڈوانے کے قائم مقام ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی چوتھائی کپڑے پر لگ جائے تو پورے کپڑے میں لگنے کے قائم مقام ہوگا اور کپڑا نا پاک ہو جائے گا۔
نجاست خفیفہ : اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کے پاک ہونے اور ناپاک ہونے میں دونوں قسم کے دلائل ہوں ، یا علماء میں اختلاف ہو۔ جیسے ان جانوروں کا پیشاب جن کا گوشت کھایا جاتا ہے کہ ان کے پاک اور ناپاک ہونے میں دونوں قسم کی احادیث ہیں۔ پاک ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے حدیث میں ہے (۱) عن انس ان ناسا من عرينة قدموا المدينة فاجتووها فبعثهم رسول الله في ابل الصدقة وقال اشربوا من البانها و ابوالها - ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی بول ما یؤكل لحمه ص ۲۱ نمبر ۷۲ ) آپ نے اہل عرینہ کو اونٹ کا پیشاب پینے کا حکم دیا۔ وہ پاک ہو گا تب ہی تو پیشاب پینے کا حکم دیا ہو گا؟ (۲) عن البراء قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا بأس ببول ما اكل لحمه (دار قطنی ، باب نجاسة البول والامر بالتنزه منه والحكم في بول ما يؤكل لحمه بص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۴ ۴۵ ) اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ماکول اللحم کا پیشاب پاک ہے۔ پیشاب کے ناپاک ہونے کی دلیل (۱) عن ابن صلى الله عباس... فقال النبي علة يعذبان وما يعذبان في كبير ثم قال بلى كان احدهما لا يستتر من بوله وكان الآخر يمشى بالنميمة - ( بخاری شریف، باب من الكبائران لایستر من بوله ، ص ۳۵ نمبر ۲۲۶ / ترمذی شریف، باب التنشد يدفی البول، ص ۳۱ نمبر ۷۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی بھی پیشاب لگنا گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ اس لئے وہ ناپاک ہے (۲) عن انس قال قال رسول الله لا تنزهوا من البول فان عامة عذاب القبر منه (دار قطنی ، باب نجاسۃ البول والامر بالمنتزه مندرج اول ص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۴۵۳) یہ دونوں قسم کی احادیث ماکول اللحم کے بارے میں ہیں۔ اس لئے اس کے پیشاب کے بارے میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اس کا پیشاب امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نجاست خفیفہ ہے اور دوسرے جانور یا انسان کے بارے میں پاکی کی احادیث نہیں ہیں اس لئے ان کا پیشاب نجاست غلیظہ ہے۔
Section: Impurities and purification from them. (271) And less than a quarter of the garment or the body of light impurity is excused. A splash of urine like the heads of needles is excused. So regarding the two statements, the order is that the statement that considers area applies to liquid impurity: if it is liquid impurity, the area of a dirham is considered, and if it is 2.75 cm, the place becomes impure. And the statement that considers weight means that if the impurity is thick, the weight of a dirham is considered, and if the impurity weighs 4.374 grams, the place is declared impure even if the area is less than 2.75 cm. This is the amount of fifty pence in England. Translation: (271) And less than a quarter of the garment or the body of light impurity is excused. Explanation: Regarding light impurity, the original narration is that it applies enough that people consider it much and abundant, then the garment becomes impure. There is proof in this expression. Abu Hanifa used to disapprove of it, and he used to say: if it falls into ablution, it invalidates ablution, and if something much of it touches the garment and then he prays in it, he repeats the prayer. (Kitab al-Athar, Section: Urine of animals etc., p. 34) This expression indicates that if urine touches much, the prayer is repeated. But if it is a quarter of the garment, then it is considered much and the garment becomes impure. Because in exposing the private parts, if a quarter is exposed, it stands in place of all being exposed. In ihram, shaving a quarter of the head stands in place of shaving all. Similarly here, if a quarter of the garment is touched, it stands in place of the whole garment and the garment becomes impure. Light impurity: It is called that regarding which there are both types of evidence for its purity and impurity, or there is a difference among scholars. Like the urine of animals whose meat is eaten: there are both types of hadith regarding their purity and impurity. Evidence for purity: (1) From Anas that some people from Uraynah came to Madinah and found its climate unhealthy, so the Messenger of Allah sent them to the camels of sadaqah and said: 'Drink from their milk and urine.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on urine of edible animals, p. 21 no. 72) He commanded them to drink camel urine. It would only be pure if he commanded them to drink it, wouldn't it? (2) From al-Bara' who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, there is no harm in the urine of what is eaten of meat.' (Darqutni, chapter on impurity of urine and command to avoid it and the ruling on urine of edible animals, p. 135 no. 445) This indicates that the urine of edible animals is pure. Evidence for impurity of urine: (1) From Ibn Abbas... The Prophet said: 'They are punished and they are not punished for a great matter. Then he said: Yes, one of them did not avoid urine, and the other used to go about with slander.' (Bukhari, chapter on major sins: not avoiding urine, p. 35 no. 226; Tirmidhi, chapter on the command to avoid urine, p. 31 no. 70) This hadith indicates that any contact with urine is a major sin. Therefore it is impure. (2) From Anas who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not be careless about urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' (Darqutni, chapter on impurity of urine and the command to avoid it, first part, p. 135 no. 453) These two types of hadith are about edible animals. Therefore the imams differed regarding its urine. Therefore its urine is light impurity according to Abu Hanifa. And for other animals or humans, there are no hadith about purity, so their urine is heavy impurity.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on light impurity (najasa khafifa) and the amount that is excused in prayer. The ruling states that less than a quarter of the garment or body affected by light impurity is excused. The commentator explains that there are two opinions within the Hanafi school regarding measurement: for thin (liquid) impurity, the area of a dirham (approx. 2.75 cm) is considered; for thick impurity, the weight of a dirham (approx. 4.374 grams) is considered. The author then defines light impurity as that concerning which there is conflicting evidence (purity vs impurity) either from texts or scholarly disagreement. The classic example is the urine of animals whose meat is eaten. The passage provides two sets of hadith: one indicating purity (the Prophet commanding the people of Uraynah to drink camel urine, and the hadith 'no harm in urine of edible animals') and another indicating impurity (the hadith about punishment in the grave due to not avoiding urine). Based on this conflict, Abu Hanifa classifies edible animal urine as light impurity, while urine of other animals and humans is heavy impurity (najasa ghaliza) because there are no purity texts for them. The ruling also establishes that if such light impurity covers a quarter of the garment or body, it is considered significant and necessitates washing; if less, it is excused.

Key Terms
نجاست خفیفہ (najasa khafifa): Light impurity: any impurity about which there is conflicting evidence (purity vs impurity) in the primary sources, leading to scholarly disagreement; e.g., urine of animals whose meat is eaten.
غليظ (ghaliz): Heavy impurity: impurity that is definitively established as najis with no conflicting evidence, e.g., urine of humans and non-edible animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the benchmark for considering light impurity 'significant' (kathir) that invalidates prayer?
A) Any amount visible to the eye
B) One quarter of the garment or body
C) The area of a dirham (2.75 cm)
D) A splash the size of a needle head

Key Takeaway
Light impurity is defined by conflicting evidence and is excused if less than a quarter; understanding this allows correct application of taharah rulings.

Urine Splashes the Size of a Needle Head Are Excused
Ruling on excusing small urine splashes due to general prevalence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a urine splash the size of a needle head is excused in the Hanafi school and identify the principle of umum balwa that supports this leniency.

Core Idea
A drop of urine the size of a needle head is excused — general prevalence (umum balwa) brings leniency.

This lesson addresses a practical concern: what if a tiny splash of urine lands on your garment? According to the Hanafi school, a very small amount — the size of a needle head — is excused due to the principle of umum balwa (common prevalence). The passage provides evidence from the Salaf and explains why leniency is granted.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify what the passage rules: a urine splash the size of a needle head on garment or body is excused (not considered impure). Note that it applies specifically to 'rashash' (splashes), not pools or larger amounts.
The term 'rashash' is key: it refers to small spatters, not collected impurity.
2
Locate the evidence
The passage cites two reports from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: one from al-Zuhri about janabah splashes, another from Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i about animal urine splashes. Also invokes the principle of umum balwa.
The evidence is from the Salaf (tabi‘in) and rational principle, not directly from Quran or Mutawatir Sunnah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The statement 'la ba'sa bihi' (no harm in it) indicates permission and exemption. The principle of umum balwa provides a rational basis: because people are regularly exposed (e.g., shepherds), leniency is granted.
The Hanafi school uses umum balwa to ease hardship in cases of widespread unavoidable impurity.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other madhhabs may not excuse even a very small amount of urine, considering any contact with najasah as requiring washing. The Hanafi position is therefore a dispensation.
This difference has practical implications: a Hanafi can pray with a needle-head splash; a Shafi'i generally cannot.

ترجمه : (۲۷۲) اور سوئی کے سرے برابر پیشاب کے چھینٹے معاف ہیں۔
تشریح : کپڑے پر یاب بدن پر پیشاب کا چھینٹا سوئی کے برابر پڑ جائے تو وہ معاف ہے اس سے کپڑا نا پاک نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) سألت الزهرى عن رجل يغتسل من الجنابة فينتضح في الاناء من جلده ، فقال : لا بأس به (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الماء يمه الحب اوید خلہ، ج اول ص ۷۲ ، نمبر (۳۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جنبی کے غسل کا چھینٹا پڑ جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ (۲) عن ابراهیم قال : لا بأس بأبوال البهائم الا المستنقع . اى المجتمع ۔ (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب ابوال الدواب و روشها ، ج اول ص ۳۷۷، نمبر۰ ۱۴۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جانور کے پیشاب کے چھینٹے پڑ جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے البتہ بہت زیادہ ہو جائے تو پھر دھویا جائے گا ۔ (۳) ایک قاعدہ یہ بھی ہے کہ جہاں لوگ مبتلاء بہ ہوتے ہیں اور اس معاملے میں عموم بلوی ہوتا ہے وہاں تخفیف آجاتی ہے، دیہات کے چروا ہے روزانہ گائے چراتے ہیں اور انکو پیشاب کا چھینٹا لگتا رہتا ہے اس لئے اس میں تخفیف آگئی اور اس کو معاف کر دیا گیا۔ [ نا چیز ایک زمانے تک گائے چراتا رہا، گائے دو ہتے وقت ہی پیشاب کرتی تھی اور کپڑوں میں چھینٹا پڑا کرتا تھا، اور اسی کپڑے کے ساتھ فجر کی نماز میں جانا پڑتا تھا، اس مجبوری میں اسی حدیث سے
استفاده کرتا )
اصول : عموم بلوی میں تخفیف آتی ہے۔
لغت : رشاش: چھینٹا ابر: سوئی ، روس الا بر : سوئی کے سر کے برابر ۔ عموم بلوی: جس چیز میں لوگ بہت مبتلا ہوتے ہیں اس کو عموم بلوی، کہتے ہیں۔
Translation: (272) And a splash of urine the size of needle heads is excused. Explanation: If a splash of urine the size of a needle falls on the garment or body, it is excused and the garment does not become impure. Evidence: (1) I asked al-Zuhri about a man who ghusl from major impurity splashes water from his skin into a vessel; he said: There is no harm in it. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on water reaching the container or its impurity, vol. 1 p. 72 no. 31) This effect indicates that if a splash from a person in janabah falls, there is no harm. (2) From Ibrahim: He said: There is no harm in splashes of animal urine except if it collects (i.e., pools). (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on urine of animals and their saliva, vol. 1 p. 377 no. 148) This effect indicates that if an animal's urine splashes, there is no harm; but if it becomes a large amount, then it must be washed. (3) There is also a principle: Where people are commonly afflicted and there is general prevalence (umum balwa), leniency comes. Village shepherds graze cows daily and get urine splashes on them, so leniency came and it was excused. [The humble one used to graze cows for a time; when a cow urinated, a splash would fall on his clothes, and he had to go to Fajr prayer with those clothes. In this difficulty, he used this hadith.] Principle: Umum balwa (general prevalence) brings leniency. Lexicon: rishash: splash; ibar: needle; ru'us al-ibar: tips of needles. Umum balwa: That in which people are commonly afflicted.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage covers the second ruling (272) that a very small splash of urine, the size of a needle head, is excused and does not make the garment impure. The commentator provides three pieces of evidence: first, a report from al-Zuhri that small splashes from a person in janabah are excused; second, a report from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that splashes of animal urine are excused unless they accumulate; third, the principle of umum balwa (general prevalence) – because people, especially shepherds, are regularly exposed to such splashes, Islamic law grants leniency. The author adds a personal anecdote about grazing cows. The key principle stated is that general prevalence (umum balwa) brings leniency (takhfif). Lexically, 'rushash' means splash, 'ibar' means needles, and 'umum balwa' is defined as a situation where many people are commonly affected.

Key Terms
رشاش (rashash): Splash: small drops of liquid (e.g., urine) that scatter from the source upon impact.
عموم بلوی (umum balwa): General prevalence: a situation where many people are commonly affected by a particular impurity or difficulty, leading to leniency in the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A urine splash the size of a needle head is excused in the Hanafi school due to the principle of umum balwa (general prevalence).

Transfer of Impurity via Wetness
Ruling on impurity transfer from wet bedding or soil to body

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which impurity transfers via wetness and apply it to determine the purity of a body part after contact with a wet najis surface.

Core Idea
Impurity transfers only if its effect (color, taste, or smell) becomes visible on the contacted body part.

This lesson clarifies a common fiqh question: when does a body part become impure after contact with a wet najis surface? The Hanafi school establishes a clear principle based on visible evidence of impurity transfer. You will learn the exact condition and why it matters for daily purification.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
Identify the situation: a person who is already impure (e.g., in janabah or with najasah on body) lies on a bedding or stands on wet soil. Both the person and the bedding/soil are wet and impure.
The wetness of the person or foot causes the bedding/soil to become wet, creating contact.
2
Check for the effect of impurity
Observe whether the effect of impurity (color, taste, or smell) appears on the body or foot after contact. This is the key condition.
If no effect is apparent, the impurity is presumed not to have transferred.
3
Apply the ruling
If the effect appears, the body part becomes impure (najis) and must be washed. If no effect appears, the body part remains pure.
The ruling is based on evidence, not mere assumption.
4
Understand the principle
The underlying principle is that impurity transfer requires manifest evidence. The Hanafi school relies on the idea that original purity (istishab) remains until change is confirmed.
This principle avoids unnecessary declarations of impurity and aligns with ease in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۷۳) اگر سونے والے کے لینے سے یا قدم کی تری سے بستر ابھیگ گیا یا مٹی بھیگ گئی اور یہ دونوں ناپاک ہیں، اور نجاست کا اثر بدن میں اور قدم میں ظاہر ہو گیا تو بدن اور قدم ناپاک ہو جائیں گے ، اور اگر نجاست کا اثر ظاہر نہیں ہوا تو نا پاک نہیں ہوں گے۔
تشریح : یہاں تین مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ نجاست کا اثر نمایاں طور پر دوسری چیز میں منتقل ہوا تو وہ چیز نا پاک ہوگی ، اور اگر

And if the effect of impurity does not appear, they do not become impure. Explanation: Here three issues are based on this principle: that if the effect of impurity is clearly transferred to another thing, then that thing becomes impure, and if...
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on transfer of impurity via wetness. If a person who is already impure (e.g., in a state of janabah or with najasah on body) lies on a bedding or stands on wet soil, and the wetness causes the impurity to transfer, then the contacted part (body or foot) becomes impure only if the effect of the impurity (color, taste, or smell) is manifest. If no effect appears, the contacted part remains pure. The commentator notes that three specific cases are built on this principle, but the text cuts off before enumerating them. The key principle is that impurity transfer requires visible manifestation of the impurity's properties.

Key Terms
اثر النجاسة (athar al-najasa): Effect of impurity: the visible, taste, or smell that indicates the presence of impurity (najasa) on a surface.

Key Takeaway

Transfer of Impurity Through Moisture: The Condition of Manifest Effect
Ruling on when sweat/foot moisture transfers impurity from bed/earth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when impurity transfers via moisture and identify the key condition (manifest effect).

Core Idea
Impurity only transfers when its effect is visibly or olfactorily manifest.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: when you come into contact with an impure surface that is moist, does the impurity transfer to you? The classical Hanafi texts provide a clear principle: transfer depends on whether the effect of the impurity becomes apparent. This lesson will walk you through the ruling, its proofs, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states that if a person's sweat or foot moisture wets an impure bed or earth, the body or foot becomes impure only if the effect of impurity appears. Otherwise, it does not.
2
Understand the condition
The key is manifest transfer: the impurity's color, smell, or taste must become visible on the recipient.
3
Examine the proofs
Three proofs are cited: the hadith of Umm Salamah (earth purifies), the hadith of stepping on impurity (earth purifies), and the athar of Ibn Abbas (dry impurity does not harm).
4
Apply the principle
In practice, this means that mere contact with a wet impure surface does not necessarily make one impure; one must check for visible signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(273) And if the bedding or earth becomes wet from the sweat of a sleeping person or the moisture of the foot, both are impure, and the effect of impurity appears on the body or foot, then the body and foot become impure; otherwise not. Translation: (273) If from the sweat of a sleeping person or the moisture of the foot, the bedding or earth becomes wet, and both are impure, and the effect of impurity appears on the body and foot, then the body and foot become impure. If the effect does not appear, they do not become impure. Commentary: Here three issues are based on the principle that if the effect of impurity is manifestly transferred, the thing becomes impure; if not, it is not considered impure due to umum balwa. Another principle: less than a dirham of heavy impurity is excused, etc. Explanation: Dry bed or earth was impure; person slept and sweat came, wetting the bed. If effect appears on body, body impure; otherwise not. Second example: foot on impure earth, moisture transfers; if effect appears on foot, it becomes impure. Proofs: (1) Hadith of Umm Salamah: the ground purifies what comes after. (2) Hadith: if one steps on impurity, the earth is a purification. (3) Ibn Abbas: if wet, wash; if dry, no harm. Glossary: ajtalla: became wet; firash: bedding; jaff: dry; laff: wrap; asr: squeeze.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This is a ruling with proofs, addressing when impurity transfers through moisture. The matn states that if sweat or foot moisture wets an impure bed or earth, and the effect of impurity (color, smell, taste) appears on the body or foot, then they become impure; otherwise not. The commentary explains that this is based on the principle of manifest transfer: impurity only transmits if its effect is clearly evident. The proofs include hadith of Umm Salamah, hadith of Abu Hurairah about earth purifying, and athar of Ibn Abbas differentiating between wet and dry impurity. The commentary also invokes the principle of umum balwa for villagers, and reiterates the excused amounts of impurity. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on how impurity spreads through moisture.

Key Terms
عرق (araq): Sweat; moisture secreted by the skin.
بلل (ball): Moisture; wetness.
فراش (firash): Bedding; any spread on the ground.
اجتل (ajtalla): Became wet (from the root ball).

Dry Cloth Wrapped in Wet Impure Cloth: The Squeeze Criterion
Ruling on dry cloth not becoming impure from non-dripping wet impure cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that determines when a dry cloth becomes impure by contact with a wet impure cloth, and apply the squeeze test to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Impurity transfers only with a perceptible flow of moisture, not with mere dampness.

This lesson clarifies a common taharah scenario: does a dry, pure cloth become impure if wrapped in a wet, impure cloth? The Hanafi ruling hinges on the quantity of moisture in the wet cloth. If the wet cloth can be squeezed to produce a drip, impurity transfers; otherwise the dry cloth remains pure. We will parse the legal criterion and apply it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its components
The act is wrapping a dry, pure cloth in a wet, impure cloth. Note the two items: one is dry and pure, the other is wet and impure. The key action is wrapping (laff) which brings them into contact.
2
Determine the key variable: wetness quantity
The wetness of the impure cloth is not absolute; it is specified as being 'such that if squeezed, it does not drip.' This indicates a very small amount of moisture.
3
Apply the squeeze test (asr)
Imagine squeezing the wet cloth. If a drop of water falls, the moisture is sufficient to carry impurity. If no drop falls, the moisture is insufficient and impurity does not transfer to the dry cloth.
The criterion is the ability to produce a drip, not just feeling damp.
4
State the ruling based on the test
If the wet cloth does not drip when squeezed, the dry cloth remains pure (tahir). If it does drip, the dry cloth becomes impure where the moisture reaches.
5
Connect to the broader Hanafi principle
This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that impurity (najasa) transfers only when the carrier is a flowing substance (sai'l). Mere dampness without flow is not sufficient.
Compare with other scenarios like a hand touching a wet impure surface.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۷۴) جیسا کہ پاک سوکھا کپڑا نا پاک نہیں ہوگا اگر تر ناپاک کپڑے میں لپیٹ دیا جائے ، اس حال میں کہ ترکپڑا کو نچوڑے تو نچوڑا نہ جائے۔
تشریح : ناپاک کپڑا بھیگا ہوا ہے لیکن اس میں پانی اتنا کم ہے کہ اس کو نچوڑے تو ایک قطرہ بھی پانی نہ گرے، ایسے کپڑے میں خشک پاک کپڑا لپیٹ دیا جائے اور اس میں ہلکی سی نمی آجائے
Translation: (274) Just as a dry, pure cloth does not become impure if it is wrapped in a wet, impure cloth, in a condition that the wet cloth is such that if squeezed, it does not drip. Commentary: The impure cloth is wet, but the water in it is so little that if squeezed, not a single drop of water falls. If a dry, pure cloth is wrapped in such a cloth, and a slight moisture transfers to it, [it does not become impure].
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This is a brief ruling. It states that a dry, pure cloth does not become impure by being wrapped in a wet impure cloth when the wet cloth is so dry that no water can be squeezed out of it. The commentary clarifies that if the wet cloth has insufficient water to drip, the slight moisture that transfers is not enough to carry impurity. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that impurity only transfers with a perceptible quantity of moisture that can flow or be squeezed out.

Key Terms
جاف (jaff): Dry; opposite of wet.
لف (laff): To wrap; to fold one thing around another.
عصر (asr): To squeeze; to press out liquid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A dry pure cloth is wrapped in a wet impure cloth. When does the dry cloth become impure?
A) Always.
B) Only if the wet cloth drips when squeezed.
C) Only if the dry cloth becomes moist.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
Impurity transfers only when the wet cloth can be squeezed to drip; mere dampness does not suffice.

Conditions for Transfer of Impurity and Purification by Removal of Essence
Rulings with proofs on impurity transfer and purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for impurity transfer and explain that removal of the essence suffices for purification, applying these rules to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Impurity transfers only when its effect visibly appears; purification requires only removal of its essence, even with one wash.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on how impurity (najasah) transfers through contact and how to become pure again. The key principle is that transfer is not automatic—it requires the impurity's effect to manifest. We also learn that purification is achieved by removing the substance of the impurity, regardless of the number of washes. The proofs from the Sunnah and the Companion Ibn Abbas reinforce these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule for impurity transfer
The passage begins with the foot stepping on impurity: the foot becomes impure only if the impurity’s effect (e.g., wetness) appears. This sets the principle of zuhur al-athar (manifestation of effect).
Dry impurity on a dry foot does not transfer.
2
Apply the rule to dry cloth in wet impure cloth
A dry pure cloth wrapped in a wet impure cloth that does not drip when squeezed remains pure because no effect transfers.
The absence of dripping indicates insufficient wetness to carry impurity.
3
Apply the rule to wet cloth on dry impure ground
A wet cloth spread on dry impure ground does not become impure unless the impurity’s effect appears on the cloth.
Dry ground does not transfer impurity even if the cloth is wet, unless the ground’s impurity becomes visible.
4
Apply the rule to wind-borne impurity
If wind blows impurity onto a cloth, the cloth remains pure unless the effect of the impurity is visible on it.
This reflects the principle of 'umum balwa' (general affliction) where minor unavoidable impurities are overlooked.
5
Understand the purification ruling and its proofs
The passage concludes that removal of the essence of impurity purifies the object, even with one wash, and cites three proofs: the hadith of Umm Salama, the hadith of Abu Huraira on dry earth, and the statement of Ibn Abbas.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

Chapter of Impurities and Purification from Them. And the foot becomes impure or not. (24) Similarly, a dry pure cloth does not become impure if wrapped in a wet impure cloth that does not drip when squeezed. (275) And a wet cloth does not become impure by spreading it over dry impure ground, if the ground becomes damp from it. Commentary
This passage presents several rulings from the Hanafi school on how impurity (najasah) transfers from one object to another through contact, along with their proofs from Hadith and athar. The opening ruling states that a foot stepping on impure ground only becomes impure if the impurity's effect (e.g., color, smell) visibly transfers. This is based on the principle of 'zuhur al-athar' (manifestation of effect). The same principle applies to a dry cloth wrapped in a wet impure cloth that does not drip when squeezed—since no effect transfers, the cloth remains pure. Similarly, a wet cloth spread on dry impure ground does not become impure unless the ground's impurity transfers to the cloth. Wind blowing impurity onto a cloth is also excused unless the effect is visible. Finally, removal of the essence of a visible impurity (even in one wash) suffices for purification. The proofs include the hadith of Umm Salama on the long garment, the hadith of stepping on impurity with sandals, and the saying of Ibn Abbas distinguishing wet and dry impurity. These rulings reflect the Hanafi principle of 'general affliction' (umum balwa) where minor unavoidable impurities are overlooked.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najasah): Impurity that prevents validity of prayer unless removed; classified into ghaliẓah and khafifah.
طهور (tahur): Purifier; something that removes or renders impurity ineffective.
عصر (asr): To squeeze or wring out liquid from a cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Impurity transfers only when its effect visibly manifests; purification is achieved by removing the essence, even with one wash.

Wind-Blown Impurity: Purity Unless Effect Appears
Ruling: garment hit by wind-blown impurity stays pure unless effect appears

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wind-blown impurity and identify when a garment becomes impure based on visible effect.

Core Idea
A garment struck by wind-blown dry impurity remains pure unless a visible trace appears.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: dry impurity carried by wind landing on a garment. The Hanafi school provides a clear principle based on the Prophet's guidance to Asma bint Abi Bakr. We examine the ruling and its proof, and see why the appearance of a visible effect is decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the scenario? Wind blows over dry impurity and hits a garment. The ruling: the garment is pure (tahir) unless a visible effect (color, smell, taste) appears on it.
The default is purity; impurity requires evidence.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Asma bint Abi Bakr (Sunan Abi Dawud, Hadith 363), where the Prophet instructed to rinse only if blood is seen.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The instruction to rinse only if blood is seen implies that impurity without visibility does not necessitate washing. Thus, for wind-blown impurity, the same principle applies: no effect, no impurity.
The presence of the word 'رأى' (saw) indicates visibility as the criterion.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that if the garment is wet, impurity is transferred regardless of visible effect. They consider the moisture as a medium.
The Hanafi school disagrees, insisting on a visible trace.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view because it is based on a clear hadith and the principle of certainty (istihsan). Practical hardship is also reduced.
Later Hanafi scholars like al-Marghinani affirm this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بريح هبت على نجاسة فاصابت الثوب الا ان يظهر اثرها فيه
Nor by wind that blew over impurity and struck a garment unless its effect appears in it.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This is the second part of the matn from the previous lesson. It deals with dry impurity that is carried by the wind and lands on a garment. The ruling is that the garment does not become impure unless a visible effect (like color or smell) appears on it. The Urdu commentary explains that if the wind blows over dry impurity and it lands on a cloth that has slight moisture but no trace is visible, the cloth remains pure. The principle (usul) stated is: 'If the visible effect of impurity appears on cloth or body, it becomes impure; if not, it remains pure.' This is based on the hadith from Asma bint Abi Bakr as mentioned in the first lesson. The term 'sabba' (هبت) refers to the blowing of wind.

Key Terms
هبت (habbat): Blow (of wind).
اثر (athar): Visible trace of impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Impure because the wind carried impurity
B) Pure because the garment is dry
C) Impure only if the impurity was liquid
D) Pure unless a visible effect appears

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that impurity from dry wind-blown sources only affects a garment if a visible trace appears; otherwise, the garment remains pure.

Purification from Visible Impurity
Ruling: visible impurity removal suffices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification from visible impurity, apply the condition of substance removal, and justify it with evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Visible impurity is purified by removal of its substance, even with one wash; difficult traces are excused.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling of Hanafi taharah: how to purify an object that has been contaminated with a visible impurity such as blood or wine. The matn gives a concise statement, and we will unpack its meaning, the evidence from the Sunnah, and the practical implications. Understanding this ruling is essential for daily worship and avoiding unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tat'hir (purification) of an object contaminated with a visible impurity (najis mar'iyyah). The ruling: the object becomes pure (tahir) when the substance (ayn) of the impurity is completely removed. This holds even if only one wash achieves that removal.
2
Locate the dalil
The matn's proof is drawn from the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish and the hadith of Abu Hurairah. In the first, the Prophet (peace be upon him) told the mustahadah to wash the blood and pray, without specifying a number. In the second, he said, 'It suffices you to wash the blood, and its effect will not harm you.'
The hadiths are ahad, but their meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'wash the blood' (al-amr) indicates that the removal of the blood itself is the operative factor. The addition 'its effect will not harm you' explicitly excuses traces that are difficult to remove. This shows that the purity is achieved by eliminating the substance, not by a set number of washes or by the complete disappearance of color or odour.
Hanafi usul: al-amr mufid lil-wujub, but here it indicates sufficiency because the goal is removal.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, some earlier scholars (e.g., Ibn Abi Layla) held that three washes are required even for visible impurities. The correct (sahih) position, adopted by the majority including Abu Hanifa and the later masters, is that removal suffices. Other schools like the Shafi'i require a specific number of washes for certain impurities (e.g., seven for dogs) even after substance is removed.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi preference for removal over number is based on the literal meaning of the hadith and the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). The mufta bihi is the sahih position: one wash is sufficient if the substance is gone. This is the ruling relied upon for fatwa.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويطهر متنجس بنجاسة مرئية بزوال عينها ولو بمرة على الصحيح. (۲۷۸) ولا يضر بقاء اثر شق زواله . (۲۷۹)
And an object impure with visible impurity is purified by the removal of its substance, even if by one wash, according to the correct view. (278) And the remaining effect whose removal is difficult does not harm. (279)
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This lesson covers two interrelated rulings in the matn (277 and 278) focusing on visible impurity. The first (277) states that an item made impure by a visible impurity (such as blood or wine) is purified once the substance (ayn) of the impurity is removed, even if this requires only a single wash. This is the correct (sahih) position of the madhhab. The proof is from the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish where the Prophet told the mustahadah to wash the blood and pray, without specifying a number of washes, indicating that removal of the substance is sufficient. The second ruling (278) adds that if a trace (such as color) remains after washing and is difficult to remove, it does not harm the purity. The evidence includes the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'It suffices you to wash the blood, and its effect will not harm you' (Sunan Abi Dawud). Also, the hadith from Aisha about using yellow dye to cover the stain indicates that if the color persists, it is excusable. The principle of sharia not imposing hardship is also invoked. The Urdu commentary elaborates on these points, citing the hadiths and explaining that difficulty removes obligation.

Key Terms
مرئية (mar'iyyah): Visible impurity that can be seen with the naked eye.
عين (ayn): Substance or physical body of the impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many washes are required to purify a garment stained with a visible impurity like blood?
A) Exactly three washes are required.
B) It must be washed until the color is completely gone.
C) One wash is sufficient if the substance is removed.
D) Seven washes are required, like for a dog.

Key Takeaway
Purification from visible impurity is achieved by removing the substance itself; once the substance is gone, the object is pure, even if a difficult trace remains.

Non-Visible Impurity: Three Washes and Wringing
Ruling: non-visible impurity requires three washes and wringing each time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying non-visible impurities and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Non-visible impurities require three washes with wringing each time—based on qiyas from the hand-washing hadith.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on purifying items affected by non-visible impurities such as urine or alcohol. The ruling specifies three washes with wringing after each wash. We will explore the textual evidence and the analogical reasoning that supports this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impurity type
Determine whether the impurity is non-visible (like dried urine or alcohol) or visible. The ruling applies only to non-visible impurities.
If the impurity is visible, the ruling is different: the trace must be removed.
2
State the required action
The Hanafi school requires washing the affected item three times, and after each wash, it must be wrung out (or squeezed) to expel the water containing the impurity.
Wringing is essential; without it, the purification is incomplete.
3
Identify the evidence
The proof is from the hadith of Abu Huraira: the Prophet ordered washing the hand three times after waking, as it may carry non-visible impurity. Also, the hadith about a dog licking a vessel orders three washes.
Both hadith are ahad (single-chain), so the dalala is zanni.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The command for three washes is for a case where impurity is non-visible. Through qiyas (analogy), the ruling is extended to all non-visible impurities on garments or vessels.
The effective cause (illa) is the presence of non-visible impurity that dissolves in water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغير المرئية
And the non-visible [impurity is purified by washing three times and wringing each time].
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This lesson addresses purification from non-visible impurities (e.g., urine, wine) that have no visible trace. The ruling is that the item must be washed three times, and each time it must be wrung out (or squeezed) to remove the absorbed impurity. The proof is from the hadith of Abu Hurairah about washing the hand after waking up: the Prophet instructed to wash it three times because one does not know where the hand spent the night. Since the impurity (if any) is not visible, three washes are prescribed by analogy. Similarly, the hadith about a dog licking a vessel requires three washes (in one narration). The Urdu commentary explains that wringing is necessary to extract the water containing the impurity. Three washes ensure the removal of the non-visible impurity. This is the standard Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
غير مرئية (ghayr mar'iyyah): Non-visible impurity, such as urine or alcohol, that cannot be seen.
تعصر (tu'sar): Wringing out the water from the fabric after each wash.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Wash it three times and wring it out after each wash.
C) Wash it seven times, one of which with soil.
D) Sprinkle water over it until the impurity is removed.

Key Takeaway
Non-visible impurities are purified by washing three times and wringing each time, based on the hadith of the hand and qiyas.

Purification of Visible Impurity and Excusing Residual Traces
Ruling on visible impurity purification and excusing difficult residue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying a visible impurity and explain under what conditions a residual trace is excused.

Core Idea
Visible impurity is purified by removing its substance; a stain that is hard to remove does not harm.

This lesson addresses two connected rulings: first, how to purify a garment from visible impurity, and second, what to do if a trace remains. The Hanafi school holds that removal of the substance itself suffices, even with a single wash, and any residual colour or stain that is difficult to remove is excused. The evidence comes from the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish and other narrations, as well as the general principle that Shariah does not impose excessive hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on purifying a visible impurity (e.g., blood) on a garment. It states that purification is achieved by removing the substance (zawāl al-‘ayn), even with one wash. This is marked as 'ala al-sahih (the correct view).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish (from Muslim) is cited: the Prophet instructed her to wash the blood and pray, without specifying a number of washes. This indicates that removal of the substance is the key.
The imperative 'faghsil' (wash) implies obligation, but the absence of a fixed number allows for one wash if removal occurs.
3
Examine the second ruling on residual traces
The passage adds that any remaining effect (athar) that is difficult to remove does not invalidate purification. Two additional hadith support this: Abu Huraira's narration where the Prophet explicitly said 'its effect does not harm you', and Aisha's instruction to change a stubborn stain with something yellow (safrah).
The general principle that Shariah does not burden with hardship is also invoked.
4
Note the authority weight
The first ruling is marked as 'ala al-sahih, indicating it is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school. The second ruling is also standard, with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf mentioned.
Cross-madhhab: other schools may require multiple washes even after removal of substance.

Chapter of impurities and purification from them. Visible [impurity] is [purified] by removal of its substance even if once according to the correct [view]. (278) And the remaining effect whose removal is difficult does not harm.
