(2) This hadith also: I asked Aisha about a menstruating woman whose garment gets blood on it? She said: Wash it; if the effect does not go, then change it with something yellow. This passage presents two connected rulings from the Hanafi school on visible impurities (najāsat mar'iyya). First, such impurities are purified simply by removing the visible substance, even with a single wash. The hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaish supports this: the Prophet instructed her to wash the blood without specifying a number, indicating that removal is the key. Second, if after washing a stain or trace remains that is difficult to remove, it does not invalidate the purification. Three proofs are given: the hadith of Abu Huraira where the Prophet explicitly says 'its effect does not harm you'; the hadith of Aisha where she recommends changing the stain with something yellow (safrah) rather than insisting on complete removal; and the general principle that Shariah does not impose excessive hardship. These rulings apply to all visible impurities such as blood, urine if visible, etc. The text marks the first ruling as 'ala al-sahih (the correct view), indicating it is the relied-upon position within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مرئية (mar'iyya): Visible impurity that has a perceptible substance, such as blood or solid stool.
اثر (athar): The residual trace (e.g., colour) of an impurity that remains after washing the substance.
على الصحيح (ala al-sahih): According to the correct view; indicating the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum requirement to purify a garment from visible impurity like blood?
A) Washing three times
B) Removing the substance, even with one wash
C) Scrubbing until no stain remains
D) Washing with a specific quantity of water

Key Takeaway
Visible impurity is purified by removing its substance; a residual stain that is hard to remove is excused.

Purification of Non-Visible Impurity: Three Washes with Squeezing
Ruling with three proofs from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying non-visible impurities and derive it from the cited ahadith.

Core Idea
Non-visible impurities require three washes with squeezing each time — a ruling derived from prophetic practice.

This passage addresses the purification of non-visible impurities (like urine or wine) that leave no visible trace. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific method: three washes, each followed by squeezing to remove the impurity-laden water. The author cites three hadith to support this requirement, using analogy (qiyas) to extend the ruling from specific cases to all non-visible impurities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impurity type
The passage distinguishes between visible and non-visible impurities. Non-visible impurities have no discernible substance (e.g., urine after drying, wine that evaporates).
Hanafi categorizes najasah as 'ayniyya (visible) and ghayr 'ayniyya (non-visible).
2
State the ruling
The ruling is: wash three times, squeezing after each wash. This is the wajib (obligatory) method.
Squeezing ensures the impurity-laden water is fully expelled.
3
Examine the first dalil (hand washing after sleep)
The hadith commands washing the hand three times when there is doubt of contamination (non-visible impurity). By qiyas, definite non-visible impurity also requires three washes.
Hadith from Muslim: 'When one of you wakes from sleep, do not dip his hand until he washes it three times.'
4
Examine the second dalil (dog lapping)
The hadith about a dog licking a vessel orders three washes. Dog saliva is a non-visible impurity, so the same rule applies by analogy.
Hadith from Dar Qutni: 'When a dog laps from a vessel, pour it out then wash it three times.'
5
Examine the third dalil (menstrual blood)
The hadith instructs rubbing menstrual blood with water (taqruṣ), which implies squeezing action. This demonstrates the need to expel impurity through pressure.
Hadith from Muslim: 'Scrape it, then rub it with water, then sprinkle it.'

ترجمه : (۲۷۹) اور جونجاست غیر مرئی سے ناپاک ہو تو وہ تین بار دھونے اور ہر بار نچوڑنے سے پاک ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح : جو نجاست نظر نہ آتی ہو جیسے پیشاب، شراب، تو اس کو تین مرتبہ دھوئے اور ہر مرتبہ نچوڑے تو پاک ہو جائے گا۔ ہر مرتبہ اس لئے نچوڑے تا کہ تمام نجاست نکل جائے۔
وجه : (۱) عن ابي هريرة ان النبى الله قال اذا استيقظ احدكم من نومه فلا يغمس يده في الاناء حتى يغسلها ثلاثا فانه لا يدرى اين باتت يده - (مسلم شریف، باب كراهته خمس المتوضی وغیرہ یدہ المشکوک فی نجاستھا فی الاناء قبل غسلها ثلاثا ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۶۴۳/۲۷۸) یہاں نجاست غیر مرئیہ ہے تو تین مرتبہ دھونے کے لئے کہا گیا تو اور نجاست غیر مرئیہ میں بھی تین مرتبہ دھویا جائے ۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال اذا ولغ الكلب فى الاناء فاهرقه ثم اغسله ثلاث مرات (دار قطنی ، باب ولوغ الكلب في الاناء، ج اول ص ۶۶ نمبر ۱۹۳ / مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب الكلب بلغ في الاناء ، ج اول ص ۷۶، نمبر ۳۳۶) اس حدیث میں کتے کا جوٹھا غیر مرئی نجاست ہے جسکو تین مرتبہ دھونے سے پاک قرار دیا اس سے استدلال کیا کہ کسی بھی غیر مرئی نجاست کو تین مرتبہ دھونے سے پاک ہو جائے گا۔ (۳) اور ہر مرتبہ نچوڑے اس کی دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن اسماء قالت : جائت امرأة الى النبى الله الله فقالت احدانا يصيب ثوبها من دم الحيضة ، كيف تصنع به ؟ قال : تحته ، ثم تقرصه بالماء ثم تنضحه ثم تصلى فيه - (مسلم شریف، باب نجاسة الدم وكيفية غسله ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۶۷۵/۲۹۱ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في مغسل دم الحيض من الثوب ، ص ۳۵ نمبر ۱۳۸) اس حدیث میں حیض کے خون کو پانی سے رگڑنے کا ذکر ہے جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نجاست کو نکالنے کے لئے نچوڑنا پڑے گا تا کہ پورے طور پر نجاست نکل جائے۔
And non-visible [impurity] is [purified] by washing it three times and squeezing each time. Translation: (279) And whatever becomes impure with non-visible impurity, it becomes pure by washing three times and squeezing each time. Explanation: That which is not visible, like urine, wine, then wash it three times and squeeze each time; it will become pure. Squeeze each time so that all the impurity comes out. Proof: (1) From Abu Huraira that the Prophet said: When one of you wakes from sleep, do not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night. (Muslim) Here the impurity is non-visible, so three washes are commanded; so also for other non-visible impurities, wash three times. (2) From Abu Huraira: When a dog laps from a vessel, pour it out then wash it three times. (Dar Qutni) In this hadith, the dog's saliva is non-visible impurity, declared pure by washing three times; analogy is made that any non-visible impurity becomes pure by three washes. (3) And squeeze each time: its proof in this hadith: Asma said: A woman came to the Prophet and said: One of us gets menstrual blood on her garment; what should she do? He said: She should scrape it, then rub it with water, then sprinkle it, then pray in it. (Muslim) In this hadith, there is mention of rubbing menstrual blood with water, which indicates that squeezing is needed to extract the impurity fully.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling for non-visible impurities (najāsat ghayr mar'iyya), such as urine or wine, that have no visible substance. The rule: such impurities require the affected item (garment, vessel, etc.) to be washed three times, with squeezing each time. The squeezing ensures that the impurity-laden water is completely expelled. Three proofs are cited: (1) The hadith about washing hands after sleep (since there is doubt about contamination) commands three washes for a non-visible impurity; (2) The hadith about a dog licking a vessel also uses three washes, and by qiyas all non-visible impurities follow this; (3) The hadith of Asma mentions a scraping/rubbing action (taqruṣ) which is akin to squeezing, demonstrating the need to extract the impurity. The Hanafi school holds this as the minhāj (standard procedure) for non-visible impurities. There is no alternative view mentioned in this text.

Key Terms
غير مرئية (ghayr mar'iyya): Non-visible impurity, such as urine or wine, that has no discernible substance on the item.
عصر (aṣr): Squeezing the garment after each wash to expel the impurity-laden water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Twice

Key Takeaway

Purification with Any Flowing Liquid That Removes Impurity
Ruling on purifying garments and body with any flowing liquid, not just water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification using any flowing liquid and apply it to examples such as vinegar or rose water, distinguishing it from the view of other schools that require water.

Core Idea
Any flowing liquid that removes impurity can purify – water is not exclusive in Hanafi fiqh.

You have learned that water is the primary purifier, but the Hanafi school expands purification to any flowing liquid that effectively removes impurity (mā'i' muzīl). This lesson presents the ruling, its evidence from the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), and the underlying principle that removal of impurity itself is the key.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm? The act is purifying a garment or body from visible impurity. The ruling (hukm) is that it is valid (sahih) using water OR any flowing liquid that removes the impurity.
The passage explicitly contrasts water with other liquids like vinegar and rose water.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The primary evidence is the hadith of Aisha where she used saliva (not water) to moisten and remove menstrual blood from her garment. The second is the common practice of rubbing a shoe on the ground to remove impurity.
Both proofs show that water is not essential; removal is the key.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the dalil prove the ruling? The hadith explicitly uses saliva (a non-water liquid) to remove impurity, and this was accepted as purification. The shoe analogy shows that rubbing (mechanical removal) suffices without water.
The wajh is that the liquid need not be water; any liquid that removes is acceptable.
4
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, the Shafi'i and Maliki schools generally require water for purification. They base on general Quranic commands to use water. Hanafi responds that the specific hadith overrides the general, and the principle is removal.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both sides have valid evidence.

تشریح : نجاست مرئی میں اصل بنیاد یہ ہے کہ وہ زائل ہو جائے تو کپڑا یا بدن پاک ہو جائے گا، چنانچہ پانی کے علاوہ کسی بہنے والی چیز سے جو نجاست کو زائل کرنے والی ہونجاست زائل کر دی جائے تو پاک ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ اصل بنیاد نجاست کا زائل ہونا ہے۔

(بخاری شریف، باب حل تصلي المرأة فى ثوب حاضت فيه، ص ۵۴ نمبر ۳۱۲ / ابوداؤد شریف باب المرأة تغسل ٹو بھا الذى تلبسه فی حیضها، ص ۶۴ نمبر ۳۶۴) خون سب کے نزدیک ناپاک ہے اور اس کو تھوک سے تر کر کے ناخن سے رگڑ دیا اور خون زائل ہو گیا تو وہ چیز پاک ہو جائے گی ، اور ظاہر ہے کہ تھوک پانی نہیں ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ پانی کے علاوہ سے بھی ناپاک چیز پاک ہو سکتی ہے (۲) جوتے پر نجاست لگی ہو اور زمین پر رگڑ دیا جائے اور نجاست زائل ہو جائے تو جوتا پاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ اصل قاعدہ یہی ہے کہ نجاست کے زیلان سے کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا۔
لغت : مائع : بہنے والی چیز ۔ مزیل : زائل کرنے والی۔ الخل : سرکہ۔ ماءالورد: گلاب کا پانی ،گلاب کارس۔
And impurity on garment and body is purified by water and by every flowing liquid that removes [impurity] like vinegar and rose water. Translation: (280) Impurity on garment and body will become pure by water and by every flowing thing that removes impurity, such as vinegar and rose water. Explanation: For visible impurity, the basic principle is that if it is removed, the garment or body becomes pure; thus if it is removed by a flowing liquid other than water that can remove impurity, it becomes pure, because the fundamental basis is removal of impurity. Proof: (1) There is a hadith. Aisha said: One of us had only one garment in which she menstruated; when something of blood got on it, she would moisten it with her saliva and scrape it with her nail. (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) Blood is impure by consensus, and she moistened it with saliva (which is not water) and scraped it; the blood was removed, so the garment became pure. So it is known that items other than water can purify. (2) If impurity gets on a shoe and it is rubbed on the ground, and the impurity is removed, the shoe becomes pure. This indicates that the basic rule is that removal of impurity purifies. Vocabulary: mā'i' (flowing liquid), muzīl (removing), khal (vinegar), mā' al-ward (rose water).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage expands the scope of purification beyond water. The Hanafi ruling is that any flowing liquid (mā'i') that effectively removes the impurity (muzīl) can be used to purify the garment or body. Examples given include vinegar and rose water. The key is removal of the impurity itself, not the use of water exclusively. Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Aisha where she used saliva (spit) to moisten menstrual blood and then scraped it off with her nail, and this was considered purification. Saliva is not water, so this demonstrates that water is not necessary. (2) The common practice of rubbing a shoe on the ground to remove impurity, which shows that rubbing and removal suffice. The passage also clarifies that this applies to visible impurities; for non-visible impurities, the earlier rule (three washes with squeezing) stands. The lexical notes define key terms: mā'i' (flowing liquid), muzīl (removing agent), khal (vinegar), mā' al-ward (rose water).

Key Terms
مائع (mā'i'): A flowing liquid; any substance that flows and can be used to remove impurity, such as vinegar, rose water, etc.
مزيل (muzīl): That which removes the impurity; the agent used to eliminate the najāsah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Any flowing liquid that removes impurity (mā'i' muzīl) purifies garment and body in Hanafi fiqh; water is not exclusive.

Purification of Leather Items by Rubbing for Thick Impurities
Ruling on purifying leather by rubbing for thick impurities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on purification of leather items by rubbing for thick impurities (jirm) and distinguish it from cases requiring washing.

Core Idea
Rubbing suffices to purify leather from thick impurities because leather does not absorb them.

This lesson presents a special Hanafi ruling on purifying leather items like socks (khuff) from thick impurities (jirm). Unlike thin impurities that require washing, thick ones can be removed by simple rubbing (dalk). The ruling is based on the material's non-absorption of thick substances. Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary hardship in daily purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item and impurity type
The ruling applies to leather items (khuff and similar) and thick impurities (jirm). Determine if the impurity is thick (e.g., dung) or thin (e.g., urine).
Thick impurities have substance (jirm); thin do not.
2
State the purification method
For thick impurities, rubbing (dalk) suffices. For thin impurities, washing is required.
The method differs based on thickness.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The proof is based on leather's non-absorption of thick impurities. Since they remain on the surface, rubbing removes them effectively.
The text cuts off but the rationale is clear from the explanation.
4
Consider cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may require washing for all impurities on leather, regardless of thickness. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
Know the practical difference when following a different madhhab.

And the khuff (leather sock) and similar [items] are purified by rubbing from an impurity that has substance, even if it is [wet]. Translation: (281) Leather sock and similar [items] will become pure by rubbing if the impurity is thick, even if it is wet. Explanation: All leather items, such as the leather sock, etc., if wet and moist impurity gets on it and it is thick like dung, then by rubbing it clean, the leather sock becomes pure. But if it is not thick like urine, then the leather sock must be washed. Proof: (1) Leather does not absorb thick impurity deeply, and whatever is on the surface will become clean by rubbing, so the leather sock [becomes pure].

Commentary
This passage provides a special ruling for leather items (such as the khuff, or leather socks) regarding purification from impurities. The Hanafi rule: if the impurity is 'jirm' (thick/has substance), even if it is wet, rubbing (dalk) suffices for purification. Examples of thick impurities include dung or mud. For thinner impurities like urine, washing is required. The rationale (mentioned briefly) is that leather does not absorb thick impurities deeply, so surface rubbing is sufficient. The text cuts off before completing the proof, but the reasoning is clear from the commentary. This ruling applies to all similar leather objects, not just socks. It is specific to the Hanafi school, leveraging the principle of mashaqqah (hardship) in frequently removing such impurities.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): Leather sock worn over the foot, often used for wiping (mash) in wudu; here it refers to any leather footwear.
دلك (dalk): Rubbing the item to physically remove the impurity without water flow.
جرم (jirm): Thick substance; an impurity that has a solid or viscous consistency, like dung.

Taharah — Purification

Purification with Any Flowing Liquid
States ruling and proof for purifying with any liquid that removes impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification with non-water liquids and cite the hadith evidence for this position.

Core Idea
Any flowing liquid that removes impurity purifies – the removal itself, not the substance, is the criterion.

In this passage, we learn a distinctive Hanafi ruling: impurity on clothes or body can be removed not only by water but by any flowing liquid that eliminates the impurity, such as vinegar or rose water. This ruling is based on the principle that purification is achieved by the removal of the filth (izalat al-najasah), and the evidence comes from the practice of the Companions. Let's examine the proof and understand why the Hanafi school takes this view, contrary to other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purification of najasah (impurity) from clothes and body. The ruling is that it is achieved with water and with every flowing liquid that removes the impurity. Note: the hukm of purification itself is obligatory for prayer; this passage describes the valid method.
The term 'mā'i' muzīl' is key: a flowing liquid that removes.
2
Locate the dalīl
The text cites two ahadith: (1) Hadith of Asma about menstrual blood – the Prophet instructed to scratch, rub with water, and sprinkle. (2) Hadith of Aisha – she used saliva (not water) to remove blood from her garment, then scratched with her nail.
Both are ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
From Asma's hadith: the rubbing and wringing indicate that removal is the goal. From Aisha's hadith: saliva is a non-water liquid that removed blood, proving that any liquid that removes impurity suffices. The common element is the removal itself.
The principle: al-istinā' bi al-izālah lā bi al-mā'.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
Other schools (e.g., Shāfiʿī) restrict purification to water only, based on general commands to use water. They interpret Aisha's action as specific to her or as a case of necessity.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf; the Hanafīs argue the removal principle is primary.
5
Evaluate the Hanafī tarjīḥ
The Hanafī position is muftā bihi based on the clear practice of the Sahābah and the principle that removal of najāsah is the basis, not the substance. The texts indicate that any mā'i' muzīl works.
The shoe analogy further supports: rubbing on ground removes impurity.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الانجاس و الطهارة عنها
بـغـسـلـهـا ثلاثا والعصر كل مرة . (۲۸۰) وتطهر النجاسة عن الثوب والبدن بالماء و بكل مائع مزيل كالخل و ماء الورد.
اس حدیث میں کتے کا جوٹھا غیر مرئی نجاست ہے جسکو تین مرتبہ دھونے سے پاک قرار دیا اس سے استدلال کیا کہ کسی بھی غیر مرئی نجاست کو تین مرتبہ دھونے سے پاک ہو جائے گا۔ (۳) اور ہر مرتبہ نچوڑے اس کی دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن اسماء قالت : جائت امرأة الى النبى الله الله فقالت احدانا يصيب ثوبها من دم الحيضة ، كيف تصنع به ؟ قال : تحته ، ثم تقرصه بالماء ثم تنضحه ثم تصلى فيه - (مسلم شریف، باب نجاسة الدم وكيفية غسله ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۶۷۵/۲۹۱ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في مغسل دم الحيض من الثوب ، ص ۳۵ نمبر ۱۳۸) اس حدیث میں حیض کے خون کو پانی سے رگڑنے کا ذکر ہے جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نجاست کو نکالنے کے لئے نچوڑنا پڑے گا تا کہ پورے طور پر نجاست نکل جائے۔ ترجمه : (۲۸۰) کپڑے سے اور بدن سے نجاست پاک ہوگی پانی کے ذریعہ اور ہر بہنے والی چیز کے ذریعہ جو نجاست زائل کرتی ہو، جیسے سرکہ، اور گلاب کا پانی۔
تشریح : نجاست مرئی میں اصل بنیاد یہ ہے کہ وہ زائل ہو جائے تو کپڑا یا بدن پاک ہو جائے گا، چنانچہ پانی کے علاوہ کسی بہنے والی چیز سے جو نجاست کو زائل کرنے والی ہونجاست زائل کر دی جائے تو پاک ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ اصل بنیاد نجاست کا زائل ہونا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ قالت عائشة ما كان لاحد انا الا ثوب واحد تحيض فيه فاذا اصابه شيء من دم قالت بريقها فقصعته بظفرها. (بخاری شریف، باب حل تصلي المرأة فى ثوب حاضت فيه، ص ۵۴ نمبر ۳۱۲ / ابوداؤد شریف باب المرأة تغسل ٹو بھا الذى تلبسه فی حیضها، ص ۶۴ نمبر ۳۶۴) خون سب کے نزدیک ناپاک ہے اور اس کو تھوک سے تر کر کے ناخن سے رگڑ دیا اور خون زائل ہو گیا تو وہ چیز پاک ہو جائے گی ، اور ظاہر ہے کہ تھوک پانی نہیں ہے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ پانی کے علاوہ سے بھی ناپاک چیز پاک ہو سکتی ہے (۲) جوتے پر نجاست لگی ہو اور زمین پر رگڑ دیا جائے اور نجاست زائل ہو جائے تو جوتا پاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ اصل قاعدہ یہی ہے کہ نجاست کے زیلان سے کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ لغت : مائع : بہنے والی چیز ۔ مزیل : زائل کرنے والی۔ الخل : سرکہ۔ ماءالورد: گلاب کا پانی ،گلاب کارس۔
Chapter of Impurities and Purification from Them. Wash it three times and wring each time. (280) Impurity is purified from clothes and body with water and with every flowing liquid that removes [impurity], like vinegar and rose water. In this hadith, the leftover of a dog is an invisible impurity which is declared pure by washing three times. From this it is inferred that any invisible impurity will become pure by washing thrice. (3) And wring each time. Its proof is in this hadith: From Asma who said: A woman came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'One of us finds the blood of menstruation on her garment, what should she do?' He said: 'Scratch it, then rub it with water, then sprinkle it, then pray in it.' (Muslim, Abu Dawood) In this hadith, rubbing the menstrual blood with water is mentioned, which indicates that for removing impurity, wringing is necessary so that the impurity is completely removed. Translation (280): Impurity will be purified from clothes and body by water and by every flowing thing that removes impurity, such as vinegar and rose water. Explanation: For visible impurity, the basic principle is that if it is removed, the cloth or body becomes pure. So if impurity is removed by any flowing thing besides water that removes it, it becomes pure, because the basic principle is the removal of impurity. Proof: (1) In a hadith, Aisha said: 'Each of us had only one garment in which she menstruated. If something of blood got on it, she would moisten it with her saliva and scratch it with her fingernail.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawood) Blood is impure by consensus, and she moistened it with saliva and scratched it, and the blood was removed, so the item became pure. It is clear that saliva is not water, so it is known that an impure thing can be purified by something other than water. (2) If impurity gets on a shoe and it is rubbed on the ground, and the impurity is removed, the shoe becomes pure. This means that the basic rule is that clothing becomes pure by the removal of impurity. Lexicon: مائع: flowing thing. مزیل: removing. الخل: vinegar. ماءالورد: rose water, rose juice.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that impurity on clothes or body is purified by water and by any flowing liquid that removes the impurity, such as vinegar or rose water. The evidence comes from two hadiths: first, the hadith of Asma about menstrual blood, where the Prophet instructed to scratch and rub with water, showing that wringing is necessary for removal. Second, the hadith of Aisha where she used saliva (not water) to remove blood, proving that any liquid that removes impurity works. The principle is that the removal of impurity itself, not the specific substance, causes purification. The commentary also gives an analogy: a shoe becomes pure by rubbing on ground. Thus, the Hanafi position is that any liquid that flows and removes impurity can purify, as long as the impurity is completely removed.

Key Terms
مائع (mā'i'): A flowing liquid, such as water, vinegar, or rose water.
مزيل (muzīl): Something that removes or eliminates the impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basic principle for purification of a visible impurity?
A) The impurity must be washed three times.
B) The impurity must be removed, regardless of the liquid used.
C) Only pure water can be used.
D) The garment must be wrung out.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits purification from najāsah using any flowing liquid that removes the impurity, based on the principle of removal and the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Purification of Leather Socks by Rubbing
Ruling with proof on purifying leather socks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying leather socks (khuff) from impurities with substance and apply the dalil (proof) from hadith to support it.

Core Idea
A leather sock is purified by rubbing if the impurity is solid; washing is only needed for liquid impurities like urine.

In this passage, the Thamaratun Najah text presents a practical ruling on taharah: how to purify leather socks (khuff) when they become soiled. The key distinction is whether the impurity has substance (jirm). This ruling is supported by two hadiths. Understanding this nuance is essential for daily practice and for recognizing the Hanafi method of using specific dalil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm (legal status) of rubbing to purify? The act is purifying the khuff after contact with impurity. The ruling is that rubbing suffices if the impurity has substance.
The hukm here is not the act of rubbing but the outcome: the khuff becomes pure.
2
Locate the condition
What condition must be met for rubbing to work? The impurity must have substance (jirm), meaning it is solid or viscous. If the impurity is liquid (like urine), washing is required.
The condition is on the impurity, not the item.
3
Examine the dalil
What proofs are cited? Two hadiths: (1) Abu Huraira: 'When one of you steps on impurity with his khuffs, then their purification is with earth.' (2) Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When one of you comes to the mosque, let him look; if he sees filth or impurity on his sandals, let him wipe it and pray in them.' These indicate rubbing on earth suffices.
Both hadiths are ahad (single transmission) and zanni in thubut and dalala.
4
Apply the principle
What is the underlying usul? The general principle is that things become pure by removal of the actual impurity. Since solid impurity does not penetrate leather deeply, rubbing removes it effectively, restoring purity.
This is a rukhsah (concession) for leather items.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
How do other schools differ? Many schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require washing for any impurity on leather, arguing that rubbing does not guarantee removal. The Hanafi school relies on the explicit hadith and the nature of leather.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in daily purification methods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۸۱) موزہ اور اس کے مانند رگڑنے سے پاک ہوگا اگر نجاست دلدار ہو چاہے وہ تر ہو۔
تشریح : چمڑے کی جتنی چیزیں ہیں جیسے موزہ وغیرہ اگر اس پر تر اور بھینگی نجاست لگی اور وہ پہنچانے کی طرح دلدار ہو تو اس کو رگڑ کر صاف کر دینے سے موزہ پاک ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر پیشاب کی طرح دلدار نہ ہو تو موزے کو دھونا ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) چمڑے کے اندر دلدار نجاست کم جاتی ہے، اور جو کچھ باہر ہے وہ رگڑنے کی وجہ سے صاف ہو جائے گی اس لئے موزہ پاک ہو جائے گا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبى الله بمعناه قال اذا وطى الاذى بخفيه فطهورهما التراب . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الاذی یصیب النعل ،ص ۶۷ نمبر ۳۸۶)(۳) عن ابی سعیدن الخدرى .... اذا جاء أحـدكـم الـى الـمـسـجـد فلينظر، فان رأي في نعليه قذراً او اذى فليمسحه و ليصل فيهما. (ابوداود شریف، باب الصلوۃ فی النحل، ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۶۵۰ مسند احمد، مسند ابی سعید الخدری تاج ثالث ص ۵۱۹، نمبر ۱۱۴۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مٹی سے رگڑنے کے بعد جو تا یا موزہ پاک ہو جائے گا
اصول: نجاست حقیقیہ کے زائل ہونے سے چیز پاک ہو جائینگی۔
Translation (281): The leather sock (khuff) and similar will be purified by rubbing if the impurity has substance (jirm), even if it is wet. Explanation: All leather items, such as the khuff, if a wet and moist impurity is on it and it has substance like mud, then by rubbing and cleaning it, the khuff becomes pure. But if it does not have substance, like urine, then the khuff must be washed. Proof: (1) The impurity with substance does not penetrate leather much, and whatever is outside is cleaned by rubbing, so the khuff becomes pure. (2) Hadith from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him) with similar meaning: 'When one of you steps on impurity with his khuffs, then their purification is with earth.' (Abu Dawood) (3) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When one of you comes to the mosque, let him look; if he sees filth or impurity on his sandals, let him wipe it and pray in them.' (Abu Dawood, Musnad Ahmad) This hadith indicates that after rubbing with earth, the sandal or khuff becomes pure. Principle: Things become pure by the removal of actual impurity.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. It states that leather socks (khuff) and similar items become pure by rubbing if the impurity has substance (jirm), meaning it is solid or viscous like mud, even if wet. If the impurity is liquid like urine, washing is required. The evidence includes hadiths showing that rubbing on earth purifies sandals and khuffs. The underlying principle is that purification occurs by the removal of the impurity itself. This ruling applies specifically to leather items due to their smooth surface; impurity with substance does not penetrate deeply.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): Leather sock worn over the foot, commonly used in the context of wiping (mash) during wudu and purification.
دلدار (dildar): Having substance (jirm), i.e., solid or viscous matter, as opposed to liquid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is a leather sock (khuff) purified if it gets wet mud on it?
A) It must be washed three times
B) It can be purified by rubbing it against the ground
C) It becomes pure automatically when dry
D) It cannot be purified and must be discarded

Key Takeaway
Leather items are purified by rubbing when the impurity has substance; this is based on hadith and the principle of impurity removal.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Purification of Smooth Objects by Wiping and Earth by Drying
Rulings on purifying smooth objects by wiping and earth by drying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying smooth objects by wiping and earth by drying, and identify the proof for each.

Core Idea
Wiping suffices for smooth surfaces; dried earth is pure for prayer but not for tayammum.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah covers two important rulings related to purification in the Hanafi school. The first concerns smooth objects like swords, which can be purified by merely wiping off impurity. The second concerns earth that has become impure but then dries—it becomes pure for prayer but cannot be used for tayammum. These rulings are based on hadith and analogy, as you'll see in the proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and separate the ruling for smooth objects (282) from the ruling for earth (283). Note the condition for each: for wiping, the object must be smooth and impurity does not penetrate; for earth, the effect must disappear and it must dry.
2
Locate the proof for each ruling
For wiping, the author cites the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about wiping sandals, then uses qiyas to apply it to swords. For earth, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar shows that dogs urinated in the mosque without washing, yet prayers were offered, indicating that drying purifies the ground for prayer.
Both proofs are ahad (individual) narrations.
3
Understand the limitation for tayammum
Although dried earth is pure for prayer, it cannot be used for tayammum. The reason is that tayammum requires 'sa'id tayyib' (pure soil), which means soil that has never been contaminated or has been thoroughly cleaned. The dried earth still contains the impurity in a dry state, so it is not considered pure enough for tayammum.
This is a key distinction often misunderstood.
4
Note the underlying principle
The principle mentioned in the text: 'Things become pure by the removal of actual impurity.' For smooth objects, wiping removes the impurity. For earth, the disappearance of effect and drying remove the impurity's presence, making it pure for prayer though not for tayammum.
This principle applies to many taharah cases.
5
Consider the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require washing for smooth objects and may permit tayammum on dried earth if it was originally pure. The Hanafi position is a concession (rukhsah) based on the evidence presented.
Understanding ikhtilaf helps in comparative fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رطبة. (۲۸۲) ويطهر السيف ونحوه بالمسح . (۲۸۳) واذا ذهب اثر النجاسة عن الارض و جفت یا جوتا پاک ہو جائے گا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبى الله بمعناه قال اذا وطى الاذى بخفيه فطهورهما التراب . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الاذی یصیب النعل ،ص ۶۷ نمبر ۳۸۶)(۳) عن ابی سعیدن الخدرى .... اذا جاء أحـدكـم الـى الـمـسـجـد فلينظر، فان رأي في نعليه قذراً او اذى فليمسحه و ليصل فيهما. (ابوداود شریف، باب الصلوۃ فی النحل، ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۶۵۰ مسند احمد، مسند ابی سعید الخدری تاج ثالث ص ۵۱۹، نمبر ۱۱۴۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مٹی سے رگڑنے کے بعد جو تا یا موزہ پاک ہو جائے گا
اصول: نجاست حقیقیہ کے زائل ہونے سے چیز پاک ہو جائینگی۔
ترجمه : (۲۸۲) اور تلوار اور اس کی مانند پاک ہوگی مل دینے سے۔
تشریح : جو چیزیں تلوار کی طرح چکنی ہوں، اور ان کے اندر نجاست گھستی نہ ہو تو اس کو اچھی طرح پونچھ دیں جس سے نجاست جو تلوارکی اندر نہ ہوتواس چھ دیں جس بالکل صاف ہو جائے تو اس سے وہ پاک ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے لوہے تانبے کا برتن ہلکڑی کا سامان جو چکنا ہو۔
وجه : (۱) اصل ہے نجاست کا زائل ہونا ، یہاں پونچھنے سے نجاست زائل ہوگئی اس لئے پاک ہو جائے گا۔(۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تلوار سے نرم چیز جوتا ہے اس کو رگڑنے سے پاک ہو جاتا ہے، اس لئے اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے تلوار بھی رگڑنے سے پاک ہو جائے گی۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی سعيدن الخدرى .... اذا جاء أحدكم الى المسجد فلينظر ، فان رأى في نعليه قذراً او اذى فليمسحه و ليصل فيهما . (ابو داود شریف ، باب الصلوة فی النحل، ص ۱۰۴، نمبر ۶۵۰ رمسند احمد ، مسند ابی سعید الخدری ، ج ثالث ،ص ۵۱۹، نمبر ۱۱۴۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مٹی سے رگڑنے کے بعد جوتا یا موزہ پاک ہو جائے گا۔
جه : (۲۸۳) اور جب زمین سے نجاست کا اثر زائل ہو کر خشک ہو جائے تو اس پر نماز جائز ہے، تیم جائز نہیں۔ تشریح : دو باتیں ہیں [1] ایک تو یہ ہے کہ زمین سے نجاست کا اثر ختم ہو جائے ، مثلا گو برسوکھ کر مٹی کی طرح ہو جائے اور یہ پتہ ہی نہ چلے کہ یہ بھی گو بر رہا ہے، [۲] اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ وہ نجاست سوکھ چکی ہو تواب یہ نماز پڑھنے کے لئے جائز ہے۔ لیکن تیم کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ تیم کے لئے آیت کے مطابق صعید طیب، یعنی پاک مٹی چاہئے اس لئے اس پر تیم جائز نہیں ہے۔ وجه (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ قال عبد الله ابن عمر كنت ابيت في المسجد في عهد رسول الله ل وكنت فتى شابا عزبا، وكانت الكلاب تبول و تقبل وتدبر في المسجد فلم يكونوا يرشون شيئا من ذلک ۔(ابوداود شریف، باب فی طهور الارض اذا بست ،ص ۶۶ نمبر ۳۸۲) کتا مسجد میں پیشاب کرتا ہو پھر اس کو کوئی دھوتا نہ ہو اور اسی پر نماز پڑھتا
Wet. (282) The sword and similar become pure by wiping. (283) When the effect of impurity disappears from the earth and it dries, or the shoe becomes pure. (2) Hadith from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When one steps on impurity with his khuffs, then their purification is with earth.' (Abu Dawood) (3) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When one of you comes to the mosque, let him look; if he sees filth or impurity on his sandals, let him wipe it and pray in them.' (Abu Dawood, Musnad Ahmad) This hadith indicates that after rubbing with earth, the sandal or khuff becomes pure. Principle: Things become pure by the removal of actual impurity. Translation (282): The sword and similar become pure by wiping. Explanation: Items that are smooth like a sword, and impurity does not penetrate them, can be wiped thoroughly so that the impurity is completely removed, and then they become pure. Examples: iron or copper vessels, wooden items that are smooth. Proof: (1) The principle is removal of impurity; here wiping removes impurity, so it becomes pure. (2) There is a hadith that a soft item like a shoe is purified by rubbing, so by analogy the sword is also purified by rubbing. The hadith is from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'When one of you comes to the mosque, let him look; if he sees filth on his sandals, let him wipe it and pray in them.' This indicates that after rubbing with earth, the shoe or khuff becomes pure. Explanation of (283): When the effect of impurity disappears from the earth and it dries, then prayer on it is permissible, but tayammum with it is not permissible. There are two matters: first, the effect of impurity from the earth disappears, e.g., dung dries and becomes like soil, so that it is not identifiable as dung. Second, that impurity has dried. Then it is permissible to pray there. But it is not permissible for tayammum, because tayammum requires pure earth (sa'id tayyib) according to the verse. Proof: Hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'I used to spend the night in the mosque during the time of the Messenger of Allah, and I was a young unmarried man, and dogs would urinate and come and go in the mosque, and they would not sprinkle anything of that.' (Abu Dawood) Dogs would urinate in the mosque, and no one would wash it, and they would pray in that place.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First (282): smooth objects like swords are purified by wiping if impurity does not penetrate. The proof is analogy with shoes, which are purified by rubbing. Second (283): when the effect of impurity on earth disappears and it dries, prayer is valid on that earth, but tayammum with it is not valid because tayammum requires pure earth. The evidence is the practice in the Prophet's mosque where dogs urinated and no one washed it, yet prayers were offered. This shows that drying suffices for purification of the ground for prayer, but tayammum requires earth free from any najasah.

Key Terms
مسح (mash): Wiping or passing the hand over an object to remove impurity, for smooth surfaces like a sword.
صعید طیب (sa'id tayyib): Pure soil or earth that is free from impurity, required for tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a sword that gets najasah according to the Hanafi school?
A) It must be washed with water.
B) It becomes pure by wiping.
C) It must be rubbed with earth.
D) It becomes pure when dry.

Key Takeaway
Smooth objects are purified by wiping; dried earth is pure for prayer but not for tayammum.

Purification of a Sword by Wiping
Ruling on purifying a sword by wiping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a sword is purified by wiping and explain the proof from hadith and qiyas (analogy to shoes).

Core Idea
A sword is purified by wiping because impurity sits on the surface and removal suffices.

The Hanafi school teaches that certain impurities can be removed from non-absorbent surfaces by simply wiping them. This ruling is based on a hadith about shoes, extended by analogy to smooth objects like swords. While other schools require washing, the Hanafi position relies on the principle that actual impurity is removed by wiping.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is purifying a sword that has become impure. The ruling: it becomes pure by wiping (masḥ).
The ruling is stated concisely: 'ويطهر السيف ونحوه بالمسح'
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The author cites a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: if one sees impurity on his shoes, he should wipe it and then pray in them.
Hadith reference: Musnad Ahmad and Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The command to wipe and then pray indicates that wiping suffices for purification, because prayer is only valid with purity.
The operative phrase is 'فليمسحه وليصل فيهما' – wipe and pray in them.
4
Trace the qiyas
The text draws an analogy: shoes are softer than a sword, yet they become pure by rubbing. So by stronger reason (qiyas awla), a sword becomes pure by wiping.
This is a qiyas based on the common illa: non-absorbent surface that can be cleaned by wiping.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools like Shafi'i require washing for all impurities, even on non-absorbent surfaces. The Hanafi school permits wiping based on the hadith and the principle of removal of actual impurity.
The principle: 'النجاسة الحقيقية تزول بالمسح'

Chapter of Impurities and Purification. (282) And the sword and the like become pure by wiping. There is a hadith from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him) with its meaning: 'When one steps on impurity with his shoes, their purification is the earth.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on impurity striking the sandal, p. 67 no. 386) (3) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... (Abu Dawud, chapter on prayer in shoes, p. 104 no. 650; Musnad Ahmad) From this hadith it is learned that after rubbing with earth, the shoe or sock becomes pure. Principle: By the removal of actual impurity, a thing becomes pure. Translation of (282): And the sword and its like become pure by wiping. Commentary: Things that are smooth like a sword, and impurities do not penetrate them, one should wipe them well so that if the impurity does not go inside the sword, one wipes it until it becomes completely clean, then it becomes pure. Like iron or copper vessels, wooden items that are smooth. Proof: (1) The principle is removal of impurity; here wiping removed impurity, so it becomes pure. (2) In this hadith, the softer thing than a sword, which is a shoe, becomes pure by rubbing, so by analogy the sword also becomes pure by rubbing. The hadith is: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... 'When one of you comes to the mosque, let him look; if he sees dirt or impurity on his shoes, let him wipe it and pray in them.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on prayer in shoes, p. 104 no. 650; Musnad Ahmad) From this hadith it is learned that after rubbing with earth, the shoe or sock becomes pure.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the purification of a sword and similar smooth objects by wiping. The author begins by stating the ruling: the sword becomes pure by wiping. Then he cites a hadith from Abu Huraira about stepping on impurity with shoes, but the main proof is the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet instructs to wipe impurity from shoes and then pray in them. The principle is that removal of actual impurity makes the object pure. In the commentary, the author explains that items like iron or copper vessels that are non-absorbent can be purified by wiping because the impurity sits on the surface. The proof uses analogy: since a shoe is softer than a sword but becomes pure by rubbing, by stronger reason a sword should become pure by wiping.

Key Terms
المسح (al-masḥ): Wiping or rubbing a surface to remove impurity
السيف (al-sayf): Sword; used as an example of a smooth metal object that does not absorb impurity
نجاسة حقيقية (najāsah ḥaqīqiyyah): Actual impurity, as opposed to hukmiyyah (abstract impurity like hadath)

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Analogy (qiyas) to shoes based on a hadith
C) Consensus of all scholars
D) The principle that water is always required

Key Takeaway
Non-absorbent surfaces like swords are purified by wiping because the actual impurity is removed; this is proven by hadith and qiyas.

Purification of Ground by Drying: Prayer Permissible, Tayammum Not
Ruling with proof on ground purification by drying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ground purification by drying and distinguish between its validity for prayer versus tayammum.

Core Idea
Drying purifies ground for prayer but not tayammum – residual impurity prevents it from being pure earth.

This passage presents a distinctive Hanafi ruling: when impurity on the ground dries and its trace disappears, the ground becomes pure for prayer. However, the same ground is invalid for tayammum because tayammum requires 'pure earth' (ṣa‘īd ṭayyib) which must be inherently pure. We will examine the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and the critical distinction between prayer and tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of the ruling
Note that the author states: prayer is permissible on the dry ground, but tayammum is not. This is a single rule with two consequences.
One ruling, two applications.
2
Understand the condition for purification
The impurity must have completely dried and its trace (colour, smell, taste) must have disappeared. Both are required.
Merely drying is insufficient if trace remains.
3
Locate the primary proof (dalīl)
The hadith of Ibn ‘Umar: dogs urinated in the mosque, the Companions did not wash it, and prayer was performed. This shows that drying itself suffices for purification of the ground.
This is a Sunnah aḥad, hence the ruling is not qaṭ‘ī.
4
Explain why tayammum is not allowed
Tayammum requires ṣa‘īd ṭayyib – pure earth. The ground that once contained impurity, even if dried, is not considered pure in the absolute sense required for tayammum. The impurity physically remains even if dry.
The distinction hinges on the definition of 'pure earth'.
5
Contrast with the case of wet impurity
If the impurity is still wet, washing with water is required, as seen in the hadith of the Bedouin urinating in the mosque.
Wet impurity must be removed; drying alone does not purify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لغت : جفت : خشک ہو گئی۔
(283) And when the trace of impurity disappears from the ground and it dries, prayer is permissible on it but not tayammum from it. Comment: (283) And when the trace of impurity from the ground is removed and it dries, prayer is permissible on it, tayammum is not permissible. Explanation: Two matters: [1] The trace of impurity from the ground is eliminated, e.g., dung dries and becomes like soil, and it is not known that it was dung; [2] And the second matter is that the impurity has dried, then prayer on it is permissible. But tayammum is not permissible, because for tayammum, according to the verse, pure earth (sa'id tayyib) is required, so tayammum on it is not permissible. Proof (1) There is a hadith: Abdullah ibn Umar said: I used to stay in the mosque during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and I was a young unmarried man, and dogs would urinate and come and go in the mosque, and they would not sprinkle anything on that... (Abu Dawud, chapter on purification of the ground when it dries, p. 66 no. 382) The dog would urinate in the mosque, then no one would wash it, and prayer was performed on it, and prayer was permissible on it without tayammum from it. (284) And it purifies the trees and grass that stand on it by their drying. ... This is proof that after the urine dried and its traces went, the place became pure. (2) In the saying of Abu Qilabah, it is clear that when the ground dries, it becomes pure. (3) I saw al-Hasan sitting on the trace of dry urine, and I said to him, and he said: It is dry. This effect shows that when urine dried on the ground, the ground became pure. (4) But if the impurity is wet or its trace has not gone, then despite it being on soil, it is purified by washing. There is a hadith: Abu Huraira said: A Bedouin stood up and urinated in the mosque, and the people came to him, but the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to them: 'Leave him, and pour a bucket or a bucketful of water on his urine, for you have been sent to make things easy, not to make things difficult.' (Bukhari, chapter on pouring water on urine in the mosque, p. 21 no. 220; Abu Dawud, chapter on the ground affected by urine, p. 66 no. 380). This hadith indicates that when the impurity is wet, water must be poured. Vocabulary: jaffat = became dry.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the purification of ground by drying. The author states that if the trace of impurity disappears from the earth and it dries, prayer on it is valid, but tayammum is not allowed. The commentary explains that the impurity must be completely dry and its effects gone. The proofs include the practice of the Companions in the mosque where dogs urinated and no washing was done, and the statement of Abu Qilabah and the action of Hasan al-Basri. However, if the impurity is still wet, it must be washed with water, as shown in the hadith of the Bedouin urinating in the mosque. The key distinction is between dry and wet impurity: dry impurity on the ground becomes pure by itself, but wet impurity requires washing.

Key Terms
جفت (jaffat): Became dry (referring to impurity or ground)
صعید طیب (ṣa‘īd ṭayyib): Pure earth used for tayammum
تیمم (tayammum): Ritual purification with earth

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Drying of impurity on the ground purifies it for prayer but not for tayammum; this distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

Purification of Trees and Grass by Drying
Ruling on purification of standing trees and grass by drying of impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification of standing vegetation by drying and apply the qiyas to similar attached objects.

Core Idea
Vegetation attached to the ground becomes pure by drying, just like the ground.

This brief ruling expands the previous rule about ground purification to trees and grass that are rooted in the earth. The Hanafi school holds that if impurity falls on standing vegetation, it becomes pure once the impurity dries and its visible effects disappear. The reasoning is qiyas (analogy): since the ground itself is purified by drying, anything that stands on it and shares its nature (being fixed and hard to wash) receives the same ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is impurity falling on standing trees or grass. The ruling is that they become pure by drying.
Ensure you distinguish this from ground purification.
2
Understand the condition
The condition for purification is that the impurity dries completely and its physical effects (color, smell, taste) vanish.
Drying alone is not enough if traces remain.
3
Recognize the qiyas
The ground is the original case (asl); vegetation is the branch (far). The common cause (illa) is being fixed and difficult to wash.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on istihsan.
4
Consider the scope
This ruling applies only to standing, rooted vegetation. Cut or detached plants are treated differently.
Detached plants must be washed like other surfaces.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools such as the Shafi'i require washing of vegetation. The Hanafi position is based on ease and analogy.
Ikhtilaf is legitimate; both views have proofs.

Source Text

Commentary: The same ruling that applies to the ground also applies to the trees and grass standing on it. That is, if impurity touches the standing tree or grass, then by that impurity drying and its effects disappearing, the tree and grass become pure.

Commentary
This is a short ruling extending the previous rule about ground purification to trees and grass that are attached to the ground. The author states that if impurity falls on standing vegetation, it becomes pure when the impurity dries and its effects vanish, exactly like the ground. The proof is analogy: since the ground becomes pure by drying, so does anything that stands on it and cannot be washed easily. This is a qiyas (analogy) based on the same principle of removal of impurity by drying.

Key Terms

Purification by Change of Substance (Istihalah)
Ruling on purification of impurity by change of substance (istihalah)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istihalah (transformation of substance) and apply it to examples such as impurity turning into salt, ash, or vinegar.

Core Idea
If an impurity's essence completely transforms (istihala), it becomes pure.

We often assume that impurity is permanent, but Islamic law recognizes that when a substance changes entirely, its ruling changes too. This lesson explores the Hanafi position on purification by transformation (istihalah), using the classical example of wine turning into vinegar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first sentence: 'And an impurity becomes pure if its substance changes.' The ruling is that complete transformation (istihalah) purifies the impurity.
The transformation must be complete, not partial.
2
Understand the scope
The text gives examples: becoming salt (e.g., falling into a salt mine) or burning to ash. Modern chemical changes (e.g., adding acid) are also included if the nature fully changes.
The key is that the original impurity is no longer present in its essential form.
3
Examine the proof
The author uses the analogy of wine: grapes are pure, wine is impure, but when wine turns to vinegar it becomes pure again. This is supported by the statement of Aisha (RA) that wine vinegar is permissible as a condiment.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (statement of a Companion), which is zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not accept general istihalah for all impurities, but they accept it for wine turning to vinegar due to explicit hadith.
The Hanafi position relies on qiyas (analogy) from that specific case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۸۵ الف) وتطهر نجاسة استحالت عينها كان صارت ملحا او احترقت
ترجمه : (۲۸۵ (الف) اور نجاست پاک ہو جائے گی اگر اس کا عین بدل گیا، مثلا نمک بن گئی یا آگ سے جل گئی۔
تشریح : نجاست کی ماہیت بدل جائے ،مثلا گدھا کان میں گرنمک بن گیا تو وہ پاک ہو جائے گا، یا نجاست راکھ میں راکھ ہو جائے، یا آج کل تیزاب ، اور کیمیکل ڈال کر چیزوں کی خاصیت بدل دیتے ہیں تو اس سے نجاست پاک ہو جائے گی۔

(مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۲۳ فی الخمر مخلل ، ج خامس ،ص ۹۸، نمبر ۲۴۰۸۳ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الخمر يجعل خلا، ج تاسع ، ص ۱۶۱، نمبر (۱۷۴۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنا دیا جائے تو اس کا کھانا حلال ہے۔ (۲) قال شهدت عمر
(285a) And an impurity becomes pure if its substance changes, such as it becomes salt or burns. Translation: (285a) And impurity becomes pure if its essence changes, for example it becomes salt or burned. Commentary: The nature of impurity changes, for example, if it falls in a salt mine and becomes salt, then it becomes pure; or impurity turns to ash; or nowadays by adding acid and chemicals, the properties change, then by that the impurity becomes pure. Proof: (1) Grapes are halal and pure, but when their substance changes into wine, they become haram and impure. Similarly, when wine's substance changes into vinegar, it becomes halal and pure. On this principle, if the substance of impurity changes and no filth remains or the property of impurity is gone, then it becomes pure. (2) In the saying of a female Companion: I asked Aisha about wine vinegar; she said: 'There is no harm in it; it is a condiment.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on wine turned into vinegar, vol. 5, p. 98 no. 24083; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on wine made into vinegar, vol. 9, p. 161 no. 1742) From this effect it is known that if wine is turned into vinegar, eating it is halal. (2) And he said: I saw Umar... (cut off).
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This ruling states that an impurity becomes pure if its very substance transforms into something else, such as turning into salt or being burned to ash. The commentary gives examples: if impurity falls into a salt mine and becomes salt, or is burned to ash, or if chemicals change its properties, it becomes pure. The proof is the analogy with wine: grapes are pure, wine is impure, but when wine turns into vinegar, it becomes pure again. This shows that the change of substance (istihalah) alters the ruling. The author also cites the statement of Aisha that wine vinegar is permissible as a condiment. The proof is that the original impurity is no longer present in its essential form.

Key Terms
استحالت عينها (istaḥālat ‘aynihā): Its substance changed, complete transformation of the essence
خمر (khamr): Wine, intoxicant
خل (khall): Vinegar

Key Takeaway
Complete transformation of the substance (istihalah) purifies an impure object, as exemplified by wine turning into vinegar.

Purification of Ground and Plants by Drying of Najasah
Ruling with proof (dalil naqli) and expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification of ground and standing plants by drying, identify the supporting evidence, and distinguish when washing is required instead.

Core Idea
Drying purifies the ground and fixed plants, but not movable objects.

This lesson addresses a practical question: if urine or other liquid impurity falls on the ground or on a tree, does the ground become pure once it dries? The Hanafi school answers yes, based on statements of the Companions and the practice of early Muslims. However, the same rule does not apply to clothing or furniture. We will examine the evidence and the boundary conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject of the Ruling
Read the matn: 'And trees and grass standing on it become pure by their drying.' The ruling applies specifically to the ground and to plants that are rooted (standing), not cut or detached.
The Arabic phrase 'كلأ قائم' (standing herbage) emphasizes that the plant is still attached to the earth.
2
State the Ruling
When a liquid impurity (e.g., urine) falls on the ground or on a standing plant, and that impurity dries completely so that no moisture or trace remains, the place becomes pure (tahir). No washing is required.
This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the Proofs
The author cites two athar and one hadith: (1) Abu Qilabah said, 'When the ground dries, it has been purified.' (2) Al-Hasan al-Basri sat on a dry urine spot, indicating its purity. (3) The hadith of the bedouin shows that wet impurity requires pouring water, implying that dry impurity does not.
These proofs are from the Salaf and from the Prophet's action (taqriri).
4
Understand the Condition and Exception
The ruling only applies when the impurity is completely dry and its effect (color, smell, taste) is gone. If the impurity is still wet or its trace remains, the ground is not pure; it must be washed with water, as in the hadith of the bedouin.
The exception clarifies that drying is not a general purifier for all surfaces.
5
Recognize the Ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'is) hold that drying never purifies; washing is always required. The Hanafi position is based on ease and the specific nature of earth and plants.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۷۲ من قال اذا کانت جافة فھو ز کا تہا، ج اول ص ۵۹ نمبر ۶۲۵) (۳) رأيت الحسن جالسا على اثر بول جاف فقلت له فقال انه جاف (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۷۲ من قال اذا کانت جافة فهوز کا تہا ، ج اول ص ۵۹، نمبر ۶۲۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ زمین پر پیشاب سوکھ گیا تو زمین پاک ہوگئی ۔ (۴) لیکن اگر نجاست تر ہے یا اس کا اثر نہیں گیا تو مٹی پر رہنے کے باوجود دھونے سے پاک ہوگی ، اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابا هريرة قال قام اعرابي قبال في المسجد فتناوله الناس فقال لهم النبي علي دعوه وهر يقوا على بوله سجلا من ماء او ذنوبا من ماء فانما بعثتم ميسرين لم تبعثوا معسرين ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب صب الماء علی البول فی المسجد ، ص ۲۱، نمبر ۲۲۰ را بود او د شریف، باب الارض یصیبھا البول، ص ۶۶ نمبر ۳۸۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ترنجاست ہو تو پانی بہانا ہوگا۔ صلى الله لغت: جفت: خشک ہو گئی۔ ترجمه: (۲۸۴) اور زمین پر جو درخت اور گھانس کھڑا ہے اس پر نجاست خشک ہونے سے پاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ تشریح: جو حکم زمین کا ہے وہی حکم اس پر کھڑا درخت اور گھاس کا بھی ہے، یعنی اگر کھڑے درخت پر اور گھاس پر نجاست لگ جائے تو اس نجاست کے سوکھ جانے اور اس کے اثرات کے چلے جانے سے درخت اور گھاس پاک ہو جائیں گے۔
And what is upon it of trees and grass standing become pure by their drying. This is evidence that after urine dries and its traces disappear, the place becomes pure. Abu Qilabah said: 'When the ground dries, it has become purified.' I saw al-Hasan sitting on the trace of dry urine and asked him, and he said: 'It is dry.' This narration indicates that when urine on the ground dries, the ground becomes pure. But if the impurity is wet or its effect remains, then despite being on soil, it only becomes pure by washing, as in the hadith: 'A bedouin urinated in the mosque, and the people grabbed him, but the Prophet said: Leave him, and pour a bucket of water on his urine; you have been sent to make things easy, not difficult.' This hadith shows that wet impurity requires pouring water. Lexicon: 'jaffa': became dry. Translation: (284) And trees and grass standing on it become pure by the drying of the impurity. Explanation: The same ruling applies to trees and grass as to the ground: if najasah falls on standing trees or grass, when it dries and its effects disappear, the trees and grass become pure.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn followed by its proofs and explanation. The ruling states that trees and grass that are rooted in the ground become pure when the najasah on them dries, just as the ground itself becomes pure by drying. The author first provides evidence from the sayings of the Companions (athar) and then clarifies the exception: if the impurity is still wet or its trace remains, washing is required. The proofs include: (1) the statement of Abu Qilabah that dry ground is pure, (2) the action of Imam al-Hasan al-Basri who sat on dry urine, (3) the hadith of the bedouin where the Prophet ordered water to be poured on wet urine, showing that wet impurity requires water. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling for plants is analogized to the ground, as both are fixed in place and the impurity on them dries similarly.

Key Terms
جفّ (jaffa): To become dry; in this context, the drying of the liquid impurity until no moisture remains.
كلأ (kala'): Herbage, grass growing from the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The tree becomes pure once the urine dries and its effect is gone.
C) The tree is permanently impure.
D) Only the ground can be purified by drying, not trees.

Key Takeaway
Ground and standing plants become pure when najasah dries; washing is only needed if the impurity is wet or its trace remains.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Purification by Istihalah: Transformation of Essence
States ruling on purification by istihalah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purification by istihalah and apply it to scenarios of substance transformation, citing the supporting proofs.

Core Idea
When the essence of an impure substance completely transforms, it becomes pure.

The Hanafi school permits purification through istihalah—a complete transformation of the substance's essence. This lesson examines the ruling, its conditions, and the proofs from the practice of the Companions. Understanding this principle helps distinguish genuine purification from mere dilution or mixing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that an impure substance becomes pure when its essence changes, e.g., dung becoming salt or burning to ash. Recognize that the ruling is a state of purity (tahara) after transformation.
2
Define istihalah
Istihalah is the transformation of the 'ayn (essence) so that the original properties no longer exist. It is not mere mixing or dilution.
The Arabic term استحالة implies a fundamental chemical change.
3
Locate the dalil
The passage cites Aisha's statement about wine vinegar and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz's directive. Identify these as qawl sahabi and practice of a caliph.
These are considered authoritative proofs in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
Aisha said, 'There is no harm; it is a condiment,' indicating that vinegar from wine is permissible and pure. This shows that transformation changes the ruling.
The specific phrase 'لا بأس به' implies permissibility.
5
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i (in one view) does not accept transformation as purifying; the substance retains its original impurity. Recognize this difference and its practical consequences.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۸۵ [الف) وتطهر نجاسة استحالت عينها كان صارت ملحا او احترقت بالنار. ترجمه: (۲۸۵ (الف) اور نجاست پاک ہو جائے گی اگر اس کا عین بدل گیا، مثلا نمک بن گئی یا آگ سے جل گئی۔ تشریح: نجاست کی ماہیت بدل جائے ،مثلا گدھا کان میں گرنمک بن گیا تو وہ پاک ہو جائے گا، یا نجاست راکھ میں راکھ ہو جائے، یا آج کل تیزاب ، اور کیمیکل ڈال کر چیزوں کی خاصیت بدل دیتے ہیں تو اس سے نجاست پاک ہو جائے گی۔ وجه: (۱) انگور حلال اور پاک ہے لیکن اس کا عین بدل کر شراب بن گئی تو حرام اور ناپاک ہوگئی ، اسی طرح شراب کا عین بدل کر سرکہ بن جائے تو حلال اور پاک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسی قاعدے پر نجاست کا عین بدل جائے اور اس میں گندگی نہ رہے یا نجاست کی خاصیت نہ رہے تو وہ پاک ہو جائے گی ۔ (۲) اس قول صحابیہ میں ہے۔ سألت عائشة عــن خـل الخمر قالت لا بأس به هــــو ادام. (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۲۳ فی الخمر مخلل ، ج خامس ،ص ۹۸، نمبر ۲۴۰۸۳ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الخمر يجعل خلا، ج تاسع ، ص ۱۶۱، نمبر (۱۷۴۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنا دیا جائے تو اس کا کھانا حلال ہے۔ (۲) قال شهدت عمر بن عبد العزيز كتب الى عامله بواسط ان لاتحملوا الخمر من قرية الى قرية وما ادركت فاجعله خلا . ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۴ فی الخمر تحول خلا ، ج خامس ، ص ۱۹، نمبر ۲۴۰۹۰ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الخمر يجعل خلا ، ج تاسع ،ص ۱۶۱، نمبر ۱۷۴۲۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ شراب کو سرکہ بنا دیا جائے تو وہ حلال اور پاک ہو جائے گا۔ اصول: ماہیت بدل جائے تو حکم بدل جاتا ہے۔ اس حدیث میں اس اصول کا ثبوت ہے۔عن ابی ھریرۃ قال قال رسول الله الله الله الخمر من هاتين الشجرتين : الكرمة و النخلة - (مسلم شریف ، باب بیان ان جمیع ما سنمر مما سخر من انخل و العنب یسمی خمر ا ص ۸۸۷ نمبر ۵۱۴۴/۱۹۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ انگور اور کھجورکی ماہیت بدل جائے تو شراب بن جاتی ہے۔
And najasah becomes pure when its essence has changed, as if it became salt or was burnt by fire. Translation: (285a) And najasah will become pure if its essence changes, for example, it becomes salt or is burned by fire. Explanation: The nature of the impurity changes, e.g., dung falls into a salt mine and becomes salt, then it is pure, or impurity becomes ash, or nowadays acids and chemicals change the properties of things, so the impurity becomes pure. Reason: (1) Grapes are lawful and pure, but when their essence changes to wine, they become unlawful and impure; similarly, when wine's essence changes to vinegar, it becomes lawful and pure. By this rule, if the essence of najasah changes and no filth remains or its quality as impurity is lost, then it becomes pure. (2) There is a saying of a female Companion: I asked Aisha about vinegar from wine, and she said: 'There is no harm; it is a condiment.' This shows that if wine is turned into vinegar, eating it is lawful. (2) I saw Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz write to his agent in Wasit: 'Do not transport wine from one village to another; if you have any, turn it into vinegar.' This shows that when wine is made into vinegar, it becomes lawful and pure. Principle: When the essence changes, the ruling changes. This hadith proves this principle: The Prophet said: 'Wine comes from these two trees: the grapevine and the date palm.' This shows that when the essence of grapes and dates changes, it becomes wine.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that an impure substance becomes pure if its essence (chemical or material nature) changes completely. The commentary gives examples: dung becoming salt in a salt mine, impurity burning to ash, or modern chemical changes. The proof is by analogy with wine turning into vinegar: wine is impure and haram, but when it becomes vinegar, it becomes pure and halal. This is supported by the statement of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) and the practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. The underlying principle is that rulings follow the essence; when the essence changes, the ruling changes. The hadith from Muslim is cited to show that wine is defined by its source, and when that source transforms, the ruling follows the new essence.

Key Terms
استحالة (istihalah): The transformation of the essence of a substance, such as when impurity changes into salt or ash, or wine changes into vinegar.
عين ('ayn): The concrete substance or material itself, as opposed to its attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because vinegar is always pure regardless of its origin.
B) Because the essence of wine changes to vinegar, and the ruling follows the new essence.
C) Because the vinegar is washed repeatedly.
D) Because it is no longer intoxicating.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi madhhab, when an impure substance undergoes a complete transformation of its essence, it becomes pure.

Purification of Mani: Rubbing When Dry, Washing When Wet
Ruling on purifying cloth and body from mani: dry by rubbing, wet by washing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying mani from cloth and body, identify the evidence from hadith, and contrast the ruling with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Dry mani is purified by rubbing; wet mani must be washed – a light impurity with easy purification.

In Hanafi fiqh, mani (semen) is considered impure (najis) but is classified as a light impurity with a simplified purification method. This lesson explains that the method depends on whether the mani is dry or wet, based on direct evidence from the practice of the Prophet's household. We will examine the hadith proofs and understand why the Hanafi school differs from others on this point.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Recite the core ruling: dry mani on cloth or body becomes pure by rubbing (fark), and wet mani becomes pure by washing (ghusl) with water.
The ruling is specific to mani; other najasat require washing regardless of state.
2
Examine the Evidence for Wet Mani
Look at the hadith of Aisha (r) where she washed mani from the Prophet's garment, and the hadith listing mani among five impurities requiring washing.
These hadith are cited to prove that wet mani necessitates washing.
3
Examine the Evidence for Dry Mani
Analyze the hadith where Aisha (r) states she rubbed dry mani from the Prophet's garment, and the Prophet prayed in it without re-washing.
This establishes that rubbing alone suffices for dry mani, as wet rubbing would not be effective.
4
Understand Intra-Hanafi and Inter-Madhhab Differences
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf considered mani pure, but the majority Hanafi view (mufta bihi) is impurity. Also, Imam al-Shafi'i holds mani is pure (tahir) and requires no action.
These differences are valid ikhtilaf; the student should understand the basis of each view.
5
Apply the Ruling in Practice
Consider a scenario: a person finds dry mani on his garment. He rubs it off and prays. According to Hanafi fiqh, the prayer is valid. If wet, he must wash it before prayer.
The ease of purification reflects the school's recognition of the difficulty of avoiding mani entirely.

(۲۸۵ [ب]) ويطهر المنى الجاف بفركه عن الثوب والبدن ويطهر الرطب بغسله. ترجمه (۲۸۵[ ب] ) کپڑے اور بدن سے خشک منی کھرچ ڈالنے سے پاک ہو جاتا ہے، اور ترمنی دھونے سے پاک ہوتی ہے تشریح : کپڑا یا بدن پر منی لگ جائے اور سوکھ جائے تو اس کو کھرچ دینے سے کپڑا اور بدن پاک ہو جائے گا وجه : (۱) ترمنی کو دھونے سے پاک ہوگی اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ سالت عائشة عـن الـمنـى يصيب الثوب؟ فقالت كنت اغسله من ثوب رسول الله الله فيخرج الى الصلوة و اثر الغسل في ثوبه بقع الماء (بخاری شریف ، باب غسل المنی و فر که، ص ۴۲ نمبر ۱۲۳۰ مسلم شریف ، باب حکم المنی ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۶۷۲/۲۸۹) (۲) دوسری حدیث ہے۔ یا عمارانـمـايـغسل الثوب من خمس، من الغائط والبول والقيء والدم والمنی (دار قطنی ، باب نجاسة البول والامر بالتنزه مند، ج اول ،ص۱۳۴، نمبر ۴۵۲ ) ان احادیث میں ہے کہ کپڑا دھونے سے پاک ہوگا۔ اور منی خشک ہو تو رگڑنے سے بھی پاک ہوگی اس کی دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة.... لقد رأيتني افركه من ثوب رسول الله فركا فيصلى فيه. (مسلم شریف، باب حکم المنی ، ص ۱۱۳۴ نمبر ۸ ۶۶۸/۲۸ ر ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی المنی یصیب الثوب ص ۳۱ نمبر ۱۱۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خشک منی ہو تو اچھی طرح رگڑنے سے بھی کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ ترمنی رگڑی نہیں جاسکتی (۲) اس حدیث میں خشک کو رگڑنے کی وضاحت ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كنت افرك المنى من ثوب رسول الله عل الله اذا كان يابسا واغسله اذا كان رطبا (دار قطنی ، باب ماورد فی طہارة المنی وحکمہ رطبا و یا بسا ، ج اول ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۱۴۴۳ مسلم شریف ، باب حکم المنی، ص ۱۱۳۴، نمبر ۶۷۴/۲۹۰)
And dry mani becomes pure by rubbing it from the garment and body, and wet mani becomes pure by washing it. Translation: Dry mani from cloth and body becomes pure by scraping, and wet mani becomes pure by washing. Explanation: If mani gets on cloth or body and dries, then scraping it off purifies the cloth and body. Reason: (1) For wet mani being purified by washing, there is this hadith: I asked Aisha about mani on a garment, and she said: 'I used to wash it from the garment of the Messenger of Allah, and he would go out to prayer, and the trace of washing on his garment was water marks.' (2) Another hadith: 'O Ammar, the garment is washed from five things: from excrement, urine, vomit, blood, and mani.' These hadiths show that the garment becomes pure by washing. And for dry mani being pure by rubbing, the evidence is this hadith: From Aisha: 'I saw myself rubbing mani from the garment of the Messenger of Allah with a rubbing, and he would pray in it.' This hadith shows that when mani is dry, the garment becomes pure by thorough rubbing, because wet mani cannot be rubbed. Another hadith clarifies rubbing dry mani: Aisha said: 'I used to rub mani from the garment of the Messenger of Allah when it was dry, and I would wash it when it was wet.'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that mani (semen) is purified differently depending on its state. When dry, it is sufficient to rub it off the cloth or body without water. When wet, it must be washed with water. The author provides several hadiths as proof. The first hadith from Aisha (used by those who consider mani impure) shows that she washed wet mani from the Prophet's garment. The second hadith lists mani among five things that require washing. For dry mani, the hadith of Aisha explicitly states that she rubbed dry mani from the Prophet's garment, and he prayed in it. This indicates that rubbing dry mani removes its impurity. The commentary also notes that wet mani cannot be rubbed effectively, so washing is necessary. The Hanafi school holds that mani is physically impure (najis), but its purification is easy.

Key Terms
منى (maniyy): Semen, the fluid emitted at the time of sexual climax.
فرك (fark): Rubbing or scraping off the dry impurity from a surface.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the method to purify a garment soiled with dry mani?
A) The garment must be washed with water.
B) Rubbing or scraping off the dry mani is sufficient.
C) The garment must be soaked in water for a day.
D) No action is needed because mani is pure.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, dry mani is purified by rubbing, wet mani by washing – a light impurity with easy purification, supported by explicit hadith.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Purification of Dead Animal Hide by Tanning
Ruling on purification of dead animal hide through tanning, with methods and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of tanning (real and ruling) accepted by the Hanafi school and explain why any method that prevents decay qualifies as tanning.

Core Idea
Tanning purifies the hide; any substance that prevents decay is sufficient – Hanafi flexibility in method.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that the hide of a dead animal is purified by tanning. The author distinguishes between real tanning (using astringents like qaraz) and ruling tanning (drying with earth or sun). The proofs include clear hadith and the principle that anything preventing decay counts as tanning, as adopted by Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The hide of a dead animal. What is the hukm? After tanning, it becomes pure (tahir).
The hide is initially najis due to the animal's death without proper slaughter.
2
Distinguish the two types of tanning
The author divides tanning into haqiqiyyah (real, using astringent plants like qaraz) and hukmiyyah (ruling, using earth or sun to dry).
Real tanning is the primary method; ruling tanning is a substitute accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
Two hadith are cited: from Ibn Abbas ('When the hide is tanned, it has become purified') and from Aisha (permission to use tanned hides, including with earth/ashes/salt).
These provide the explicit textual basis for purification by tanning
4
Understand the Hanafi principle from the athar
Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said: 'Anything that prevents decay is tanning.' Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifah adopt this view, making the definition broad.
This is the key Hanafi position: method is not restricted to specific substances.
5
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school requires specific astringent substances; the Hanafi school is more inclusive, accepting any method that removes moisture and prevents decay.
This difference has practical implications for everyday use of hides.
